# Amp models {#firstHeading .firstHeading lang="en"}

:::::::::::::: {#bodyContent .mw-body-content}
::: {#siteSub .noprint}
From Fractal Audio Wiki
:::

::: {#contentSub}
:::

::: {#jump-to-nav}
:::

[Jump to navigation](#mw-head){.mw-jump-link} [Jump to
search](#p-search){.mw-jump-link}

:::::: {#mw-content-text .mw-content-ltr lang="en" dir="ltr"}
::::: mw-parser-output

Amp models
:   This page lists every amplifier model in Fractal Audio's current
    generation of guitar processors and plugins, adding essential
    details such as the name of the modeled amplifier, the appropriate
    speaker cabinet, the amp controls, the type of power tubes, and
    comments from Fractal Audio.

Differences
:   The list below can be slightly different from what you see on your
    device. Possible reasons:
    - You\'re using older firmware, or the firmware on your device
      isn\'t synced yet with the latest Axe-Fx firmware.
    - You\'re using the AM4 that has a slightly shorter list because (1)
      some models have been consolidated into a single model, and (2)
      some legacy models have been deprecated (Brit Pre, old Vibrato
      Verb, one of the Legend models, one of the Chieftain models, Dizzy
      V4 Blue, Thordendal).
    - You\'re using ICONS where some models have a different name (i.e,
      Supertweed is FAS Supertweed in ICONS:Fullerton).

<!-- -->

DynaCabs
:   For each amp model, the matching DynaCab is mentioned, based on the
    AM4 with "automatic Amp+Cab linking" enabled.

<!-- -->

Factory presets
:   Many models are showcased through the factory presets on your
    device. Make sure you have the latest ones installed.

<!-- -->

Guide to the Fractal Audio Amp models
:   In "[Yek\'s Guide to the Fractal Audio Amp models
    (PDF)](https://www.dropbox.com/s/8fvjvrqnryihp86/Yeks_Guide_to_the_Fractal_Audio_Amp_Models.pdf){.external
    .text target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}", forum
    member Yek (Alexander van Engelen) discusses all amp models in the
    Axe-Fx II at the time of writing (2017). Most of the information is
    still valid. The guide was preceded by a [series of
    threads](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/search/1550534/?q=%22Fractal+Audio+AMP+models%22&o=date&c%5Btitle_only%5D=1&c%5Bnode%5D=61&c%5Buser%5D%5B0%5D=10160){.external
    .text target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"} on Fractal
    Audio\'s User Forum.
:   [![YeksGuide.png](/wiki/images/thumb/e/ea/YeksGuide.png/150px-YeksGuide.png){decoding="async"
    width="150" height="214"
    srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/e/ea/YeksGuide.png/225px-YeksGuide.png 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/e/ea/YeksGuide.png/300px-YeksGuide.png 2x"}](https://www.dropbox.com/s/8fvjvrqnryihp86/Yeks_Guide_to_the_Fractal_Audio_Amp_Models.pdf){target="_blank"
    rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

    rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

<!-- -->

Find a model
:   **FENDER** - 5F1 Tweed (EC), 5F8 Tweed, 6G4 Super, 6G12 Concert, 59
    Bassguy, 65 Bassguy, Band-Commander, Deluxe 6G3, Deluxe Tweed,
    Deluxe Verb, Double Verb, Dweezil\'s Bassguy, Jr Blues, Princetone,
    Super Verb, Tremolo Lux, Vibra-king, Vibrato Lux, Vibrato Verb

**MARSHALL** - 1959SLP, 1987X, Brit 800, Brit AFS100, Brit JM45, Brit
JVM, Brit Pre, Brit Silver, JMPRE-1, JS410, Plexi

**MESA** - Recto, Texas Star, Triple Crest, USA Bass 400, USA JP IIC+,
USA Metro Blues, USA MK IIC+, USA MK IV, USA MK V, USA Pre

**BOGNER** - Bogfish, Euro Blue, Euro Uber, Shiver

**FRIEDMAN** - Dirty Shirley, Friedman BE, Friedman HBE, Friedman
Smallbox

## []{#5F1_TWEED_CHAMPLIFIER_(narrow-panel_Fender_Tweed_Champ,_5F1)}[5F1 TWEED CHAMPLIFIER (narrow-panel Fender Tweed Champ, 5F1)]{#5F1_TWEED_CHAMPLIFIER_.28narrow-panel_Fender_Tweed_Champ.2C_5F1.29 .mw-headline}

[![5f1 Fender
t.png](/wiki/images/thumb/3/33/5f1_Fender_t.png/300px-5f1_Fender_t.png){decoding="async"
width="300" height="278"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/3/33/5f1_Fender_t.png/450px-5f1_Fender_t.png 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/3/33/5f1_Fender_t.png/600px-5f1_Fender_t.png 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:5f1_Fender_t.png){.image}

Cab:

- original: Fender 1x8
- matching DynaCab: 1x8 5F1 Tweed

Volume control

Power tubes: 6V6

1.  \"This particular amp exhibits a unique breakup characteristic due
    to its single-ended design and simple circuit.\"
2.  \" Some of these old amps, and the 5F1 is one of them, will actually
    produce a sub-octave. It\'s why some players value them so much
    because it makes them sound full and warm.\"

## []{#5F1_TWEED_EC_CHAMPLIFIER_(2011_Fender_EC_Vibro-Champ)}[5F1 TWEED EC CHAMPLIFIER (2011 Fender EC Vibro-Champ)]{#5F1_TWEED_EC_CHAMPLIFIER_.282011_Fender_EC_Vibro-Champ.29 .mw-headline}

[![EC-Vibro-Champ.jpg](/wiki/images/5/58/EC-Vibro-Champ.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300"
height="300"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:EC-Vibro-Champ.jpg){.image}

Cab:

- original: Fender 1x8
- matching DynaCab: 1x8 5F1 Tweed

Volume, Tremolo effect

Power tubes: 6V6

1.  \"The circuit is slightly different than the original 5F1. It has
    cathode bypass caps giving it more gain.\"
    [\[1\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/fractal-audio-amp-models-5f1-tweed-fender-champ-5f1.111067/page-2#post-1508977){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"It\'s a single-ended power amp with negative feedback and bias
    tremolo. Subtle is the only possibility with this configuration.
    Bias tremolo works by modulating the quiescent operating point of
    the power tubes. With a single-ended power amp with negative
    feedback the gain doesn\'t change much as you change the operating
    point, hence the tremolo effect is subtle. Bias tremolo works best
    on amps with little to no negative feedback.\"
    [\[2\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/fw-q8-5f1-tweed-ec-4-scene-preset-vid-demo.126829/post-1509387){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#5F8_TWEED_BRIGHT_(Keith_Urban's_1959_narrow-panel_high-power_Fender_Tweed_Twin,_5F8)}[5F8 TWEED BRIGHT (Keith Urban\'s 1959 narrow-panel high-power Fender Tweed Twin, 5F8)]{#5F8_TWEED_BRIGHT_.28Keith_Urban.27s_1959_narrow-panel_high-power_Fender_Tweed_Twin.2C_5F8.29 .mw-headline}

Keith Urban\'s #1 Tweed Twin.

Cab:

- original: Fender 2x12 (P12N). Keith Urban\'s cab has Two-Rock speakers
- matching DynaCab: 2x12 Double Verb

Volume Bright, Volume Normal, Presence, Middle, Bass, Treble

Power tubes: 6L6, cathode follower

1.  \"Based on a 1959 Fender Twin Amp. This particular model is based on
    Keith Urban's "#1". Thank you Keith for allowing us the use of your
    prized amplifier.\"
2.  \"All the Fender models except the 59 Bassman and 5F8 Tweed don\'t
    have cathode followers.\"
    [\[3\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-version-5-00-beta-3.148907/page-3#post-1764588){.external

## []{#59_BASSGUY_BRIGHT_(1959_narrow-panel_Fender_Tweed_Bassman,_5F6-A)}[59 BASSGUY BRIGHT (1959 narrow-panel Fender Tweed Bassman, 5F6-A)]{#59_BASSGUY_BRIGHT_.281959_narrow-panel_Fender_Tweed_Bassman.2C_5F6-A.29 .mw-headline}

[![Bassman.jpg](/wiki/images/6/68/Bassman.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300"
height="273"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Bassman.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Normal channel
- Bright channel
- Jumpered channels

Cab:

- original: Fender 4x10 with Jensen Alnico 25W P10R or 40W P10Q
- matching DynaCab: 4x10 Bassguy RI

Volume Normal, Volume Bright, Bass, Middle, Treble, Presence

Power tubes: 6L6/5881, cathode follower

1.  \"All the Fender models except the 59 Bassman and 5F8 Tweed don\'t
    have cathode followers.\"
    [\[6\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-version-5-00-beta-3.148907/page-3#post-1764588){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The Bassman was reworked using an original 59 Bassman 5F6-A as a
    reference. This has a 12AY7 input buffer which has less gain than
    the reissue which uses a 12AX7A (7025 actually, same thing).\"
3.  \"The Bassman and Deluxe Tweed models are both modeled using a 12AY7
    as the input buffer. The Preamp Tube Type parameter only affects the
    tubes after the input buffer.\"
    [\[7\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/12ay7-preamp-tube-for-tweed-deluxe-and-bassman-models.175834/post-2135435){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"The input to the second 12AX7 is a summing node. Both volume
    controls affect the signal. If you plug into the Bright input the
    Normal volume control will also control the volume to some degree
    and change the frequency response.\"
    [\[8\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/bassman-how-do-the-way-the-2-drive-controls-interact.181986/post-2232557){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#59_BASSGUY_RI_JUMPED_(Fender_59_Bassman_LTD_Vintage_Reissue)}[59 BASSGUY RI JUMPED (Fender 59 Bassman LTD Vintage Reissue)]{#59_BASSGUY_RI_JUMPED_.28Fender_59_Bassman_LTD_Vintage_Reissue.29 .mw-headline}

[![FENDER BASSMAN
RI.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/1/19/FENDER_BASSMAN_RI.jpg/275px-FENDER_BASSMAN_RI.jpg){decoding="async"
width="275" height="300"
srcset="/wiki/images/1/19/FENDER_BASSMAN_RI.jpg 1.5x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:FENDER_BASSMAN_RI.jpg){.image}

Jumpered channels model

Cab:

- original: Fender 4x10 with Jensen Alnico 25W P10R or 40W P10Q
- matching DynaCab: 4x10 Bassguy RI

Volume Normal, Volume Bright, Bass, Middle, Treble, Presence

Power tubes: 6L6

See [59
Bassguy](/wiki/index.php?title=Amp_models#59_BASSGUY_BRIGHT_.281959_narrow-panel_Fender_Tweed_Bassman.2C_5F6-A.29 "Amp models")

1.  \"There are quite a few differences between a 5F6-A and the reissue:
    [\[9\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/bassman-how-do-the-way-the-2-drive-controls-interact.181986/post-2358853){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
    1.  12AX7A vs. 12AY7 input tube.
    2.  Different tone stack (this is a big one).
    3.  Different presence network.
    4.  Different B+ voltage.
    5.  6L6s vs 5881s (minimal difference).

## []{#65_BASSGUY_BASS_(1965_blackface_Fender_Bassman_head,_AB165)}[65 BASSGUY BASS (1965 blackface Fender Bassman head, AB165)]{#65_BASSGUY_BASS_.281965_blackface_Fender_Bassman_head.2C_AB165.29 .mw-headline}

[![Ab165.png](/wiki/images/thumb/f/f3/Ab165.png/300px-Ab165.png){decoding="async"
width="300" height="136"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/f/f3/Ab165.png/450px-Ab165.png 1.5x, /wiki/images/f/f3/Ab165.png 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Ab165.png){.image}

Models:

- Bass channel
- Normal channel

Cab:

- original: Fender 2x12 (Oxford)
- matching DynaCab: 2x12 65 Bassguy

Volume, Bass, Treble, Bright switch (Normal channel only), fixed
Presence circuit (Presence should be at 10)

Power tubes: 6L6

1.  \"Has a pissed-off Marshall vibe to it.\"
    [\[10\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/490912){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The 65 Bassguy was matched to a 65 Bassman that Dweezil sent me.
    It\'s a vicious amp that sounds more like a Plexi than a Fender.
    It\'s the infamous AB165 circuit which is very crunchy and bright
    and does not sound like your typical Fender.\"
    [\[11\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/am-i-the-only-one-who-noticed-that-some-amps-have-alot-more-gain.51123/page-2#post-658833){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"It\'s a crazy sounding amp, sounds nothing like your typical
    Fender.\"
    [\[12\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/another-v10-preview.62489){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"The AB165 uses 7025 preamp tubes (which are relabeled 12AX7). The
    phase inverter, however, is a 12AT7. The secret to the AB165 is the
    summing stage. It uses an inverting summing amp to sum the Normal
    and Bass inputs. This stage clips, because of all the local negative
    feedback, quite hard.\"
    [\[13\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/){.external .autonumber
    target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## [65 BASSGUY NORMAL]{#65_BASSGUY_NORMAL .mw-headline}

\
\

------------------------------------------------------------------------

Regarding the following 1959SLP and 1987X models:

1.  \"One of the first mods people make to real \'Plexi\' Marshalls is
    to \"clip the bright cap\". The bright cap varied over the years,
    supposedly depending on what was lying around in the shop. The model
    defaults to the bright cap in the circuit. If you turn off Bright
    you\'re effectively clipping the bright cap. The bright cap in
    Marshalls can be very bright and harsh. However, if you crank the
    Master you might find the extra brightness helps compensate for the
    power amp getting darker.\"
2.  \"It\'s the way a Plexi is supposed to sound. That\'s due to the
    cathode follower. That raspiness helps it cut through in a mix. I
    own three of them and they are that fizzy.\"
    [\[14\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/576475){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"Don\'t be afraid to turn the bass all the way down or the treble
    all the way up. Just like with the actual amp. For example, on the
    Normal channel of a Plexi most people turn the bass way down.
    Otherwise it\'s too flubby.\"
    [\[15\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/577248){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"My settings for a \"typical\" Plexi tone are Bass: 2, Mid: 8,
    Treble 7.5. Adjust Presence to taste.\"
    [\[16\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1179420){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  (Boston/Rockman sound) \"Plexi Jump. Everything on 7. Put a Filter
    block in front: Type: Peaking, Freq: \~800 Hz, Q: 0.707, Gain 12
    dB.\"
6.  \"What you are hearing is output transformer high frequency
    resonance. Old Plexis didn\'t do this because they had good
    transformers. New transformers are crappy and resonate at the cutoff
    frequency because they are underdamped. This causes a raspy, fizzy
    texture to the distortion. The transformer resonance is adjustable
    but the parameter isn\'t exposed to the user. When you turn it up
    you get that same squishy rasp that you are hearing. For the Plexis
    I have the damping set to flat with no resonance because that\'s how
    our vintage Plexis measure. Our 50W is a little underdamped but
    people complain about raspy high frequencies so I erred on the safe
    side.\"
    [\[17\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/dimed-real-plexi-vs-dimed-simulation-q8-01.127161/page-2#post-1513888){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  \"When modding Marshalls for higher gain sometimes the modder will
    decrease the input frequency response to reduce noise and fizziness.
    You can do this by reducing the high-cut frequency in the input EQ.
    Or you can use a high-shelf filter which is a little more subtle.
    Another technique is to put a capacitor across the second-to-last
    triode stage. This is the \"Triode 1 Plate Freq\" parameter. Reduce
    this to around 2 kHz to start which is typical of amps like an
    SLO100, etc.\"
    [\[18\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/dialling-in-the-marshalls.143682/post-1707222){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
8.  \"All the distortion comes from the power amp so the tone controls
    don\'t do much.\"
    [\[19\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-4-cygnus-firmware-public-beta.170253/post-2052743){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
9.  \"The following models have the 0.68uF cap on the second triode:
    [\[20\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-firmware-version-20-05-public-beta-beta-1.187133/page-4#post-2317922){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
    - Plexi 50W Normal
    - Plexi 50W High 2
    - Plexi 50W Jumped
    - Brit Brown
    - Plexi 100W Normal
    - Plexi 100W High
    - Plexi 100W Jumped
    - Plexi 100W 1970
    - 1959SLP Normal
    - 1959SLP Treble
    - 1959SLP Jumped\"

## []{#1959SLP_JUMPED_(100W_Marshall_Super_Lead_Plexi_1959_reissue)}[1959SLP JUMPED (100W Marshall Super Lead Plexi 1959 reissue)]{#1959SLP_JUMPED_.28100W_Marshall_Super_Lead_Plexi_1959_reissue.29 .mw-headline}

## []{#5153_100W_BLUE_(EVH_5150-III)}[5153 100W BLUE (EVH 5150-III)]{#5153_100W_BLUE_.28EVH_5150-III.29 .mw-headline}

[![5153.png](/wiki/images/thumb/0/04/5153.png/300px-5153.png){decoding="async"
width="300" height="130"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/0/04/5153.png/450px-5153.png 1.5x, /wiki/images/0/04/5153.png 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:5153.png){.image}

Models:

- 100W amp, Green channel
- 100W amp, Blue channel
- 100W amp, Red channel
- 100W Stealth amp, Green channel
- 100W Stealth amp, Blue channel
- 100W Stealth amp, Red channel
- 50W amp, Blue channel

Cab:

- original: 5150 4x12, 2x12 (G12H, G12EVH)
- matching DynaCab: 4x12 5153, 2x12 5153 Stealth

Gain, Low, Mid, High, Volume, Presence, Resonance/Depth (50w and Stealth
models only)

Power tubes: 6L6

1.  \"IMO, it\'s a very good amp. The build-quality is great and the
    design is very good. It is similar to the previous versions but
    voiced a bit different. Personally, I think all of the 5150\'s have
    more gain stages than necessary which just makes for unnecessary
    failure points but the \"OMG, this amp has sooo many toobz it must
    sound awesome\" marketing makes it understandable. It\'s incredibly
    heavy though.\"
    [\[26\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/679483){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"A 5150 uses a fixed bias with no adjustment. Depending on the
    tubes used the bias can run from average to cold. The model uses
    average. Some people like a colder sound. If you prefer your amps
    biased cold, then reduce the bias parameter to taste.\"
    [\[27\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/742231){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The 50W version has a different input network than the 100W
    version for that channel. The 50W version has about twice the gain
    as a result. Otherwise things are pretty similar. You can simulate
    this using the Input Trim knob.\"
    [\[28\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1042144){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"The red channels (of 50w and 100w models) are identical.\"
    [\[29\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/5153-50w-blue-red.106463/#post-1273739){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"Some amps have a fixed depth circuit, e.g. 5153, Freidman BE/HBE,
    Dirty Shirley, TripTik, Tucana, et. al. In these cases the Depth
    knob will default to a value that corresponds to the fixed
    circuit.\"
    [\[30\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/lets-talk-about-the-depth-control.88747/#post-1071598){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"The 5150 models are absolutely identical to our reference amp.\"
    [\[31\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/legacy-amp-models-consider-revisiting-full-honest-request-and-opinion.160349/post-1919792){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  \"The Normal Gain input has a very low input impedance, about 44K in
    addition to cutting the gain in half. Use the Input Impedance
    feature of the Input block to simulate. Try 32K.\"
    [\[32\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/why-fractal-is-good-for-my-sanity-and-my-wallet.167246/post-2008937){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
8.  \"Another technique is to use negative feedback to the grid. This is
    done in 5150-based designs which makes the stage clip even harder.
    The last stage of a 5150 basically looks like a diode clipper. The
    harder the clipping the more overtones that are created and the
    better the tone cuts. Without those overtones your sound is lost in
    the mix.\"
    [\[33\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/fizz-is-good.67719/#post-833875){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
9.  \"A 5150\'s presence control has almost no effect from 0 to 7. After
    7 the treble increases rapidly. The taper of the presence control in
    a 5150 is a log30 IIRC (maybe log10, I\'d have to check my notes).
    If anything it should be linear. Ideally it should be reverse log.
    (\...) Why they chose a log taper in the 5150 is a mystery. Since
    the power amp has similarities to a Marshall perhaps Eddie wanted
    the presence control to behave like his old Marshalls. Another
    possibility is the designer felt the amp was too bright with all
    knobs at noon (and a linear taper presence pot) and changed the
    taper to reduce the brightness.\"
    [\[34\]](https://www.thegearpage.net/board/index.php?threads/blind-test-mesa-dual-rectifier-vs-mystery-modeler-update-results-revealed.2208367/post-31639265){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
10. \"Amps with low amounts of negative feedback in the bass region are
    sensitive to the impedance curve. The 5153 is one of these amps due
    to its NFB circuit.\"
    [\[35\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/evh-amp-vs-axe-fx-qc-and-tmp.3593/post-133163){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
11. (about bias) \"Rev. D of the schematic which was Jan. 15 2013 specs
    30mA per tube. This was changed to 27.5 mA per tube somewhere
    between then and Dec. 11 2015. There apparently haven\'t been any
    changes to that spec since. So in the past 10 years every amp
    shipped has been at least 27.5 mA.\"
    [\[36\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/5150-presence-knob.199908/page-5#post-2492348){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
12. \"The Presence control on the real amps is the wrong taper IMO. The
    amps use a 20A taper. As such the Presence knob doesn\'t do anything
    until you turn it up to around 3/4. The 50W version of those amps,
    however, use a reverse-log taper, which is the correct taper IMO. My
    belief is they realized the taper was wrong and implemented the fix
    on the 50W version which was introduced later.\"
    [\[37\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/5150-presence-knob.199908/post-2491966){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
13. \"Changed Presence control taper on all 6160 and 5153 amp models to
    replicate the actual amp.\"
14. \"That model doesn\'t use a cathode follower.\" and \"They don\'t
    exhibit any nonlinear behavior. Therefore the model doesn\'t use a
    cathode follower. Models only use a cathode follower when they
    exhibit nonlinearity.\" and \"The 5153 is specifically designed so
    that the cathode follower doesn\'t do what a cathode follower
    usually does.\"
    [\[38\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-25-04-release.205702/page-6#post-2567387){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
15. \"A 2203 isn\'t known for string definition. It suffers from
    considerable bias excursion as do most vintage designs. You can turn
    down the Master Bias Excursion which will help or use a more modern
    amp (like a 515x) which is intentionally designed to limit bias
    excursion. \[IMO people who want \"string definition\" don\'t want
    what I call \"clutter\". Vintage designs exhibit considerable bias
    excursion. This causes the duty cycle to change and introduces
    intermodulation distortion (IMD). IMD manifests as a low-frequency
    rumble (among other things). IMD, however, makes things sound warmer
    when rolling off the volume. Without some IMD amps can sound
    sterile, especially at lower gain. Turning down the Master Bias
    Excursion reduces the amount of IMD. You can also experiment with
    the Preamp Bias control and Cathode Follower parameters. Cathode
    followers introduce their own type of \"clutter\". The 5150 used a
    plate-driven tone stack with feedback to eliminate the clutter
    associated with a cathode follower. The 5153 uses a cathode follower
    but attenuates the signal prior to prevent overdriving the cathode
    follower thereby eliminating the clutter.\"
    [\[39\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/high-gain-string-definition.213497){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
16. \"The 5150 family is unique in that it has a high treble boost after
    the preamp. It\'s quite a bit too. IIRC it\'s about 20 dB. It\'s
    done right before the phase inverter. I presume Eddie had lost much
    of his high frequency hearing by this point and the designer added
    this stage to satisfy Eddie\'s need for brightness.\"
    [\[40\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/5153-makes-other-amps-sound-muffled.220435/#post-2778867){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
17. \"The more stages an amp has the more the tube\'s gain affects the
    overall gain. For example, if the tube\'s gain is 100 and there are
    five gain stages (like a 5150) the total gain would be 100\^5 =
    10x10\^9. If the tube gain is 95 the overall gain would be 95\^5 =
    7.74x10\^9. That\'s about 2.5 dB lower. This is a greatly simplified
    example. FWIW, our reference amp\'s gain agrees with the theoretical
    gain..\"
    [\[41\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/5150-block-letter-now-sounds-muffled.220486/page-5#post-2783746){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#5153_100W_STEALTH_BLUE_(EVH_5150III_100S_100W)}[5153 100W STEALTH BLUE (EVH 5150III 100S 100W)]{#5153_100W_STEALTH_BLUE_.28EVH_5150III_100S_100W.29 .mw-headline}

1.  \"The Blue channel gain knob affects the Red channel somewhat. I
    modeled it with the Blue channel gain knob at noon.\"
    [\[42\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-23-04-release.199875/post-2491407){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The Red channel has much more gain but the Gain pot taper is very
    different. The Red channel has a 5A taper, while the Blue channel
    has a 30A taper so at noon it will appear as though the Blue channel
    has more gain.\"
    [\[43\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-23-04-release.199875/post-2491406){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

    Blue channel has about 2.5 times more gain. The Green channel has
    over five times the gain.\"
    [\[45\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-23-04-release.199875/page-10#post-2492792){.external

## []{#AC-20_12AX7_BASS_(Morgan_AC20_Deluxe)}[AC-20 12AX7 BASS (Morgan AC20 Deluxe)]{#AC-20_12AX7_BASS_.28Morgan_AC20_Deluxe.29 .mw-headline}

[![Morgan.jpg](/wiki/images/6/6f/Morgan.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300"
height="189"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Morgan.jpg){.image}

Models:

- 12AX7 Bass
- 12AX7 Treble
- EF86 Bass
- EF86 Treble

The AM4 has a single model with switches

Cab:

- original: Morgan 1x12 (G12 Alnico Blue)
- matching DynaCab: 1x12 AC20

Volume, Cut, Sun/Moon switch (= Bright switch), Brilliance switch (=
Bass Cut), power scaling (not modeled), EF86/12AX7 switch

Power tubes: EL84

No negative feedback

1.  \"The AC-20 model is based on the amp with the power scaling at
    maximum power which effectively disables it (and sounds best IMO).\"
    [\[46\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1079502){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The AC-20 has power scaling. The Axe-Fx II does not model the
    power scaling circuit as there is no point in that.\"
    [\[47\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/power-level-ac-20.89488/#post-1079494){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"As with the real amp I dial in quite a bit of Hi-Cut.\"
    [\[48\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/recommend-an-amp-for-p-w.106093/#post-1268874){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"I think an AC-20 does the Vox thing better than Vox.\"
    [\[49\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/recognition-and-respect-to-cliff-and-his-morgan-ac20.155040/post-1844685){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"AC-30\'s have a poorly designed cathode follower. The bias point
    is totally wrong and crushes one side of the signal considerably.
    IMO either the cathode resistor should be 100K or the plate resistor
    of the preceding stage should be higher, 200K. The clipping is
    extremely asymmetric. Too much IMO. A little asymmetry is good
    because it warms things up. Too much causes excessive even-order
    harmonics which makes things fuzzy and indistinct. The clipping is
    so asymmetric on an AC-30 that it\'s almost a half-wave rectifier.
    You can tweak this by adjusting the Preamp Bias point and/or
    lowering the Cathode Follower Compression. Or you can lower the
    Harmonics value which reduces the asymmetric distortion. The
    downside of that is that it then overdrives the phase inverter
    causing blocking distortion from excessive bias excursion. Another
    thing to try is to increase the Grid Clipping value which will add a
    little headroom. Start with the Bias point. AC-30\'s are very
    sensitive to the tube type and part tolerances. A tiny change in the
    bias point can make a big difference. The default bias point is
    based on Mullard ECC83 tubes. I prefer the AC-20 because it doesn\'t
    have a cathode follower so doesn\'t suffer from these problems. The
    cathode follower in an AC-30 doesn\'t even do all that much.
    Normally you use a cathode follower to preset a low-impedance source
    to the tone stack but the tone stack in an AC-30 doesn\'t present
    that great of a load anyways.\"
    [\[50\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-version-5-02.148983/page-11#post-1767187){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"One reason I like the AC-20 is that it runs the tubes hotter and
    exhibits less crossover distortion.\"
    [\[51\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/papery-buzz-under-some-models.149193/page-2#post-1772639){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  \"The Sun/Moon equals the Bright Switch. The Bass/Treble switch
    would be different amp models. So AC20 EF86 Bass model would be the
    Bass/Treble switch in the Bass position, the switch on the back in
    EF86 position and then the Bright switch on the model is the
    Sun/Moon switch on the amp.\"
    [\[52\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-version-10-00.154850/post-1842330){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
8.  \"So I was testing the next beta and selected the AC-20. Was hearing
    a lot of ghost notes compared to the old algorithm (in the debug
    build I can select between algorithms with a hidden parameter) and
    figured that couldn\'t be right. Hooked up the real AC-20 and, sure
    enough, ghost notes galore at the same settings.\"
    [\[53\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-10-0-public-beta.154714/post-1840850){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
9.  \"Our reference amp is a head with matching 1x12 cab.\"
    [\[54\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/recognition-and-respect-to-cliff-and-his-morgan-ac20.155040/post-1844744){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
10. \"The normal channel on a Vox would be closest to the Morgan. The
    Brilliant channel is a \"Top Boost\" which means it has a tone stack
    and a significant midrange cut. The normal channel has no tone
    stack. You can\'t compare a a Morgan AC20 to the Brilliant channel
    of an AC30 and declare that one sounds better than the other.
    Totally different preamps and, therefore, different sound.
    Personally I think the AC20 is a better amp. Better made, better
    quality components, much better transformers. If you want that
    chimey AC30 sound you put an EQ before it and suck out some mids.\"
    [\[55\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/how-accurate-is-fractals-amp-modeling.168786/post-2064189){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## [AC-20 EF86 BASS]{#AC-20_EF86_BASS .mw-headline}

## [AC-20 EF86 TREBLE]{#AC-20_EF86_TREBLE .mw-headline}

## []{#ANGLE_SEVERE_1_(Engl_Savage_120)}[ANGLE SEVERE 1 (Engl Savage 120)]{#ANGLE_SEVERE_1_.28Engl_Savage_120.29 .mw-headline}

[![Savage.png](/wiki/images/thumb/3/39/Savage.png/300px-Savage.png){decoding="async"
width="300" height="104"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/3/39/Savage.png/450px-Savage.png 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/3/39/Savage.png/600px-Savage.png 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Savage.png){.image}

Models:

- Lead channel, Contour switch: off (boosts lower midrange around 500
  Hz)
- Lead channel, Contour switch: on (boosts from 1200 Hz and cuts lower
  midrange)

The AM4 has a single model with Contour switch

Cab:

- original: Engl 4x12 (V30, V60)
- matching DynaCab: 4x12 Recto Straight

Gain (input sensitivity), Lead (distortion), Lead Boost switch, Contour
switch, Bass, Middle, Treble, Rough/Smooth switch (not modeled), Master,
Presence, Depth Boost switch

Power tubes: 6550

1.  \"From noon and up it\'s a presence boost, from noon down it\'s a
    presence cut.\"
    [\[56\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-ii-quantum-rev-1-03-firmware-release.106931/page-12#post-1280997){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"(\...) Engl Savage presence network which reduces negative
    feedback as the control is turned down causing an increase in
    volume.\"
    [\[57\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-5-cygnus-firmware-public-beta-2.170901/post-2059273){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  "The Depth control on the amp is a switch. You would set the Depth
    on the model to either 0 or 10 to duplicate this behavior. Depth
    being controlled by a switch goes back to Peavey and their patent
    for a pot to control depth. If you use a pot for depth you had to
    pay them royalties so amp makers would use a switch to get around
    this. I believe the patent has expired so newer amps more often have
    a knob. Also note that older versions of the Savage had a different
    feedback network that caused the volume to change pretty
    dramatically as a function of Presence. Newer versions (like our
    reference amp) have an added resistor that makes the Presence
    control behave more predictably."
    [\[58\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-29-00-public-beta.214333/page-8#post-2690802){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## [ANGLE SEVERE 2]{#ANGLE_SEVERE_2 .mw-headline}

## []{#ARCHEAN_(100W_PRS_Archon)}[ARCHEAN (100W PRS Archon)]{#ARCHEAN_.28100W_PRS_Archon.29 .mw-headline}

[![Archon.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/d/d0/Archon.jpg/325px-Archon.jpg){decoding="async"
width="325" height="183"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/d/d0/Archon.jpg/488px-Archon.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/d/d0/Archon.jpg/650px-Archon.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Archon.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Archean Clean: Clean channel
- Archean: Lead channel, Bright: off
- Archean Bright: Lead channel, Bright: on

Based on 100W amp
[\[59\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-release-version-14-01.165716/post-1990412){.external
.autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

Cab:

- original: Celestion V-Type
- matching DynaCab: 4x12 Friedman GB

Master, Bass, Middle, Treble, Bright switch, Volume, Depth, Presence,
Output Power (not modeled)

Power tubes: 6L6

1.  \"You have to crank the MV on the real amp. The preamp is very
    \"dry\" so to get the juices flowing the power amp needs to be
    working hard. This also smooths out that funky midrange.\"
    [\[60\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-release-version-14-01.165716/page-10#post-1990153){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"I think part of the reason the real Archon needs to be cranked is
    because the power supply is too stiff. It\'s got six (!!!) big caps
    filtering the B+. That\'s too much filtering IMO unless you\'re
    playing at arena volumes. If I were to make a modification to the
    amp it would be a switch to disconnect four of those caps so the
    supply is more bouncy at moderate volumes. Maybe also a tube
    rectifier to add some more sponge.\"
    [\[61\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-release-version-14-01.165716/page-10#post-1990169){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#ATOMICA_HIGH_(Cameron_Atomica)}[ATOMICA HIGH (Cameron Atomica)]{#ATOMICA_HIGH_.28Cameron_Atomica.29 .mw-headline}

[![Atomica.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/e/e4/Atomica.jpg/300px-Atomica.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="128"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/e/e4/Atomica.jpg/450px-Atomica.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/e/e4/Atomica.jpg/600px-Atomica.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Atomica.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Low gain input
- High gain input

Cab:

- original: cab with G12H speakers
- matching DynaCab: 4x12 5153

Thump/Depth, Presence, Bass, Middle, Treble, Master, Gain, Edge (=
Bright switch), 3-way Gain Voice switch

Power tubes: EL34

Saturation: on

1.  \"The Atomica can tolerate high MV because it is a \"Jose-style
    MV\". The Jose-style MV imparts a very high source resistance to the
    tone stack which causes much more insertion loss and therefore lower
    drive level into the power amp.\"
    [\[62\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/748843){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"Cameron amps are basically modified Marshalls. The Atomica is
    essentially a slightly modified JCM800 with a Jose-style zener
    clipper.\"
    [\[63\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/dialling-in-the-marshalls.143682/page-5#post-1706652){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  (fuzzy tone with Bright on) \"That\'s the way those amps sound with
    the bright switch on. It\'s due to the location of the drive
    control. Turn down the Preamp Bias Excursion to reduce it. The
    problem with those \"Mid Stage Drive\" designs using a Plexi drive
    network is that if you bypass the drive pot with a cap (bright cap)
    you also bypass any grid stoppage and the next stage goes into
    blocking distortion very easily. There\'s essentially a straight
    shot into the grid for all the high frequencies. Friedman probably
    realized this and that\'s why there\'s no bright cap on the BE as
    the BE is very similar to the Atomica.\"
    [\[64\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-4-cygnus-firmware-public-beta.170253/post-2052829){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"The Cameron is a genuine Cameron. I don\'t know the lineage of the
    Atomica.\"
    [\[65\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/are-any-of-the-cameron-models-of-mark-cameron-built-amps.199792/#post-2489827){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"I have an early Mark-built CCV. I\'m not sure about the provenance
    of the Atomica.\"
    [\[66\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/there-is-actually-a-jose-modded-marshall-in-the-fractal.7763/page-2#post-367370){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}\"

## [ATOMICA LOW]{#ATOMICA_LOW .mw-headline}

## []{#BAND-COMMANDER_(1968_silverface/blackface_Fender_Bandmaster_head,_AB763)}[BAND-COMMANDER (1968 silverface/blackface Fender Bandmaster head, AB763)]{#BAND-COMMANDER_.281968_silverface.2Fblackface_Fender_Bandmaster_head.2C_AB763.29 .mw-headline}

[![Bandmaster.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/7/7c/Bandmaster.jpg/300px-Bandmaster.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="122"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/7/7c/Bandmaster.jpg/450px-Bandmaster.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/7/7c/Bandmaster.jpg/600px-Bandmaster.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Bandmaster.jpg){.image}

Vibrato channel model

Cab:

- original: Fender 2x12
- matching DynaCab: 2x12 65 Bassguy

Vibrato channel: Volume, Bright switch, Treble, Bass, Tremolo effect

Power tubes: 6L6

1.  \"The vibrato channel is loaded down by the vibrato circuit. The
    normal channel isn\'t. You can probably get close using the vibrato
    channel model by increasing the MV trim.\"
    [\[67\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/maroon-5-axe-fx-iii-awesomeness.146287/page-2#post-1730430){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#BIG_HAIR_(custom_model)}[BIG HAIR (custom model)]{#BIG_HAIR_.28custom_model.29 .mw-headline}

[![Logo small.png](/wiki/images/e/ef/Logo_small.png){decoding="async"
width="50"
height="50"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Logo_small.png){.image}

Custom Fractal Audio model

Matching DynaCab: 4x12 1960TV

Power tubes: 6L6

1.  \"It was a total guess. I just tuned it by ear. It\'s just my idea
    of what 80\'s hair metal might sound like.\"
    [\[68\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/700269/){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The FAS models are idealized and have some of the \"design flaws\"
    removed or reduced.\"
    [\[69\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-10-00-public-beta-2.154782/post-1841528){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"If I had my way there would be only FAS models but too many people
    demand reproductions of existing amps.\"
    [\[70\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/fas-class-a-is-even-better-than-the-real-thing.162257/post-1944014){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"The FAS models typically remove or minimize the undesirable
    characteristics of those old amps. Guitar tube amp design was
    nascent in the 60s and 70s and designers didn\'t fully understand
    the impact of overdriving tubes. One of the biggest issues was
    blocking distortion which is excessive bias excursion. When the grid
    conducts it shifts the bias point and in those old amps it can shift
    so much that the tube goes into cutoff prematurely. More modern
    designs employ grid stoppers and smaller coupling capacitors to
    reduce bias excursion.\"
    [\[71\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/fas-class-a-is-even-better-than-the-real-thing.162257/post-1944071){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#BLANKENSHIP_LEEDS_(Dweezil_Zappa's_Blankenship_Leeds_21)}[BLANKENSHIP LEEDS (Dweezil Zappa\'s Blankenship Leeds 21)]{#BLANKENSHIP_LEEDS_.28Dweezil_Zappa.27s_Blankenship_Leeds_21.29 .mw-headline}

[![Blankenship.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/3/30/Blankenship.jpg/300px-Blankenship.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="145"
srcset="/wiki/images/3/30/Blankenship.jpg 1.5x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Blankenship.jpg){.image}

Cab:

- original: 2x10, 1x12, 2x12 (G12M)
- matching DynaCab: 1x12 Div13 CJ11

Volume, Tone, Tremolo effect

Power tubes: EL84

No negative feedback

1.  \"Based on a Blankenship Leeds which is a boutique version of an 18W
    Marshall. This particular amp is known for sounding "big" despite
    being relatively low power.\"
2.  \"The model was matched to Dweezil\'s amp. He loaned it to me
    because it was one of his favorite amps and I can see why. It\'s a
    really cool amp.\"
3.  \"The amp has no hi-cut circuit therefore the control won\'t do
    anything. Neither will the Depth.\"
4.  \"18W Marshalls are kind of a bad design. The phase inverter drives
    the power tubes too hard which results in excessive bias excursion."
    [\[72\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/marshall-1974x.121516/#post-1446363){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"The phase inverter design causes significant bias excursion. That
    bias excursion, however, causes the amp to sound more open when
    driven hard (at the expense of crossover distortion).\"
    [\[73\]](https://www.thegearpage.net/board/index.php?threads/is-digital-getting-too-real.2275913/post-32977457){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#BLUDOJAI_CLEAN_(Bludotone_Ojai)}[BLUDOJAI CLEAN (Bludotone Ojai)]{#BLUDOJAI_CLEAN_.28Bludotone_Ojai.29 .mw-headline}

[![Bludotone
2.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/1/1b/Bludotone_2.jpg/350px-Bludotone_2.jpg){decoding="async"
width="350" height="200"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/1/1b/Bludotone_2.jpg/525px-Bludotone_2.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/1/1b/Bludotone_2.jpg/700px-Bludotone_2.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Bludotone_2.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Clean channel, PAB (Pre-Amp Bypass) off
- Overdrive channel, PAB off
- Overdrive channel, PAB on

Cab:

- original: Bludotone 1x12, 2x12 (G12-65, EVM)
- matching DynaCab: 4x12 Rumble EV12L

Volume, Overdrive Drive and Overdrive Level (Overdrive channel only),
Treble, Middle, Bass, Master, Presence. Switches: Bright, Mid (not
modeled), Rock/Jazz (not modeled). Footswitchable Pre-Amp Bypass (PAB):
bypasses the tonestack (Bass/Middle/Treble)

Power tubes: 6L6

Forum member AustinBuddy, previous owner of the original amp:

1.  \"The model is of a 100w 6L6 BludoDrive Ojai by Bludotone amps,
    using Fractal\'s MIMIC process. The Ojai has the same schematic as
    the famous \"Tan\" boutique amp played by Robben Ford. It pairs well
    with the factory Rumble 4X12 cabinet. On the Ojai there is a bright
    cap on the Master Volume. As you turn the MV down, it will get
    thinner. This makes the MV even more sensitive than usual since
    there's another interaction going on. To get the most range out of
    this amp, experiment with Master Volume and listen how it interacts
    with low or high Drive settings, similar to the real amp. The
    breakup range/tones between is wide and dynamic and can respond to
    your playing dynamics, getting crunchier as you dig in and cleaner
    as you play lighter. The amp\'s Bass response should increase
    noticeably as you turn up the Master Volume from the default MV
    position. Pair it with a G12-65H speaker. Cab Pack 17 has many
    choices (full disclosure, I produced 5 of the 6 Cabs in that Cab
    Pack). The BludoMix Cab in factory firmware is a 1x12 Alnico dual
    port cab, and will sound good but perhaps a tad darker (great for
    Jazz) on clean sounds than the G12-65H will. Now, if you like, put a
    Zen drive in front on the BludoClean amp\....or a boost\...and
    listen to how that clean channel wakes up fast for grittier leads
    and touch-responsiveness. For BludoLead, take the Lead default amp
    values. Put the Master Volume on 5. Put drive at 4-5 and Overdrive
    at 4-5, and experiment with the tone stack swaps above. If you want
    the amp to feedback effortlessly on a note, raise the overdrive
    setting higher combined with the gain, provided you have sufficient
    volume coming out your speakers to hit your guitar pickups in a
    reinforcing loop, it will do it! Throw a boost or Zen drive on that,
    if you like\...\"
    [\[74\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/dumble-ford-2-again.105028/page-2#post-1267280){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The tone stack in the PAB models is a neutral tone stack which is
    the same as lifting the ground. Put all knobs at noon if you want
    authentic. Unlike the amp, however, you can actually adjust the tone
    controls and something will happen. In the virtual realm we can have
    lifted tone stacks that actually still work.\"
    [\[75\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/love-3-0-but.147215/page-3#post-1739726){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"Pre, mid and post aren\'t absolute locations. They\'re relative to
    the particular model. In the Lead model there is a buffer and then
    three gain stages IIRC. Pre means the tone stack is before the three
    gain stage in this case. Changing it to Mid would put it after the
    first gain stage. In the Clean model there is only a buffer and one
    gain stage. In this case mid means the stack is between the buffer
    and gain stage. Changing it to pre would put it before the buffer.
    Since there are only two tubes pre would indicate before the buffer
    which is not what we want. In the PAB model there is no tone stack
    so I put a neutral tone stack after the gain stages (with a fixed
    attenuation after the buffer). This allows the most flexibility. The
    HRM case the neutral tone stack is replaced by a Marshall tone
    stack.\"
    [\[76\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-version-3-01.147229/page-2#post-1739969){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"The real amp has Overdrive Volume (sometimes labeled Ratio) and a
    Master Volume. The models assume the Overdrive Volume is at
    maximum.\"
    [\[77\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-release-version-16-01-cygnus.172911/post-2091820){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#BOGFISH_BROWN_(Bogner_Fish_preamp)}[BOGFISH BROWN (Bogner Fish preamp)]{#BOGFISH_BROWN_.28Bogner_Fish_preamp.29 .mw-headline}

[![Fish.png](/wiki/images/thumb/f/fb/Fish.png/300px-Fish.png){decoding="async"
width="300" height="62"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/f/fb/Fish.png/450px-Fish.png 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/f/fb/Fish.png/600px-Fish.png 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Fish.png){.image}

Models:

- Strato channel
- Brown channel

Matching DynaCab: 4x12 Friedman V30

Master, Gain, Bass, Mid, Treble

Power tubes: EL34

1.  \"I used the power amp models from the XTC.\"
    [\[78\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/bogner-strato-and-brown-poweramp-modeling.76238/#post-931081){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## [BOGFISH STRATO]{#BOGFISH_STRATO .mw-headline}

\

------------------------------------------------------------------------

Regarding the following BRIT 800 models:

1.  \"It is a very bright model. However, it sounds exactly like the amp
    it was based on. If it is too bright, you can adjust the various
    tone controls and parameters to reduce the brightness to your
    tastes. They are designed to be run loud and the brightness
    decreases as the MV is increased. The sound of 80\'s hair metal for
    sure.\"
    [\[79\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/afxii-jcm800-model.38498/#post-525964){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The saturation switch switches in a zener diode clipping stage
    right before the tone stack. This is the Arrendondo Mod.\"
    [\[80\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-ii-technical-questions-thread.35997/page-38#post-494304){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"Rips my head off here. I have to turn the presence way down. Check
    the MV. Too high and will get muddy.\"
    [\[81\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/jcm-800-sounds-a-bit-muddy-with-fw-6-0-tips.51063/#post-657800){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"That \"interference\" is due to all the treble peaking used in the
    design. JCM800s have quite a bit of treble boost. When you first
    attack the string the note is unpitched. It\'s basically a brief
    explosion of noise. The treble boosting amplifies the upper
    frequencies of this noise burst which is what you hear. However,
    when you playing in a loud mix that treble boosting helps the sound
    cut. Modern designs use more carefully crafted treble boosting to
    retain the cut but tame some of the harshness of the attack. This is
    accomplished typically by putting a capacitor in parallel with the
    plate resistor(s) which rolls off around a few kHz. This preserves
    the treble boost in the upper midrange but softens the attack. I
    believe the SLO100 was one of the first amps to do this. You can see
    this in the Axe-Fx II as your Triode Freq parameters. You can soften
    the JCM800 attack by lowering the Triode Freq values. Most modern
    hi-gain designs use some form of HF rolloff like this. Another
    reason is that JCM800s use relatively low amounts of negative
    feedback (which is why they\'re so loud). This causes a treble boost
    in the power amp. Increase the Damping parameter to increase the
    negative feedback.\"
    [\[82\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/cliff-how-can-i-ever-have-doubted-you.63107/#post-781950){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"Those amps are all designed to get their character from power amp
    distortion. If you don\'t push the power amp all you are hearing is
    the preamp which is voiced to be trebly. The power amp then
    compresses the highs and the sound gets fatter.\"
    [\[83\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1235311){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  (moving Master volume to post phase inverter) \"It\'s called PPI MV
    or the \"Lar-Mar Mod\".\"
    [\[84\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/dial-in-popular-mods.119757/#post-1424257){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  \"At low MV the source resistance into the PI is low which raises
    the highpass frequency due to the coupling cap and raises the
    lowpass frequency due to the Miller capacitance and snubber. As you
    increase the MV the source resistance increases which decreases both
    of these things. As you keep raising the MV the source resistance
    then starts to decrease as you get above 50% of the pot value.\"
    [\[85\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/setting-the-master-volume.119903/page-2#post-1428935){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
8.  \"When modding Marshalls for higher gain sometimes the modder will
    decrease the input frequency response to reduce noise and fizziness.
    You can do this by reducing the high-cut frequency in the input EQ.
    Or you can use a high-shelf filter which is a little more subtle.
    Another technique is to put a capacitor across the second-to-last
    triode stage. This is the \"Triode 1 Plate Freq\" parameter. Reduce
    this to around 2 kHz to start which is typical of amps like an
    SLO100, etc.\"
    [\[86\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/dialling-in-the-marshalls.143682/post-1707222){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
9.  \"JCM800s sound better with a hot bias IMO. The problem is the plate
    voltage is too high so when you set the bias higher the dissipation
    goes up and tube life is shortened. IMO they should\'ve made the
    plate voltage around 420V. That would allow a hotter bias with
    longer tube life at the expense of slightly less volume but JCM800s
    are ungodly loud anyways so\...\"
    [\[87\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/why-your-amp-doesnt-sound-like-our-amp.172907/post-2091305){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
10. \"A JCM800 sounds best when it is getting its distortion from a
    combination of preamp and power amp distortion.\"
    [\[88\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/setting-the-master-volume.119903/page-5#post-2618859){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
11. \"The factory value for the bright cap in a JCM800 is 1nF
    (1000pF).\"
    [\[89\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/what’s-the-deal-with-the-bright-cap-setting.216177/#post-2717240){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
12. \"I have four JCM800s. Every one has a 1000pF bright cap.\"
    [\[90\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/what’s-the-deal-with-the-bright-cap-setting.216177/#post-2717251){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#BRIT_800_2204_HIGH_(50W_Marshall_JCM_800_2204)}[BRIT 800 2204 HIGH (50W Marshall JCM 800 2204)]{#BRIT_800_2204_HIGH_.2850W_Marshall_JCM_800_2204.29 .mw-headline}

[![2203.png](/wiki/images/thumb/9/93/2203.png/325px-2203.png){decoding="async"
width="325" height="181"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/9/93/2203.png/488px-2203.png 1.5x, /wiki/images/9/93/2203.png 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:2203.png){.image}

Models:

- Low input
- High input

Cab:

- original: Marshall 4x12 (G12M, G12H, G12-75, V30)
- matching DynaCab: 4x12 1960TV

Pre-amp Volume, Bass, Middle, Treble, Presence, Master

Power tubes: EL34

1.  \"It\'s a vertical input Canada export version. I went through
    several before settling on this one as it was the best sounding by
    far.\"
    [\[91\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/jcm-800-question.103215/#post-1235691){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"Some of them are really dull. We have two 50 watters. One is a
    Canadian export with bat-handle switches and sounds glorious. All
    nasty and spitty and full of \"artifacts\". The other is a
    \"regular\" one with the rocker switches. It sounds like it has a
    blanket over it in comparison. Our model is based on the Canadian
    one. Oh, and I should add that someone removed the bright cap from
    the Canadian one. Probably because it\'s so nasty with it in. I
    installed a new one to bring it back to it\'s original glory. The
    key to JCM800\'s is to crank the MV to overcome the brightness of
    the preamp.\"
    [\[92\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/help-requested-new-afx-xl-and-digital-distortion-in-the-sound.123815/page-2#post-1478884){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"Our reference amp had the bright cap removed by a previous owner.
    I put it back in. I like it on, even with a bright guitar.\"
    [\[93\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/jcm800-with-our-without-bright-switch.131049/#post-1552301){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"The reference amp used for our model is a Canadian Export version
    (with the \"bat handle\" power switches). We have two JCM800s and
    this particular amp sounds way better than the regular one with the
    rocker type power switches. It\'s not as harsh with a warmer high
    end.\"
    [\[94\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/nux-mg300-vs-fm3-comparison.165102/post-1980841){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"We have two of them. One sounds amazing, the other not so much.
    The model is based, naturally, on the amazing sounding one.\"
    [\[95\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/buttons-functioning-as-on-amps.170531/post-2052806){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"The 2204 models have a 10K dropping resistor between the B+ and
    PI. The 2203 models have 20K. The 2203 has about 17% more preamp
    gain than the 2204 as a result.\"
    [\[96\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/brit-800-2204-vs-2203-thoughts.200705/post-2508569){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  (Low model) \"Preamp gain is very low in these amps. Turn the Master
    Volume up. I usually run it at 10.\"
    [\[97\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/brit-800-2203-low-and-brit-800-2204-low-almost-no-volume.208166/#post-2598865){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#BRIT_800_2203_HIGH_(100W_Marshall_JCM_800_2203_JMP)}[BRIT 800 2203 HIGH (100W Marshall JCM 800 2203 JMP)]{#BRIT_800_2203_HIGH_.28100W_Marshall_JCM_800_2203_JMP.29 .mw-headline}

[![JCM8002203.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/0/05/JCM8002203.jpg/300px-JCM8002203.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="119"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/0/05/JCM8002203.jpg/450px-JCM8002203.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/0/05/JCM8002203.jpg/600px-JCM8002203.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:JCM8002203.jpg){.image}

Model:

- Low input
- High input

Fractal Audio\'s 2203 is an unmodified unit with metal toggle switches
and faded brown grille cloth. It has vertical inputs and drake
transformers. The picture above is of the actual amp.

Cab:

- original: Marshall 4x12 (G12M)
- matching DynaCab: 4x12 1960TV

Presence, Bass, Middle, Treble, Master Volume, Pre-Amp Volume

Power tubes: EL34

See [Brit
800](/wiki/index.php?title=Amp_models#BRIT_800_2204_HIGH_.2850W_Marshall_JCM_800_2204.29 "Amp models")

1.  \"The reference amp I just received had no bright cap. It wasn\'t
    snipped out. It may have been removed by unsoldering it but if they
    did they cleaned up as there is no residual flux on the terminals.
    This is the second JCM800 I\'ve encountered with no bright cap. I
    installed a bright cap in it because every schematic shows a bright
    cap and the model is based on the amp w/ the bright cap installed.
    Other tidbits about it: B+ is a bit on the low side, around 450V.
    Feedback is 100K from 4-ohm tap. Transformers are same as US/UK
    versions. OT has 4/8/16 taps but 16-ohm tap is not connected. Preamp
    measures virtually identical to my 2204.\"
    [\[98\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/leons-new-video-comparing-2203-in-different-modelers.3866/#post-146022){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  (Low model) \"Preamp gain is very low in these amps. Turn the Master
    Volume up. I usually run it at 10.\"
    [\[99\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/brit-800-2203-low-and-brit-800-2204-low-almost-no-volume.208166/#post-2598865){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The 2204 models have a 10K dropping resistor between the B+ and
    PI. The 2203 models have 20K. The 2203 has about 17% more preamp
    gain than the 2204 as a result.\"
    [\[100\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/brit-800-2204-vs-2203-thoughts.200705/post-2508569){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## [BRIT 800 2203 LOW]{#BRIT_800_2203_LOW .mw-headline}

## []{#BRIT_800_#34_(50W_Marshall_JCM_800_with_Santiago_#34_modifications)}[BRIT 800 #34 (50W Marshall JCM 800 with Santiago #34 modifications)]{#BRIT_800_.2334_.2850W_Marshall_JCM_800_with_Santiago_.2334_modifications.29 .mw-headline}

[![Logo small.png](/wiki/images/e/ef/Logo_small.png){decoding="async"
width="50"
height="50"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Logo_small.png){.image}

Custom Fractal Audio model

Matching DynaCab: 4x12 1960TV

Power tubes: EL34

See [Brit
800](/wiki/index.php?title=Amp_models#BRIT_800_2204_HIGH_.2850W_Marshall_JCM_800_2204.29 "Amp models")

1.  \"Based on the "Santiago #34" modifications.\"
2.  \"The Brit 800 #34 does a better Slash than the AFS100 IMO. The
    AFS100 models are based on the actual amp but I think my version of
    #34 sounds more like AFD. I based the model on information I\'ve
    collected over the years about the mods that were done.\"
    [\[101\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-ii-quantum-rev-7-00-firmware-release.124944/page-5#post-1486357){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The Brit 800 #34 has a ton of treble boost and will squeal with
    certain guitars and/or certain IRs and/or certain types of
    amplification. Nature of the beast. No other amp has anywhere near
    the amount of treble boost. The AFD100 amp that Marshall produced
    years later (that was supposed to be a #34 copy) has nowhere near
    the amount of treble boost and has a huge snubber cap on the PI
    (which rolls off the treble). My gut tells me that they did this
    because they feared there would be too many reports of pickup squeal
    (or the amps would be too unstable at high gain).\"
    [\[102\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/squealing-like-mad.132058/#post-1563723){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

1.  \"Based on popular modified Marshall JCM800. These mods make the amp
    "heavier" and less strident.\"

## []{#BRIT_AFS100_1_(Marshall_AFD100SCE)}[BRIT AFS100 1 (Marshall AFD100SCE)]{#BRIT_AFS100_1_.28Marshall_AFD100SCE.29 .mw-headline}

[![AFD.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/5/58/AFD.jpg/300px-AFD.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="121"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/5/58/AFD.jpg/450px-AFD.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/5/58/AFD.jpg/600px-AFD.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:AFD.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Amp in mode \"#34\"
- Amp in mode \"AFD\"

Cab:

- original: Marshall 4x12 (V30)
- matching DynaCab: 4x12 Friedman V30

Gain, Bass, Middle, Treble, Presence, Master, #34/AFD switch, Depth
(Brit Super model only)

Power tubes: 6550

1.  \"I have an actual Slash signature model and spent a lot of time
    measuring, listening and comparing.\"
    [\[105\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-ii-quantum-rev-2-01-firmware-release.111657/page-8#post-1337247){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The Brit 800 #34 does a better Slash than the AFS100 IMO. The
    AFS100 models are based on the actual amp but I think my version of
    #34 sounds more like AFD. I based the model on information I\'ve
    collected over the years about the mods that were done.\"
    [\[106\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-ii-quantum-rev-7-00-firmware-release.124944/page-5#post-1486357){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The Brit 800 #34 has a ton of treble boost and will squeal with
    certain guitars and/or certain IRs and/or certain types of
    amplification. Nature of the beast. No other amp has anywhere near
    the amount of treble boost. The AFD100 amp that Marshall produced
    years later (that was supposed to be a #34 copy) has nowhere near
    the amount of treble boost and has a huge snubber cap on the PI
    (which rolls off the treble). My gut tells me that they did this
    because they feared there would be too many reports of pickup squeal
    (or the amps would be too unstable at high gain).\"
    [\[107\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/squealing-like-mad.132058/#post-1563723){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"The amount of treble peaking needed for an amp at a given drive is
    highly dependent on the guitar. For example my guess is that the
    AFD100 was designed around a Les Paul. With my Suhr it\'s much too
    bright because that\'s a very bright guitar. So one of the first
    things I do with the AFS100 model is turn down the bright cap a
    bit.\"
    [\[108\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/firmware-1-11.140004/page-2#post-1660177){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"Reference amp is a Slash AFD100 Signature Special Collector\'s
    Edition #76. Hand-signed by Slash with COA.\"
    [\[109\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-19-00-beta-3.180388/post-2207142){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"Default MV is quite high in that model which will mask the effect
    of the Presence control since the power amp is distorting heavily. I
    find that amp sounds best with the power amp driven hard). Turn the
    MV down and you\'ll notice the Presence control will have much more
    effect.\"
    [\[110\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-firmware-version-21-00.189017/post-2343032){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#BRIT_BROWN_(custom_model:_Plexi_\"Brown_Sound\")}[BRIT BROWN (custom model: Plexi \"Brown Sound\")]{#BRIT_BROWN_.28custom_model:_Plexi_.22Brown_Sound.22.29 .mw-headline}

[![Logo small.png](/wiki/images/e/ef/Logo_small.png){decoding="async"
width="50"
height="50"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Logo_small.png){.image}

Custom Fractal Audio model

Matching DynaCab: 4x12 5153

Power tubes: EL34

Saturation: on

1.  \"The Brit Brown was built by ear.\"
    [\[111\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/evhs-original-plexi-and-the-fas-brit-brown-amp.81986/#post-995265){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"Brit Brown is my personal take on what the ultimate \"Brown\"
    plexi should sound like. It\'s based on a 100W SLP with Arredondo
    mods and a few little voicing tweaks.\"
    [\[112\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1152917){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The FAS models are idealized and have some of the \"design flaws\"
    removed or reduced.\"
    [\[113\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-10-00-public-beta-2.154782/post-1841528){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"If I had my way there would be only FAS models but too many people
    demand reproductions of existing amps.\"
    [\[114\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/fas-class-a-is-even-better-than-the-real-thing.162257/post-1944014){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"The FAS models typically remove or minimize the undesirable
    characteristics of those old amps. Guitar tube amp design was
    nascent in the 60s and 70s and designers didn\'t fully understand
    the impact of overdriving tubes. One of the biggest issues was
    blocking distortion which is excessive bias excursion. When the grid
    conducts it shifts the bias point and in those old amps it can shift
    so much that the tube goes into cutoff prematurely. More modern
    designs employ grid stoppers and smaller coupling capacitors to
    reduce bias excursion.\"
    [\[115\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/fas-class-a-is-even-better-than-the-real-thing.162257/post-1944071){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"There\'s a 0.68uF cap on the second triode.\"
    [\[116\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-firmware-version-20-05-public-beta-beta-1.187133/post-2317922){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#BRIT_JM45_(Marshall_JTM_45)}[BRIT JM45 (Marshall JTM 45)]{#BRIT_JM45_.28Marshall_JTM_45.29 .mw-headline}

[![JTM.png](/wiki/images/thumb/7/74/JTM.png/300px-JTM.png){decoding="async"
width="300" height="167"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/7/74/JTM.png/450px-JTM.png 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/7/74/JTM.png/600px-JTM.png 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:JTM.png){.image}

Models:

- Treble (High) channel
- Jumpered channels

Cab:

- original: Marshall 4x12 (G12M, G12H)
- matching DynaCab: 4x12 1960TV

Volume Normal, Volume High Treble, Bass, Middle, Treble, Presence

Power tubes: EL34

1.  \"They had no Master Volumes so people rarely got the Drive past
    3.00 since it would melt your face. Without the specter of having
    your skin flayed off as is afforded by a model of the amp, the
    temptation is to turn the Drive way up. When you do this the low
    notes get very muddy. Single notes can form an almost perfect square
    wave which will sound like a synthesizer.\"
    [\[117\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/jm45-and-jm45-jump-sound-horrible-for-low-e-and-a-strings-not-a-bug.76286/#post-931633){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"Our reference amp has a 100 pF bright cap. Many JTM45s did not but
    I think they sound better with one. A JTM45 with a bright cap is
    similar to a Superlead. If you want the Channel 1 sound with an
    Axe-Fx use the Brit JM45 Jump model and turn the Treble Drive knob
    all the way down.\"
    [\[118\]](http://www.thegearpage.net/board/index.php?threads/fractal-vs-helix-the-comparison-series-made-by-yours-truly.1757067/page-2#post-22868763){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"When modding Marshalls for higher gain sometimes the modder will
    decrease the input frequency response to reduce noise and fizziness.
    You can do this by reducing the high-cut frequency in the input EQ.
    Or you can use a high-shelf filter which is a little more subtle.
    Another technique is to put a capacitor across the second-to-last
    triode stage. This is the \"Triode 1 Plate Freq\" parameter. Reduce
    this to around 2 kHz to start which is typical of amps like an
    SLO100, etc.\"
    [\[119\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/dialling-in-the-marshalls.143682/post-1707222){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"The very first models used a 5881, after that KT66 then EL34.\"
    [\[120\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/jtm45-bug.164255/post-1969445){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  (negative feedback) \"I\'ve seen JTM45s with 27K off the 16-ohm tap.
    That\'s a lot of feedback. In this case you would then double the
    feedback on top of the 3.3 so 9.9 or so.\"
    [\[121\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/negative-feedback.188769/post-2340464){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## [BRIT JM45 JUMPED]{#BRIT_JM45_JUMPED .mw-headline}

## []{#BRIT_JVM_OD1_GREEN_(Marshall_JVM410H)}[BRIT JVM OD1 GREEN (Marshall JVM410H)]{#BRIT_JVM_OD1_GREEN_.28Marshall_JVM410H.29 .mw-headline}

[![Jvm.png](/wiki/images/thumb/9/98/Jvm.png/300px-Jvm.png){decoding="async"
width="300" height="116"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/9/98/Jvm.png/450px-Jvm.png 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/9/98/Jvm.png/600px-Jvm.png 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Jvm.png){.image}

Models:

- OD1 Green
- OD1 Orange
- OD1 Red
- OD2 Green
- OD2 Orange
- OD2 Red

Cab:

- original: Marshall 4x12 G12T75
  [\[122\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/santiago-alvarez-electronics-engineer-jvm-yjm-afd.477/page-22#post-349437){.external
  .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
- matching DynaCab: 4x12 1960TV

Master, Bass, Middle, Treble, Gain, Presence, Resonance/Depth, Reverb
effect (not modeled)

Power tubes: EL34

1.  \"IMO, the reason the JVM sounds good is the plate cap on the
    second-to-last triode. That smooths out the tone considerably. The
    second-to-last triode is associated with \"Triode 1 Freq\" in the
    advanced parameters. You can adjust this to simulate adding a cap to
    the plate. The other thing that helps the tone is the 220K plate
    resistor on the last triode. This shifts the bias point down vs. a
    \"classic\" Marshall. Unfortunately the bias points aren\'t exposed
    to the user.\"
    [\[123\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/holy-crap-the-new-jvm-sounds-great.44628/#post-588030){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The JVM has a huge plate resistor on the cathode follower, the JS
    does not.\"
    [\[124\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/jvm-sounding-weird.150157/page-2#post-1785256){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  (about OD 1 Orange and Red compression):
    - \"Real amp does this. Poor cathode follower design.\"
    - (why doesn\'t this happen with the Green channel) \"Because the
      Green channel only has one tone stack hanging off the cathode
      follower.\"
    - (why doesn\'t this happen with the OD2 channels) \"OD1 has a
      different tone stack. The gains are the same. The models are very
      accurate.\"
      [\[125\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/jvm-410-model-issue.156087){.external
      .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"With an amp like the JVM it\'s very easy to saturate the virtual
    power amp. The real amp has two masters, a channel master and a
    global master. So the level in to the power amp is the product of
    those two masters. The model only has one so if you set the MV the
    same as the channel master and the global master isn\'t at 10 then
    you\'ll be overdriving the model\'s power amp much more than the
    amp. Just lowering the MV a touch will make the amp brighter for a
    given Presence value.\"
    [\[126\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/5150-presence-knob.199908/page-6#post-2492390){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"Our reference amp has 47K resistors in series with the treble pot.
    These resistors reduce the maximum treble. The schematic does not
    show these. However, the JVM410HJS (Satriani model) schematic shows
    these and the JS version does have these. My guess is that Marshall
    started using the same control board for both versions at some point
    to simplify things, reduce inventory, etc. (..) The JVM410 is also
    problematic because the internal layout is poor. The output
    transformer is on the wrong side of the chassis and causes the
    output to couple into the input. There\'s a shield in there but
    there\'s still a ton of crosstalk. The net effect is that it causes
    resonances that are dependent upon the Master Volume. You can test
    this yourself. Hook the amp to a load-box. Listen to the output at
    the FX Send (or Preamp Out). Turn the MV up and down and the tone
    will change dramatically.\"
    [\[127\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/marshall-jvm410hjs-real-amp-versus-axe3.197259/page-5#post-2669930){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"Our reference amp is a a late-model production amp that has never
    been modded.\"
    [\[128\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/marshall-jvm410hjs-real-amp-versus-axe3.197259/page-5#post-2669952){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  "The JVM is a cool amp but cleans are not its strength. There are
    many clean models that can give you something better."
    [\[129\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/jvm410h-clean.213321/#post-2673993){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
