## []{#BRIT_PRE_(Marshall_JMP-1_preamp)}[BRIT PRE (Marshall JMP-1 preamp)]{#BRIT_PRE_.28Marshall_JMP-1_preamp.29 .mw-headline}

[![Cliff
JMP-1.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/2/27/Cliff_JMP-1.jpg/300px-Cliff_JMP-1.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="90"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/2/27/Cliff_JMP-1.jpg/450px-Cliff_JMP-1.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/2/27/Cliff_JMP-1.jpg/600px-Cliff_JMP-1.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Cliff_JMP-1.jpg){.image}

OD channel model

This model is not available on the AM4, because it has been superseded
by the later JMPRE-1 models.

Volume, Gain, Bass, Mid, Treble, Presence, Bass Shift (not modeled)

Power tubes: EL34

1.  \"The two channels have preset tone stacks. Then there is a
    digitally controlled 4-band graphic EQ which is the B/M/T and
    Presence. This technique gets around the problem of trying to
    digitally control a tone stack. The Triaxis uses LDRs in place of
    potentiometers. The Soldano X-99 uses motorized pots. Both
    techniques being expensive. So the JMP-1 uses a fixed tone stack and
    then a digitally controlled graphic EQ. The Axe-Fx model of the
    JMP-1 is \"better\" in the sense that the tone controls control the
    tone stack rather than a graphic EQ. You then have the separate
    graphic EQ to further tailor the sound. What I didn\'t do, and why
    people probably feel the model differs, is \"normalize\" the tone
    controls so that with B/M/T at noon the tone stacks match. On the
    Axe-Fx you might need to set the Bass to 3, Mid to 7, etc. to get
    the tone to match. I just used a standard Marshall tone stack
    whereas the JMP-1 uses a standard Marshall tone stack but the pots
    are replaced with fixed resistors but those values don\'t
    necessarily correspond to the pots at noon.\"
    [\[130\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1228348){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The JMP-1 tone controls have more range than the actual preamp.
    The preamp has about +/- 8 dB for each tone control while the model
    has the standard +/- 12 dB.\"
3.  \"Brit Pre is a legacy model from the original Axe-Fx. It\'s not as
    accurate but some people really liked it so we kept it and created
    new models for the Ares/Cygnus platform.\"
    [\[131\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-release-version-19-02-public-beta.181521/post-2224791){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#BRIT_SILVER_(Marshall_Silver_Jubilee,_previously:_Lerxst_Omega)}[BRIT SILVER (Marshall Silver Jubilee, previously: Lerxst Omega)]{#BRIT_SILVER_.28Marshall_Silver_Jubilee.2C_previously:_Lerxst_Omega.29 .mw-headline}

[![Silver
Jubilee.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/9/98/Silver_Jubilee.jpg/300px-Silver_Jubilee.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="139"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/9/98/Silver_Jubilee.jpg/450px-Silver_Jubilee.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/9/98/Silver_Jubilee.jpg/600px-Silver_Jubilee.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Silver_Jubilee.jpg){.image}

Lead channel with Gain pushed in

Cab:

- original: Marshall 4x12 (V30)
- matching DynaCab: 4x12 Lerxst

Presence, Bass, Middle, Treble, Gain, Master

Power tubes: EL34

1.  (before 24.03) \"Our reference amp for the Silver Jubilee is
    actually not a Silver Jubilee. It\'s a Lerxst Omega that Alex
    Lifeson gave me.\"
    [\[132\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-5-cygnus-firmware-public-beta-2.170901/post-2058221){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The model is now based on a Silver Jubilee. The Lerxst is actually
    almost identical except for the taper of the mid control. In a
    Silver Jubilee the mid pot is log, in the Lerxst it\'s linear. Guess
    Alex likes mids\... So if you want the sound of the old model turn
    up the mids.\"
    [\[133\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-24-03-release.200627/post-2504840){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"It\'s the lead channel w/ the gain knob pushed in. The pull rhythm
    clip thing is this amp is an enigma. If implies that it\'s only
    active in the rhythm channel but it affects the lead channel too.\"
    [\[134\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-24-03-release.200627/post-2504798){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

Marshall AFD100 in AFD mode, based on schematics only

## []{#BUDDAH_DUOMASTER_(Budda_Twinmaster)}[BUDDAH DUOMASTER (Budda Twinmaster)]{#BUDDAH_DUOMASTER_.28Budda_Twinmaster.29 .mw-headline}

[![Budda
Twinmaster.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/3/39/Budda_Twinmaster.jpg/250px-Budda_Twinmaster.jpg){decoding="async"
width="250" height="202"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/3/39/Budda_Twinmaster.jpg/375px-Budda_Twinmaster.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/3/39/Budda_Twinmaster.jpg/500px-Budda_Twinmaster.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Budda_Twinmaster.jpg){.image}

Cab:

- original: 1x15 Budda Phat 15, 1x12 Budda Phat 12
- matching DynaCab: 2x12 Double Verb

Bass, Treble, Volume

Power tubes: EL84

1.  \"I bought a Budda Twinmaster, pulled it apart and traced the
    circuit since I couldn\'t find a schematic for it anywhere. Funky
    amp. Paraphase phase inverter. Weird Bridge-T sorta tone stack. I\'m
    convinced the feedback is connected to the wrong node but I
    quadruple-checked and my schematic is definitely correct. I think it
    was probably a mistake but then they said \"Hmmm, but it sounds good
    so don\'t fix it\".\"
    [\[136\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-12-cygnus-firmware-public-release-candidate.172027/post-2075782){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The Buttery model was REPLACED by a Budda Twinmaster model.
    Totally different model.\"
    [\[137\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-12-cygnus-firmware-public-release-candidate.172027/post-2076481){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#CA3+_CLEAN_(Custom_Audio_Amplifiers_3+_SE_preamp)}[CA3+ CLEAN (Custom Audio Amplifiers 3+ SE preamp)]{#CA3.2B_CLEAN_.28Custom_Audio_Amplifiers_3.2B_SE_preamp.29 .mw-headline}

[![CAE.png](/wiki/images/thumb/3/3e/CAE.png/300px-CAE.png){decoding="async"
width="300" height="81"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/3/3e/CAE.png/450px-CAE.png 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/3/3e/CAE.png/600px-CAE.png 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:CAE.png){.image}

Models:

- Clean channel
- Rhythm channel
- Lead channel

Matching DynaCab: 4x12 Friedman V30

Gain, Bass, Middle, Treble, Master, Bright switch. Active tube EQ:
Treble and Bass

Power tubes: EL34

1.  \"The CA3+SE model is basically an OD100.\"
    [\[138\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/is-the-suhr-od-100-in-the-axe.75090/#post-918169){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"An OD100 is the head version of a CAE 3+.\"
3.  \"That\'s a \"James\" tone-stack. You can find simulations on-line
    but typically you would get close using shelving filters with
    frequencies of 100 and 1000 Hz.\"
    [\[139\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/cae-3-se-global-eq-anybody-know-the-freqs.33103/#post-461976){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#CAMERON_CCV_1A_(Cameron_CCV-100)}[CAMERON CCV 1A (Cameron CCV-100)]{#CAMERON_CCV_1A_.28Cameron_CCV-100.29 .mw-headline}

[![Ccv.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/f/f7/Ccv.jpg/300px-Ccv.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="143"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/f/f7/Ccv.jpg/450px-Ccv.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/f/f7/Ccv.jpg/600px-Ccv.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Ccv.jpg){.image}

Models:

- (1A) Channel 1, less gain
- (1B) Channel 1, more gain
- (2A) Channel 2, Bright 1 switch left, Bright 2 switch left, Gain Style
  switch left
- (2B) Channel 2, Bright 1 switch left, Bright 2 switch right, Gain
  Style switch left
- (2C) Channel 2, Bright 1 switch left, Bright 2 switch left, Gain Style
  switch right
- (2D) Channel 2, Bright 1 switch left, Bright 2 switch right, Gain
  Style switch right
  [\[140\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/just-a-heads-up.97371/#post-1168902){.external
  .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

Matching DynaCab: 4x12 Friedman GB

Channel 1: Punch (= Resonance/Depth), Presence, Master, Bass, Middle,
Treble and Gain, 3-way Voicing switch (resonance), 3-way Dark switch
(presence), 3-way Gain Style switch ("Jose Master" gain/clipping), 3-way
Bright switch (less noticeable at higher gain settings)

Channel 2: Punch (= Resonance / Depth), Presence, Solo Master, Master,
Bass, Middle, Treble, two Gain controls, 3-way Gain Style switch, two
Bright switches, Drive switch

The 2C and 2D models have lower output because of the Sat switch
position.

Power tubes: EL34

1.  \"The amp was modeled with the Voicing switch in the middle
    position. The \"Dark\" switch is the Negative feedback control. Set
    Negative Feedback to 3.6 to reproduce the switch in the middle
    position. Set it to 9.8 to reproduce the switch in the right
    position. 5.0 for left position (default). The amp has a dozen
    switches and, frankly, there isn\'t a lot of difference between some
    of the settings. The Drive switch sounds virtually identical whether
    left or right. I don\'t like it in the middle.\"
    [\[141\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/just-a-heads-up.97371/#post-1168912){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  (Drive knob) \"Our reference amp has a linear taper pot so the
    behavior is very abrupt. The model matches the amp extremely
    accurately (as do all G3 models).\"
    [\[142\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/fw-18-01-camron-ccv-not-a-bug.97385/#post-1168811){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"It\'s a bit of a quirky amp and kind of a one-trick pony but, man,
    what a trick.\"
    [\[143\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/fw-18-01-camron-ccv-not-a-bug.97385/#post-1168922){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"Yes, it\'s actually not a very high gain amp. The topology is very
    similar to a JCM800.\"
    [\[144\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/fw-18-01-camron-ccv-not-a-bug.97385/#post-1169347){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"The key to the CCV sound is the Sat Switch.\"
    [\[145\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1169015){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"Camerons have linear taper MV and you need it with them because
    the signal level into the power amp is very low due to the Jose
    topology.\"
    [\[146\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/mv-poll.170996/post-2059425){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  \"Humans perceive high frequency thermal noise as hiss. The more
    gain the more hiss. Diezel\'s have a lot of filtering. Large grid
    stoppers, plate capacitors, etc. This reduces the bandwidth which
    lowers the hiss. Camerons are pretty much wide open. Small grid
    stoppers or bypass caps on the grid stoppers, no plate caps, etc.\"
    [\[147\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/why-lower-gain-cameron-ccv-amp-model-feels-more-noisy-than-much-higher-gain-herbie-3.188658/post-2339783){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
8.  \"The Cameron is a genuine Cameron. I don\'t know the lineage of the
    Atomica.\"
    [\[148\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/are-any-of-the-cameron-models-of-mark-cameron-built-amps.199792/#post-2489827){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
9.  \"I have an early Mark-built CCV. I\'m not sure about the provenance
    of the Atomica.\"
    [\[149\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/there-is-actually-a-jose-modded-marshall-in-the-fractal.7763/page-2#post-367370){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
10. \"The presence capacitor is very large compared to a typical Plexi.
    Therefore the presence control lets a lot more midrange through as
    you turn it up.\"
    [\[150\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/cameron-ccv.214447/#post-2691079){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#CAPT_HOOK_1A_(Hook_Captain_34)}[CAPT HOOK 1A (Hook Captain 34)]{#CAPT_HOOK_1A_.28Hook_Captain_34.29 .mw-headline}

[![Capt34.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/9/91/Capt34.jpg/300px-Capt34.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="122"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/9/91/Capt34.jpg/450px-Capt34.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/9/91/Capt34.jpg/600px-Capt34.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Capt34.jpg){.image}

Models:

- (1A) Channel 1, EQ Bypass off, Boost switch off
- (1B) Channel 1, EQ Bypass switch engaged (no Bass/Middle/Treble),
  Boost switch on
- (2A) Channel 2, Edge switch off
- (2B) Channel 2, Edge switch on
- (3A) Channel 3, Edge switch off
- (3B) Channel 3, Edge switch on

Cab:

- original: Hook 2x12 or 4x12 (V30, G12H, G12-65, WGS)
- matching DynaCab: 2x12 5153 Stealth

Channel 1: Gain (with Pull function), Level, Bass, Mid, Treble, Boost
switch (not modeled), EQ bypass switch, Bright switch. Shared: Presence
and Balls

Channels 2 and 3: Gain, Level, Bass, Mid, Treble, Boost switch, Edge
switch (changes tone stack). Shared: Presence and Balls

Power tubes: EL34

1.  \"This amp uses a mu follower which yields a complex distortion with
    smooth decay. To simulate the Boost switch use the Boost switch in
    the amp block as it has the same amount of gain.\"​
    [\[151\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1426113){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"A mu follower is similar to a cascode configuration except the
    output is off the cathode instead of the plate. So the output
    impedance is lower.\"
    [\[152\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/the-hook.120307/#post-1432379){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  (mimic Pull Gain on clean channel) \"Just set the Tonestack Type to
    Hook Clean 2.\"
    [\[153\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-ii-quantum-rev-5-00-firmware-released.120358/page-10#post-1433059){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"The Capt. Hook\'s \"thing\" is that it\'s basically a JCM800 with
    the cathode follower replaced by a mu-follower. A mu-follower
    doesn\'t compress and distort like a cathode follower does. This
    results in the amp sounding more open and smoother.\"
    [\[154\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/recommended-adjustment.133602/page-2#post-1579933){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"The Hook Clean 1 is a Fender style tonestack which has a lot more
    insertion loss than the others.\"
    [\[155\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-ii-quantum-rev-5-00-firmware-released.120358/page-10#post-1433058){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"The Hook uses a \"mu follower\" instead of a cathode follower.
    Cathode followers have low output impedance but distort quite
    easily. Mu followers address some of the problems of cathode
    followers.\"
    [\[156\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/dialling-in-the-marshalls.143682/page-7#post-1708218){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#CAR_AMBLER_(Carr_Rambler)}[CAR AMBLER (Carr Rambler)]{#CAR_AMBLER_.28Carr_Rambler.29 .mw-headline}

[![Rambler.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/6/6c/Rambler.jpg/300px-Rambler.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="297"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/6/6c/Rambler.jpg/450px-Rambler.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/6/6c/Rambler.jpg/600px-Rambler.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Rambler.jpg){.image}

Cab:

- original: Carr 1x12 (Eminence Elsinore)
- matching DynaCab: 1x12 Car Ambler

Volume, Treble, Middle, Bass, Pentode/Triode (not modeled), Reverb
effect (not modeled), Tremolo effect

Power tubes: 6L6

No negative feedback

1.  \"It\'s basically a Deluxe Reverb preamp with a cathode bias 6L6
    power amp and no negative feedback. Sort of a Fender-meets-Vox
    thing.\"
    [\[157\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/carr.78974/#post-960532){.external

## []{#CAROL-ANN_OD-2_(Carol-Ann_OD-2)}[CAROL-ANN OD-2 (Carol-Ann OD-2)]{#CAROL-ANN_OD-2_.28Carol-Ann_OD-2.29 .mw-headline}

[![Od2.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/9/98/Od2.jpg/300px-Od2.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="199"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/9/98/Od2.jpg/450px-Od2.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/9/98/Od2.jpg/600px-Od2.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Od2.jpg){.image}

Overdrive channel model

Cab:

- original: EV-12L, Classic Lead 80, Scholz
- matching DynaCab: 1x12 Scholz

Master, Pre Gain, Drive, Bass, Middle, Treble, Presence, Sparkle (not
modeled), Shift switch (not modeled)

Power tubes: 6L6

1.  \"CAs are definitely dark amps. Sound great though.\"
    [\[158\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-10-cygnus-firmware-public-beta-7.171198/post-2066490){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"If you like the base Dumble sound but want a little more gain
    without the fuzziness of a Fuchs try the Carol-Ann models.\"
    [\[159\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/fuchs-ods-in-cygnus.172291/post-2081523){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

Alan Phillips:

1.  \"In the real world the OD2 is very very fussy on speaker choice
    too. The real world speakers of choice are EVM12L in a 1x12 rear
    ported and 2x12 with Celestion Classic Lead 80\'s. I found the 12L
    emulation did a pretty good job. Some of the others sounded so
    artificial with that model. Like a Rockman. Coupled with the right
    cab the emulated model does a good job of representing the basic
    tonal signature of the amp\".
2.  \"It\'s not a competitive model, it\'s a live demo of an OD2 as
    tweaked by me. Damn sight better than sound clips for auditioning to
    guys that haven\'t got the ability to get to a Dealer. Clearly it
    doesn\'t give you the full experience of the full amp, but is a good
    tonal taster. I repaired a Soldano SLO for him one day and when he
    came over my house to pick it up we just decided it would be a good
    idea to put a CA model in there. Having the actual builder involved
    kind of closes the loop fully. I\'m happy to endorse that model
    because I put a lot of hours testing it and putting together a ton
    of technical information, fourier analysis graphs, frequency
    response graphs, schematics etc that would make validation of a
    mathematical model much easier. In reality even though the power amp
    and the preamp are modeled the pre-amp got the most effort. As I
    said in another thread, I tuned that by putting the axe in to the
    actual power amp of an OD2 and running that side by side with a full
    OD2. The final tweaks were made like that using parametric eq blocks
    that were hard coded in to the model. You could call that the icing
    on the cake and basically put the same level of tuning into the
    model as I do with a actual OD2. The only difference was I was using
    a GUI, not resistors and capacitors.\"
3.  \"The OD2 and to some degree the OD3 uses HRM style gain staging
    with a Plexi PI and power amp. Thats common knowledge, I\'ve talked
    about it in depth many times. I really liked the idea of driving the
    tonestack from a common cathode stage as opposed to a cathode
    follower like a Marshall because it got rid of some of the artifacts
    I don\'t like with say a JCM-800. Yes that\'s something that Dumble
    came up with that I have to give him major props for. I wanted an
    amp that would have a little more gain than a JCM-800 but with the
    character of a Plexi without any fizz or harsh upper mid/lower
    treble frequencies. Remember this was BEFORE anyone had even
    degooped or documented a Bluesmaster style circuit and the only
    thing Shad was building was his post count at AmpGarage asking about
    Dumble circuits. I do find it amazing it took other guys years to
    catch on with moving the pots to the front. It does require a bit
    more thought than just moving the pots as the ranges of those
    trimmers Dumble used is impractical when used as front panel
    controls (which they were not really intended to be). I do also
    agree with you that from a pure tone standpoint having nothing on
    the front panel is always going to be better. The JB100 model is
    basically an OD2 with the entire OD circuit on the board with
    predefined filters made up of quality components without adjustment
    through fragile trimmers. The OD2 was never designed to be put side
    by side in a Dumble clone fest in some guys living room with
    everyone playing their best Ford licks, it was designed to be used
    on stage for guys who played in cover/blues/wedding/classic rock
    bands. The seperate eq and the tube driven effects loop were added
    for that situation. I have always tried to avoid that association as
    much as possible because the average Dumble lover is typically
    looking for a particular set of tones that may or may not be found
    in this amp. Early customer interaction with guys like yourself made
    me want to make sure people knew it was not a tonal clone of a
    Dumble to avoid returns/misunderstandings. The OD-2 is not the best
    amp for those tones, I totally agree with you, but a Dumble or clone
    doesn\'t really do fast dampened power chords like the OD-2 will do
    either. On the other hand, it is much more suited for blues and
    classic rock, not the Ford/Carlton thing. Bear in mind that its
    function and tone that the average player is looking for, not a
    particular design architecture. The fact I did use an HRM style
    circuit obviously (and unfortunately) placed me in the Dumble
    category. However, 2500 amps later its not really seen that way any
    more as the CA\'s have always had their own thing going on tonally
    that is very much more in a modified Marshall vein. The newer models
    like the Triptik 2 have absolutely nothing in common with any
    Dumble, not even a common cathode driven tonestack. For anyone that
    has played a number of real Dumbles, there is a certain thing (I
    hear it more in the clean channel) that is uniquely his signature.
    There\'s a certain swirl to the clean tone that is always present in
    his amps. However the amp doesn\'t overdrive anywhere close to like
    what I like when pushed hard. For me I would rather focus on that
    tone in a Plexi Marshall, but who knows what the original guy he
    modified this for wanted. All of this hopefully explains why I have
    always shied away from the Dumble comparison thing, I was truly and
    honestly never trying to clone a Dumble.\"
    [\[160\]](https://www.thegearpage.net/board/index.php?threads/fuchs-ods-classic-whats-the-word.1845787/page-4#post-24506473){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#CAROL-ANN_TRIPTIK_CLASSIC_(Carol-Ann_Triptik)}[CAROL-ANN TRIPTIK CLASSIC (Carol-Ann Triptik)]{#CAROL-ANN_TRIPTIK_CLASSIC_.28Carol-Ann_Triptik.29 .mw-headline}

[![Triptik.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/6/69/Triptik.jpg/350px-Triptik.jpg){decoding="async"
width="350" height="210"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/6/69/Triptik.jpg/525px-Triptik.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/6/69/Triptik.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Triptik.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Clean channel
- Classic channel
- Modern channel

Cab:

- original: Carol-Ann 1x12 (Scholz Classic)
- matching DynaCab: 1x12 Scholz

Input Level, Drive on channels 2 and 3, Bass, Middle, Treble, Presence,
Master, Classic/Modern voice switch

Power tubes: EL34

1.  \"This TripTik is badass. Dumble meets Marshall with a sprinkle of
    5150 power amp.\"
    [\[161\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/since-10-06-came-out.70996/#post-870346){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"I think what people like about this amp is the same reason people
    like the BE/HBE. These amps share the same aggressive low-cut on the
    input and then add bass back in the power amp. This gives clear bass
    response without getting flubby.\"
3.  (speaker) \"It\'s a Scholz Classic.\"
    [\[162\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-ii-firmware-15-00-released.87350/page-7#post-1057172){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"Some amps have a fixed depth circuit, e.g. 5153, Freidman BE/HBE,
    Dirty Shirley, TripTik, Tucana, et. al. In these cases the Depth
    knob will default to a value that corresponds to the fixed
    circuit.\"
    [\[163\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/lets-talk-about-the-depth-control.88747/#post-1071598){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"CAs are definitely dark amps. Sound great though.\"
    [\[164\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-10-cygnus-firmware-public-beta-7.171198/post-2066490){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"If you like the base Dumble sound but want a little more gain
    without the fuzziness of a Fuchs try the Carol-Ann models.\"
    [\[165\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/fuchs-ods-in-cygnus.172291/post-2081523){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

Alan Phillips from Carol-Ann:

1.  (Classic mode): \"On the real amp, you would set the Input level at
    2 O\'clock and the Gain at 1 to 2 O\'clock to get a great classic
    rock rhythm tone. It\'s not overly different in character to the
    modern setting, less gain and less low end essentially.\"
2.  \"It does classic rock extremely well and has one of the best clean
    channels I\'ve ever designed.\"
    [\[166\]](https://www.thegearpage.net/board/index.php?threads/carol-ann-od2r-the-best.1908068/#post-25776544){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#CAROL-ANN_TUCANA_CLEAN_(Carol-Ann_Tucana_3)}[CAROL-ANN TUCANA CLEAN (Carol-Ann Tucana 3)]{#CAROL-ANN_TUCANA_CLEAN_.28Carol-Ann_Tucana_3.29 .mw-headline}

[![Tucana.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/f/f3/Tucana.jpg/300px-Tucana.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="187"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/f/f3/Tucana.jpg/450px-Tucana.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/f/f3/Tucana.jpg/600px-Tucana.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Tucana.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Clean channel
- Lead channel

Cab:

- original: G12M, Classic Lead 80, Scholz
- matching DynaCab: 1x12 Scholz

Input Level, Bass, Mid, Treble, Gain (Overdrive channels), Master (all
channels), Presence

Power tubes: KT88

1.  \"One of the best amps in the world IMO. I have a Dumble and a
    Trainwreck and various other boutique amps and the Tucana is better
    than all of them.\"
    [\[167\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1153214){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"Some amps have a fixed depth circuit, e.g. 5153, Freidman BE/HBE,
    Dirty Shirley, TripTik, Tucana, et. al. In these cases the Depth
    knob will default to a value that corresponds to the fixed
    circuit.\"
    [\[168\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/lets-talk-about-the-depth-control.88747/#post-1071598){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"CAs are definitely dark amps. Sound great though.\"
    [\[169\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-10-cygnus-firmware-public-beta-7.171198/post-2066490){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"If you like the base Dumble sound but want a little more gain
    without the fuzziness of a Fuchs try the Carol-Ann models.\"
    [\[170\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/fuchs-ods-in-cygnus.172291/post-2081523){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

Carol-Ann:

1.  \"Now I can only speak for the actual amp, but my preference of
    speaker is a Celestion Creamback 65, though I gig these regularly
    with a 2x12 with Celestion T75\'s. Its pretty forgiving on speakers
    compared with some models. The foot controller and bias monitor are
    two of the wonderful features of the actual amp, but are both moot
    in the model\...\...unless Cliff wants to model the effects of real
    world mains power fluctuations from place to place, but the \'green
    zone\' of the bias monitor is 62-65% plate idle dissipation power
    and it measures and compensates for plate voltage and screen power ,
    which means the real amp runs best at a slightly cooler bias. The
    bias monitor just allows you to set that consistently from venue to
    venue regardless of the main power.\"
    [\[171\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1035178){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"It\'s very very difficult for anyone to get a bad tone out of the
    real amp. It\'s designed that way, the range and limits on the
    controls, even the biasmon system makes it difficult for even a very
    inexperienced player to FU. The real amp has a more British overtone
    to it due to the fact I am British and I designed it. The gain
    staging, overdrive voicing and output stage are night and day to
    ANYTHING Mesa, any owner of the real amp would attest to that.\"
    [\[172\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1049358){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The Tuc 3 is very very tolerant of most cabs and speakers, unlike
    say the OD2. I feel people need to approach this model very simply.
    Don\'t mess with extended parameters, basically don\'t try and
    redesign it. Use a reliable Celestion based cabinet model. I have a
    fantastic 4x12 with 2 old greenbacks and two old v30s that is the
    best cab I\'ve played the real amp through. In actual levels of gain
    with the two adjustable gain controls, the amp has a maximum gain
    level very similar to the Triptik, the setting of these two controls
    with respect to each other is critical.\"
    [\[173\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1049367){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"Real world, it has the same amount of actual gain as the Triptik.
    Way more than most people would need for recording or live playing.
    Input gain on 10 o clock, gain on 2 o clock is a 70s /80s lead tone,
    put the input level up to 2 o click and it\'s a very sustained lead
    tone or a very modern heavy rhythm tone.\"
    [\[174\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1049530){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"You don\'t need to crank the real amp to get a ton of overdrive. I
    actually designed the original for myself and I play in a rock cover
    band. There\'s nowhere I would ever be able to get the amp to the
    point of pushing the power tubes in to overdrive. You gain stage a
    design based on its application. For a design that needs a lot of
    overdrive at a low volume, you do most of that and the harmonic
    makeup in the preamp. The Tucana falls in to this category. The
    master volumes in a 500 seat club rarely get above 10 O Clock on the
    real amp and at that point there\'s still tons of clean headroom
    left. Of course the power amp adds to the harmonic content, but it
    adds very little overdrive. Another interesting point to note is
    that the Tucana has a high pass filter in the power amp feedback
    loop, which gives you a nice tight low end because the bass is
    subjected to more gain. For an amp designed to be pushed hard in to
    power tube overdrive, this should be omitted as all bets are off in
    the feedback loop when you hit the rails. In other words that filter
    requires headroom to function properly, as does the presence control
    of any amp where it\'s a component of the feedback loop.\"
    [\[175\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1050147){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#CLASS-A_30W_(Vox_AC30)}[CLASS-A 30W (Vox AC30)]{#CLASS-A_30W_.28Vox_AC30.29 .mw-headline}

[![Ac30.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/e/ee/Ac30.jpg/300px-Ac30.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="120"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/e/ee/Ac30.jpg/450px-Ac30.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/e/ee/Ac30.jpg/600px-Ac30.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Ac30.jpg){.image}

Models:

- AC-30: Normal channel of AC30HW head, Bright switch disabled
- AC-30 Bright: possibly a model of the Bright channel of an older Vox
  AC-30
- AC-30 Brilliant: [according to this
  thread:](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/it’s-2026-what-is-the-ac30-brilliant.219596/post-2766579){.external
  .text target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"} same as TB,
  with a different tonestack (Matchbox D-30)
- AC-30 Hot: Top Boost channel of AC30HW head in \"Hot\" mode (no tone
  stack)
- AC-30 TB: Top Boost channel of AC30HW head in \"Cool\" mode (regular,
  with tone stack)

\
[![AC30HW
controls.png](/wiki/images/thumb/7/74/AC30HW_controls.png/800px-AC30HW_controls.png){decoding="async"
width="800" height="102"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/7/74/AC30HW_controls.png/1200px-AC30HW_controls.png 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/7/74/AC30HW_controls.png/1600px-AC30HW_controls.png 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:AC30HW_controls.png){.image}

Cab:

- original: Vox 2x12 (Alnico, G12M)
- matching DynaCab: 2x12 Class-A 30W

Volume, Bright switch (Normal channel), Treble, Bass (Top Boost
channel), Hot/Cool switch (Top Boost channel), Tone Cut, Master (Hot
model only)

Power tubes: EL84

No negative feedback

1.  \"An AC30 has no power amp feedback so it doesn\'t have presence or
    depth controls. It has a \"Cut\" control which is basically an
    adjustable snubber on the phase inverter.\"
    [\[181\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/7-18-firmware-need-help-witch-ac30-and-cabs-block-settingd.19793/post-338285){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"Note that the particular AC-30 used for the model has this
    scratchy high end. (\...) It\'s a hand-wired version and that can
    lead to this type of sound as the parasitics cause boosting of the
    very high frequencies when the amp is driven hard.\"
    [\[182\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/970333){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The bright cap value is normalized to a Drive pot of 1M. An AC30
    has a 500K pot so the value will read out as half the actual value.
    IOW, it\'s displaying 60 pF which is equivalent to 120 pF.\"
    [\[183\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1064264){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"The Hot model models the AC-30HW model set to Hot. This bypasses
    the EQ for more gain. For authenticity, leave all tone controls at
    noon.\"
5.  \"AC30\'s have no negative feedback on the power amp. This means the
    output voltage follows the speaker impedance. Therefore you get a
    boost at the low frequency resonance of the speaker which causes the
    low end to get loose when you crank it.\"
    [\[184\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/crunchy-ac-30-tb-need-some-help-tightening-up-the-low-end.117675/#post-1404022){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"AC-30\'s have a poorly designed cathode follower. The bias point
    is totally wrong and crushes one side of the signal considerably.
    IMO either the cathode resistor should be 100K or the plate resistor
    of the preceding stage should be higher, 200K. The clipping is
    extremely asymmetric. Too much IMO. A little asymmetry is good
    because it warms things up. Too much causes excessive even-order
    harmonics which makes things fuzzy and indistinct. The clipping is
    so asymmetric on an AC-30 that it\'s almost a half-wave rectifier.
    You can tweak this by adjusting the Preamp Bias point and/or
    lowering the Cathode Follower Compression. Or you can lower the
    Harmonics value which reduces the asymmetric distortion. The
    downside of that is that it then overdrives the phase inverter
    causing blocking distortion from excessive bias excursion. Another
    thing to try is to increase the Grid Clipping value which will add a
    little headroom. Start with the Bias point. AC-30\'s are very
    sensitive to the tube type and part tolerances. A tiny change in the
    bias point can make a big difference. The default bias point is
    based on Mullard ECC83 tubes. I prefer the AC-20 because it doesn\'t
    have a cathode follower so doesn\'t suffer from these problems. The
    cathode follower in an AC-30 doesn\'t even do all that much.
    Normally you use a cathode follower to preset a low-impedance source
    to the tone stack but the tone stack in an AC-30 doesn\'t present
    that great of a load anyways.\"
    [\[185\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-version-5-02.148983/page-11#post-1767187){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  \"The reference AC30 is an AC30HWHD.\"
    [\[186\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-version-5-07.150305/page-6#post-1788283){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
8.  \"Our Vox models are based on a fairly new AC30HWHD head. The model
    matches that particular amp very well. Will it match an AC30 from a
    different era exactly? Probably not.\"
    [\[187\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/how-accurate-is-fractals-amp-modeling.168786/post-2027668){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
9.  \"The normal channel on a Vox would be closest to the Morgan. The
    Brilliant channel is a \"Top Boost\" which means it has a tone stack
    and a significant midrange cut. The normal channel has no tone
    stack. You can\'t compare a a Morgan AC20 to the Brilliant channel
    of an AC30 and declare that one sounds better than the other.
    Totally different preamps and, therefore, different sound.
    Personally I think the AC20 is a better amp. Better made, better
    quality components, much better transformers. If you want that
    chimey AC30 sound you put an EQ before it and suck out some mids.\"
    [\[188\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/how-accurate-is-fractals-amp-modeling.168786/post-2064189){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
10. \"So-called Class-A amps (like the AC30) don\'t actually exhibit
    much power supply sag because, well, they\'re Class-A (or nearly).
    The tubes are biased hot so when one tube is conducting more the
    other is conducting less and the net supply current doesn\'t change
    much. Contrast this with Class-AB where when one tube conducts the
    other goes into cutoff causing a net increase in supply current and
    concomitant supply sag. What Class-A amps do exhibit is \"cathode
    squish\". The capacitor on the cathodes charges up and shifts the
    bias point. This reduces the gain and acts as a sort of compressor.
    It\'s a unique compression and the amp \"opens up\" at the same time
    and crossover distortion increases.\"
    [\[189\]](https://www.thegearpage.net/board/index.php?threads/does-this-sound-like-an-ac30-to-you.2325505/post-34009664){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
11. \"An AC-30 has no negative feedback which is why it sounds the way
    it does.\"
    [\[190\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/help-me-dial-in-the-ac30.192021/post-2387421){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
12. \"In a tube power amp the lows and highs distort first because they
    are boosted by the speaker impedance. This causes the sound to
    become more midrangey and focused. Then as the signal decays the
    sound becomes fuller and less midrangey. It\'s literally one of the
    most important things in the way a tube amp operates and is
    responsible for its unique and pleasing overdrive behavior and why
    they became the gold-standard. This is also what makes an AC30 so
    unique. AC30s have no negative feedback so the lows and highs are
    fully boosted by the speaker impedance. When you drive them hard
    they get focused. When you back off the volume the become full and
    chimey.\"
    [\[191\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/fender-tone-master-pro.3286/page-184#post-145948){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#DELUXE_6G3_(brownface_Fender_Deluxe,_6G3)}[DELUXE 6G3 (brownface Fender Deluxe, 6G3)]{#DELUXE_6G3_.28brownface_Fender_Deluxe.2C_6G3.29 .mw-headline}

Bright channel model

Matching DynaCab: 1x12 Deluxe Verb

Volume, Tone

Power tubes: 6V6

Info to be added

[GuitarPlayer
article](https://www.guitarplayer.com/gear/the-1962-fender-6g3-deluxe-could-be-all-the-amp-you-ever-need){.external
.text target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

[https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dpZ-r3eSVjE](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dpZ-r3eSVjE){.external
.free target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

[https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MlsY1XeFF4w](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MlsY1XeFF4w){.external
.free target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

[https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-pgamUAnpAo](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-pgamUAnpAo){.external
.free target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

[https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=fchEx9mM6qI](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=fchEx9mM6qI){.external
.free target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

1.  The Fat switch controls the value of a capacitor in the tone stack.
    The 6G3 does not have a tone stack so the switch is not applicable.
    The Bright switch and Bright cap control the value of a capacitor
    across the Drive pot. The 6G3 does not have a conventional drive
    circuit so these are not applicable.
    [\[194\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-31-01-beta.217019/page-11#post-2735374){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#DELUXE_TWEED_BRIGHT_(1957_narrow-panel_Fender_Tweed_Deluxe,_5E3)}[DELUXE TWEED BRIGHT (1957 narrow-panel Fender Tweed Deluxe, 5E3)]{#DELUXE_TWEED_BRIGHT_.281957_narrow-panel_Fender_Tweed_Deluxe.2C_5E3.29 .mw-headline}

[![Deluxe.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/3/3d/Deluxe.jpg/300px-Deluxe.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="285"
srcset="/wiki/images/3/3d/Deluxe.jpg 1.5x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Deluxe.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Bright input
- Normal input
- Jumpered inputs

Cab:

- original: Fender 1x12 (Jensen P12R or C12N, or Celestion Alnico Blue)
- matching DynaCab: 1x12 Deluxe Tweed

Volume Normal, Volume Bright, Tone

Power tubes: 6V6

No negative feedback

1.  \"Based on a Fender 5E3 Deluxe. Note that this amp only has a single
    tone control. This is modeled by the Treble control in the
    Axe-Fx II. The Bass and Mid controls are functional and recreate the
    amp when set to noon. Also note that this amp suffers from extreme
    blocking distortion at or near maximum gain. This is common in very
    old designs. As it is virtually unplayable like this, the model uses
    a somewhat reduced level of grid conduction to lower the amount of
    blocking distortion and make the amp more playable at high Drive
    settings.\"
2.  \"The G3 version of the 5E3 Deluxe Tweed model is a hoot. Totally
    unpredictable, nasty, gnarly and raunchy. I couldn\'t stop playing
    it yesterday. Just like the real amp you have to be careful with
    your volume control and how you approach the amp so that you keep it
    right on the edge of playability. So cool.\"
    [\[195\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1144722){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The Deluxe Tweed amp model is a 5E3. The 1x12 Deluxe Tweed Mix cab
    is the IR.\"
    [\[196\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/59-deluxe.106336/page-2#post-1272464){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"Yup, that\'s the key. Crank the treble almost all the way up.\"
    [\[197\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/59-deluxe.106336/page-3#post-1273603){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"The actual amp has no grid stopper resistor on the second stage
    and therefore has LOTS of blocking distortion.\"
    [\[198\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-version-5-00-beta-3.148907/page-3#post-1764588){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"IMO the designs are poor because\... wait for it\... they exhibit
    a papery buzz. The problem with most cathode biased Class A amps is,
    1: they aren\'t really Class A (more like hot Class AB) and 2: They
    go into Class B operation when they are overdriven. The cathode
    capacitor charges up and the bias point shifts dramatically. This
    causes lots of crossover distortion (papery buzz). It\'s worse on
    lower notes because lower notes have more energy and charge the cap
    more. The is probably the reason Leo Fender switched to fixed bias
    amps with negative feedback. Fixed bias is just that, the bias point
    is fixed so the amp doesn\'t shift into Class B operation when
    overdriven (not as much anyways, depends on the bias circuit, grid
    stoppers, etc.). Negative feedback linearizes the amp and reduces
    the crossover distortion (at the expense of gain). That\'s why the
    buzzing went away when you increased negative feedback. Crossover
    distortion is a unique sound. For cleaner sounds it tends to be
    objectionable. For overdriven sounds some find it desirable. EVH
    ostensibly liked his amps biased cold to get some crossover
    distortion. There are even some amps that have circuits to
    intentionally generate crossover distortion. Some distortion pedals
    also do this. Lowering the Cathode Resistance reduces the crossover
    distortion as it keeps the amp in Class A operation longer but the
    tubes run hotter and don\'t last as long. This is not a problem with
    our virtual amps though. I forget the actual values but I\'m pretty
    certain if you look at the Cathode Resistance value for those amps
    it\'s pretty high. This means the amps are biased somewhat cold to
    begin with and shift to very cold as soon as overdriven.\"
    [\[199\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/papery-buzz-under-some-models.149193/page-2#post-1772639){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  (fuzzy lows) \"That\'s what those amps do. Always been that way.
    Just to be sure I just compared the Deluxe Verb model with the
    reference amp and it\'s correct. Those are old designs. Simple
    circuits with minimal frequency shaping. As such there\'s a lot of
    bass going into the power amp. That coupled with the resonance
    magnification of the speaker impedance causes frequencies around the
    resonance (in the 50-100 Hz region) to distort early. The low E
    string is 82 Hz so it\'s right in that zone.\"
    [\[200\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-10-00-public-beta-2.154782/post-1842156){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
8.  \"When you dime the controls and whack a big chord the sound \"goes
    away\" a bit just like the real amp and then comes back a bit
    later.\"
    [\[201\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/you-guys-gals-are-in-for-another-treat.169535/post-2042185){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
9.  \"The 5E3 model is now \"jumped\" so it has both Normal and Bright
    drives. You can get all sorts of different distortion textures by
    playing with the two drives in conjunction with the tone control. As
    with the real amp everything now interacts. One of the beta testers
    was remarking that his 5E3 clone sounded more \"choked\" in
    comparison to the model. I said \"I bet your clone has the wrong
    type of tube in V1. It\'s supposed to be a 12AY7 but many clones
    have a 12AX7A in V1.\" He checked and, sure enough, 12AX7A in V1.\"
    [\[202\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/cygnus-beta-first-impressions.169942/post-2045461){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
10. \"I\'ve added a non-jumped version of the 5E3 with both volume
    knobs. Now we can wait for the inevitable \"When I turn the Bright
    Drive all the way down the Normal Drive doesn\'t do anything\"
    comments.\"
    [\[203\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-4-cygnus-firmware-public-beta.170253/post-2051108){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
11. \"Amp doesn\'t have a bright cap.\"
    [\[204\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/deluxe-tweed-bright-switch.173082/post-2094005){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
12. \"Some of the undesirable characteristics are what makes a
    particular amp unique. For example a Deluxe 5E3 is characterized by
    significant blocking distortion. Without that it doesn\'t sound like
    a Deluxe and you can\'t do the Neil Young thing.\"
    [\[205\]](https://www.thegearpage.net/board/index.php?threads/is-digital-getting-too-real.2275913/post-32977457){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
13. \" If you plug into a real Deluxe the \"unused\" control effects the
    sound.\"
    [\[206\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-release-version-17-00.177099/post-2159734){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
14. \"I finished the 57 Tweed Deluxe today and it\'s glorious. Clean to
    \"Cinammon Girl\" with the volume knob. I never appreciated that amp
    until I spent some serious time with it.\"
    [\[207\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/you-guys-gals-are-in-for-another-treat.169535/post-2042068){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
15. \"The Bassman and Deluxe Tweed models are both modeled using a 12AY7
    as the input buffer. The Preamp Tube Type parameter only affects the
    tubes after the input buffer.\"
    [\[208\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/12ay7-preamp-tube-for-tweed-deluxe-and-bassman-models.175834/post-2135435){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
16. \"The model is based on plugging into the Bright input. The Normal
    input gain control affects the Bright input and the effect is most
    noticeable as turn it up towards 10.\"
    [\[209\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-29-01-public-beta-2-beta-4.214999/page-7#post-2700639){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#DELUXE_VERB_NORMAL_(1965_blackface_Fender_Deluxe_Reverb,_AB763)}[DELUXE VERB NORMAL (1965 blackface Fender Deluxe Reverb, AB763)]{#DELUXE_VERB_NORMAL_.281965_blackface_Fender_Deluxe_Reverb.2C_AB763.29 .mw-headline}

[![Deluxereverb.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/f/f7/Deluxereverb.jpg/300px-Deluxereverb.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="192"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/f/f7/Deluxereverb.jpg/450px-Deluxereverb.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/f/f7/Deluxereverb.jpg/600px-Deluxereverb.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Deluxereverb.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Normal channel
- Vibrato channel

Cab:

- original: Fender 1x12 with a Jensen C12(K), EVM 12L, or JBL D120. Or
  Fender 2x10 with Jensen C10N or C10Q, or a Jensen 25W Alnico P10R
- matching DynaCab: 1x12 Deluxe Verb

Volume, Bass, Treble, Reverb effect, Vibrato effect (not modeled)

Power tubes: 6V6

1.  \"A DR is numbered 1-10 so 3 on a DR is around 2.2 on the Axe-Fx.
    The model is based on the Vibrato input #1 which has more gain than
    the normal input. To simulate plugging into the #2 jack (which has
    half the gain) set Input Trim to 0.5.\"
    [\[210\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1260148){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"We got our reference Deluxe Reverb out of storage today, hooked it
    up and measured and compared. Gain measures spot-on and A/B testing
    sounds identical. With a Suhr Modern guitar with stock pickups both
    the amp and the model were starting to break up around 3 (which
    equals 2.2 on the Axe-Fx since the knobs start at zero not one). A
    Deluxe Reverb breaks up easily since it has 6V6 power tubes. The
    preamp is virtually identical to a Twin Reverb but 6V6s break up
    earlier than 6L6s. For a given voltage into the power amp a 6V6 has
    about 70% of the headroom compared to a 6L6.\"
    [\[211\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1262483){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The values for the Deluxe Reverb model are based on measurements
    of an actual 65 Deluxe Reverb, not some hypothetical values on some
    spec sheet.\"
    [\[212\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/speaker-page-does-any-of-this-make-sense.110373/#post-1322466){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  (fuzzy lows) \"That\'s what those amps do. Always been that way.
    Just to be sure I just compared the Deluxe Verb model with the
    reference amp and it\'s correct. Those are old designs. Simple
    circuits with minimal frequency shaping. As such there\'s a lot of
    bass going into the power amp. That coupled with the resonance
    magnification of the speaker impedance causes frequencies around the
    resonance (in the 50-100 Hz region) to distort early. The low E
    string is 82 Hz so it\'s right in that zone.\"
    [\[213\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-10-00-public-beta-2.154782/post-1842156){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"We have two Deluxe Reverbs, a vintage 1965 Deluxe Reverb that the
    model is based on and a Reissue. The vintage one sounds great, the
    reissue doesn\'t quite sound as good. It\'s biased too cold. The
    comparison was between the model and the Reissue because the vintage
    amp is worth a small fortune and I only use that when actually
    working on models. It stays in climate controlled storage
    otherwise.\"
    [\[214\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-10-00-public-beta-2.154782/post-1842188){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"Reissue: the preamp tubes that ship in those are junk (Groove
    Tubes). The way I model an amp is to start out theoretically based
    on the schematic. It\'s usually pretty accurate. On our Deluxe
    Reverb model the real amp had much less gain than predicted. I was
    racking my brain trying to figure it out. Finally I decided to
    replace all those Groove Tubes with a different brand and, voila\'.
    the amp now had the same gain as predicted.\"
    [\[215\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/leons-new-video-comparing-2203-in-different-modelers.3866/page-5#post-148603){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  \"The DR is my go-to clean-to-edge-of-breakup amp and I just
    verified the model against it a few days ago. It\'s extremely
    accurate.\"
    [\[216\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/fractal-audio-firmware-update-thread.673/page-117#post-152618){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
8.  \"The amp\'s measured gain, and resulting distortion, agrees nearly
    exactly with predictions. It\'s also worth noting that the amp has
    new tubes and before the tubes were replaced the gain was about 20%
    less than predicted. Deluxe Reverbs distort quite easily on the
    Vibrato channel. If you want clean use the Normal channel. If you
    want really clean use the Normal channel and set the Input Trim to
    0.5 to simulate using the Low input.\"
    [\[217\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/does-the-fractal-deluxe-reverb-sound-broken-to-anyone-else.5269/page-5#post-214886){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
9.  \"One of my favorite things to do is dime the Drive and Treble on
    the Deluxe Reverb Vibrato and turn the Bass way down.\"
    [\[218\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/have-you-dimed-your-fender-amp-today.208284/#post-2600181){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
10. \"Our reference Deluxe Reverb measured about 20% less gain before
    the tubes were replaced. This was partially due to the use of Groove
    Tubes in the reference amp. Groove Tubes tend to have a lower mu
    than a \"normal\" 12AX7A. The Groove Tubes were replaced with a
    different brand with a measured mu of approx 100 (as it should
    be).\"
    [\[219\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/not-quite-like-the-real-amp.209204/#post-2613715){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
11. \"You\'d be amazed how \"Plexi\" a Deluxe Reverb can sound. Turn the
    bass down, volume and treble all the way up and put it into a
    4x12.\"
    [\[220\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/us-deluxe-reverb-mild-drive-pedal-what-took-me-so-freakin-long.8146/page-2#post-334670){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
12. "Take a Deluxe Reverb. Gain on 10, Treble on 10, Bass at 0. Nasty."
    [\[221\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/fractal-icons-plugin.10851/page-21#post-461613){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#DIAMANTE_FIRE_(22W_Diamond_Del_Fuego)}[DIAMANTE FIRE (22W Diamond Del Fuego)]{#DIAMANTE_FIRE_.2822W_Diamond_Del_Fuego.29 .mw-headline}

[![FUEGO.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/5/55/FUEGO.jpg/300px-FUEGO.jpg){decoding="async"

22W Class-A amplifier with two channels, designed by Roy Blankenship,
based on a \'60s Class-A 18W Marshall

Modeled channel: not disclosed

Volume, Tone, Tremolo effect (on one of the channels)

Power tubes: EL84

No negative feedback

Fractal Audio:

## []{#DIRTY_SHIRLEY_1_(40W_Friedman_Dirty_Shirley)}[DIRTY SHIRLEY 1 (40W Friedman Dirty Shirley)]{#DIRTY_SHIRLEY_1_.2840W_Friedman_Dirty_Shirley.29 .mw-headline}

[![Dirtyshirley.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/5/53/Dirtyshirley.jpg/325px-Dirtyshirley.jpg){decoding="async"
width="325" height="140"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/5/53/Dirtyshirley.jpg/488px-Dirtyshirley.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/5/53/Dirtyshirley.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Dirtyshirley.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Earlier version of the amp with different component values, a little
  more aggressive than the regular model
- Current version of the amp

Cab:

- original: Friedman 4x12 (V30, G12M, G12-65, G12H)
- matching DynaCab: 4x12 Friedman GB

Gain, Master, Bass, Middle, Treble, Presence

Power tubes: 5881

1.  \"If you want more clarity in the low mids (\...) reduce Negative
    Feedback. Friedman\'s designs are a bit odd in that he takes the
    feedback off the speaker jack rather than off a transformer tap.
    (\...) The amp will sound tighter and clearer in the low mids.\"
    [\[224\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/underrated-amp-models.109894/page-2#post-1316362){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The design is weird as the negative feedback is taken off the
    speaker jack. So if you use a 16-ohm speaker you get more feedback
    (and much more bass) than if you use an 8-ohm speaker. (\...) It\'s
    too much bass for me so I turn down the Depth and reduce Negative
    Feedback a bit.\"
    [\[225\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/question-about-the-friedman-amp-presets.110511/#post-1322655){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"I always lower the negative feedback. Friedman amps are a bit
    strange because the negative feedback is taken off the speaker jack
    instead of one of the transformer taps. The matching cabs are 16
    ohms but if you use an 8-ohm cab you\'ll get 30% less feedback.\"
    [\[226\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/couple-of-observations-about-the-friedmans-in-7-02.126030/page-2#post-1504343){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"They are very dark amp when used with the matching 16-ohm cabinet.
    The feedback is off the speaker jack (don\'t ask me why, doesn\'t
    make sense). This results in a lot of negative feedback at high
    frequencies which makes the sound dark. The amp is modeled assuming
    a 16-ohm load. If you use them into an 8-ohm cabinet they\'re
    brighter. To simulate this lower the negative feedback by 1/sqrt(2).
    This results in a negative feedback value of 3.\"
    [\[227\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-4-cygnus-firmware-public-beta.170253/post-2052720){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"At first I didn\'t like it but for some genres it works. The old
    version (new model) has a 2.2 nF cap on the cathode follower while
    the newer version has 4.7 nF. The larger cap smooths out the
    distortion. The cathode bypass cap values are different as well
    which changes the midrange response.\"
    [\[228\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-ii-quantum-rev-7-00-public-beta-2.124097/page-18#post-1477587){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"Some amps have a fixed depth circuit, e.g. 5153, Freidman BE/HBE,
    Dirty Shirley, TripTik, Tucana, et. al. In these cases the Depth
    knob will default to a value that corresponds to the fixed
    circuit.\"
    [\[229\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/lets-talk-about-the-depth-control.88747/#post-1071598){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  \"Dirty Shirley 1 is actually the latest version of the amp.\"
    [\[230\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-4-cygnus-firmware-public-beta.170253/post-2048948){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
8.  \"Dirty Shirley 2 is the brighter of the two (has a 2.2nF cathode
    cap instead of 4.7nF).\"
    [\[231\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-4-cygnus-firmware-public-beta.170253/post-2052814){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
9.  \"They are dark amps.\"
    [\[232\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/cygnus-dirty-shirley-dark.173450/post-2100020){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## [DIRTY SHIRLEY 2]{#DIRTY_SHIRLEY_2 .mw-headline}

[![Dirtyshirley.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/5/53/Dirtyshirley.jpg/300px-Dirtyshirley.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="129"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/5/53/Dirtyshirley.jpg/450px-Dirtyshirley.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/5/53/Dirtyshirley.jpg/600px-Dirtyshirley.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Dirtyshirley.jpg){.image}

## []{#DIV/13_CJ_(Divided_By_13_CJ_11)}[DIV/13 CJ (Divided By 13 CJ 11)]{#DIV.2F13_CJ_.28Divided_By_13_CJ_11.29 .mw-headline}

[![Cj11.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/3/39/Cj11.jpg/300px-Cj11.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="261"
srcset="/wiki/images/3/39/Cj11.jpg 1.5x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Cj11.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Mid Gain Boost: off
- Mid Gain Boost: on

The AM4 has a single model with Mid Boost switch

Cab:

- original: Divided by 13 (G12M)
- matching DynaCab: 1x12 Div13 CJ11

Volume (pull: Mid Gain boost), Treble, Bass, Master

Power tubes: 6V6

No negative feedback

1.  \"It is a bassy amp. Works best with single coils.\"
    [\[233\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/13-goodness-st-michael-blues.56060/#post-706664){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"You increase the LOW CUT FREQ to reduce the fuzziness on bass
    notes but then it won\'t sound like the real thing.\"
    [\[234\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/724268){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#DIV/13_CJ_BOOST}[DIV/13 CJ BOOST]{#DIV.2F13_CJ_BOOST .mw-headline}

## []{#DIV/13_FT37_HIGH_(Divided_By_13_FTR_37)}[DIV/13 FT37 HIGH (Divided By 13 FTR 37)]{#DIV.2F13_FT37_HIGH_.28Divided_By_13_FTR_37.29 .mw-headline}

[![Ftr37.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/f/fe/Ftr37.jpg/300px-Ftr37.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="369"
srcset="/wiki/images/f/fe/Ftr37.jpg 1.5x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Ftr37.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Low: channel 1, Mid Gain Boost: off
- High: channel 1, Mid Gain Boost: on

The AM4 has a single model with Mid/Gain Boost switch

Cab:

- original: Divided by 13 (G12H and Alnico)
- matching DynaCab: 2x12 Chiefman

Volume (pull: Mid Gain Boost), Treble, Bass

Power tubes: 6V6

No negative feedback

## []{#DIV/13_FT37_LOW}[DIV/13 FT37 LOW]{#DIV.2F13_FT37_LOW .mw-headline}

## []{#DIZZY_V4_BLUE_2_(Diezel_VH4)}[DIZZY V4 BLUE 2 (Diezel VH4)]{#DIZZY_V4_BLUE_2_.28Diezel_VH4.29 .mw-headline}

[![VH4 DIEZEL
BLUE.png](/wiki/images/thumb/4/40/VH4_DIEZEL_BLUE.png/325px-VH4_DIEZEL_BLUE.png){decoding="async"
width="325" height="151"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/4/40/VH4_DIEZEL_BLUE.png/488px-VH4_DIEZEL_BLUE.png 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/4/40/VH4_DIEZEL_BLUE.png/650px-VH4_DIEZEL_BLUE.png 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:VH4_DIEZEL_BLUE.png){.image}

Models:

- Blue faceplate, channel 2 Crunch
- Blue faceplate, channel 3 Mega
- Blue faceplate, channel 4 Lead
- Silver faceplate, channel 2 Crunch
- Silver faceplate, channel 3 Mega
- Silver faceplate, channel 4 Lead

The AM4 doesn\'t have Dizzy V4 Blue models

Cab:

- original: Diezel 4x12 (V30, G12-100)
- matching DynaCab: 4x12 Recto Straight

Power tubes: KT77

Gain, Volume, Bass, Mid, Treble, Presence (4kHz), Deep (80Hz), Bright
switch (not on channels 3 and 4)

1.  \"The reason Diezels compress so much is due to the cathode follower
    design. You can reduce the compression in the models by lowering the
    Compression parameter in the Cathode Follower section.\"
    [\[235\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-release-version-14-00.165157/post-1981183){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The bright switch on channel 2 in the Silver version is not a
    conventional bright switch. It switches in a treble peaker later in
    the circuit. The model models the amp with the bright switch on.\"
    [\[236\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/cygnus-dizzy-amps-bug.173361/post-2102309){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"Humans perceive high frequency thermal noise as hiss. The more
    gain the more hiss. Diezel\'s have a lot of filtering. Large grid
    stoppers, plate capacitors, etc. This reduces the bandwidth which
    lowers the hiss. Camerons are pretty much wide open. Small grid
    stoppers or bypass caps on the grid stoppers, no plate caps, etc.\"
    [\[237\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/why-lower-gain-cameron-ccv-amp-model-feels-more-noisy-than-much-higher-gain-herbie-3.188658/post-2339783){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
