## []{#DOUBLE_VERB_NORMAL_(1966_blackface_Fender_Twin_Reverb)}[DOUBLE VERB NORMAL (1966 blackface Fender Twin Reverb)]{#DOUBLE_VERB_NORMAL_.281966_blackface_Fender_Twin_Reverb.29 .mw-headline}

[![Twin.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/7/78/Twin.jpg/300px-Twin.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="229"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/7/78/Twin.jpg/450px-Twin.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/7/78/Twin.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Twin.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Normal: based on 1966 blackface Fender Twin Reverb, tuned by Andy
  Fuchs, AB763 circuit, Normal channel
- Vibrato: based on the Vibrato channel of the same amp
- Silverface: based on the Vibrato channel of a 1971 100 watts
  "Silverface"

Cab:

- original: Fender 2x12 with original speakers
- matching DynaCab: 2x12 Double Verb

Volume, Bass, Middle, Treble, Bright switch, Reverb effect (not
modeled), Vibrato effect (not modeled)

Power tubes: 6L6

1.  (make the Twin cleaner) \"Reduce MV (or MV Trim). The biggest reason
    Silverface Twins were cleaner is because the PI had less gain.
    Reducing the MV or MV Trim will simulate the lower gain.\"
    [\[238\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/910015){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  (original Double Verb model) \"The Twin Reverb that the model is
    based on breaks up like that. The model is MIMIC\'d and is extremely
    accurate. It\'s a Blackface Twin which breaks up easy compared to
    later Twins. Furthermore, as with all models, it is modeled on the
    \"Hi\" input. If you don\'t want it to break up as easy turn Input
    Trim to 0.5 to simulate using the \"Low\" input, reduce Input Drive
    and MV as necessary. You may want to turn the Bright Switch off as
    well. People who want squeaky clean usually turn the Bright Switch
    off on these amps. However, you\'d be surprised that a Twin isn\'t
    nearly as clean as you think. It\'s just so damn loud that you get
    the sensation that it\'s clean because a light touch on the strings
    creates a lot of volume.\"
    [\[239\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/968763){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The model is extremely accurate and is based on a 1966 Blackface
    Twin Reverb. Part of the reason the Blackface era are so sought
    after is because they distort. They are NOT clean amps by any
    stretch.\"
    [\[240\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/twin-issue.119594/#post-1422765){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"A Dual Showman with the AB763 circuit has one less gain stage than
    a Twin Reverb so it will have less gain. There are two gain stages.
    The Vibrato channel of an AB763 Twin Reverb has three gain stages.
    An AA769 Dual Showman Reverb on the Vibrato channel will have
    similar gain as it has three gain stages. The circuit number, i.e.
    AB763, does not mean that the circuits are identical. It refers to
    the circa of the design. An AB763 Dual Showman is not the same
    circuit as an AB763 Twin Reverb.\"
    [\[241\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/twin-issue.119594/page-2#post-1423069){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"The Super Reverb is really just a 50W version of a Twin Reverb
    with different speakers.\"
    [\[242\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/wanted-amps-to-model.56753/page-4#post-713267){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#DOUBLE_VERB_SILVERFACE_(1971_silverface_Fender_Twin_Reverb)}[DOUBLE VERB SILVERFACE (1971 silverface Fender Twin Reverb)]{#DOUBLE_VERB_SILVERFACE_.281971_silverface_Fender_Twin_Reverb.29 .mw-headline}

## []{#DOUBLE_VERB_VIBRATO_(1966_blackface_Fender_Twin_Reverb)}[DOUBLE VERB VIBRATO (1966 blackface Fender Twin Reverb)]{#DOUBLE_VERB_VIBRATO_.281966_blackface_Fender_Twin_Reverb.29 .mw-headline}

## []{#DWEEZIL'S_BASSGUY_(Dweezil_Zappa's_1965_blackface_Fender_Bassman,_AB165)}[DWEEZIL\'S BASSGUY (Dweezil Zappa\'s 1965 blackface Fender Bassman, AB165)]{#DWEEZIL.27S_BASSGUY_.28Dweezil_Zappa.27s_1965_blackface_Fender_Bassman.2C_AB165.29 .mw-headline}

Model of 1965 Bassman Bass channel, modded by Blankenship

Cab:

- original: Fender 2x12 (Oxford)
- matching DynaCab: 4x12 1960TV

Volume, Negative feedback, fixed Presence circuit (Presence should be at
10)

Power tubes: 6L6

See [65
Bassguy](#65_BASSGUY_BASS_.281965_blackface_Fender_Bassman_head.2C_AB165.29)

1.  \"It\'s Dweezil\'s Blankenship modified Bassman. Dweezil\'s Bassman
    has two channels like a regular Bassman. The Normal channel is
    \"normal\" and corresponds to the 65 Bassguy Nrml model. The Bass
    Instrument channel is modified and that\'s the basis for the new
    model (Dweezil\'s B-man). It has a boatload of gain and sounds more
    like a Plexi than a Fender.\"
    [\[243\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-ii-quantum-rev-3-00-public-beta.113410/page-5#post-1356686){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"Just finished matching this modded 65 Bassman that Dweezil sent
    me. It\'s a crazy sounding amp, sounds nothing like your typical
    Fender. It was modded by Roy Blankenship.\"
    [\[244\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/another-v10-preview.62489){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The 65 Bassguy was matched to a 65 Bassman that Dweezil sent me.
    It\'s a vicious amp that sounds more like a Plexi than a Fender.
    It\'s the infamous AB165 circuit which is very crunchy and bright
    and does not sound like your typical Fender.\"
    [\[245\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/am-i-the-only-one-who-noticed-that-some-amps-have-alot-more-gain.51123/page-2#post-658833){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"The actual amp has no tone stack so for maximum authenticity all
    tone controls would be at noon (but don\'t be afraid to tweak them).
    In the actual amp the Treble control is re-purposed as a Negative
    Feedback control. Experiment with different values of Negative
    Feedback. Lower values are looser.\"
    [\[246\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/help-with-trying-out-a-new-amp-block-dweezils-b-man.114154/#post-1365573){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#ENERGYBALL_(Engl_Powerball)}[ENERGYBALL (Engl Powerball)]{#ENERGYBALL_.28Engl_Powerball.29 .mw-headline}

[![Powerball.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/b/b0/Powerball.jpg/300px-Powerball.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="161"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/b/b0/Powerball.jpg/450px-Powerball.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/b/b0/Powerball.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Powerball.jpg){.image}

Lead channel model

Cab:

- original: Engl 4x12 (V30, V60)
- matching DynaCab: 4x12 Recto Straight

Lead channel: Gain, Lo/Hi Lead switch, Bass, Mid-Open, Mid-Focused,
Treble, Open/Focused switch (boosts 300-500 Hz) mode, Presence, Depth
Punch

Power tubes: 6L6

1.  (Cygnus) \"The model was completely redone.\"
    [\[247\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-12-cygnus-firmware-public-release-candidate.172027/post-2079284){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

\

------------------------------------------------------------------------

Regarding the following EURO models:

1.  \"People think Bogners are dark but they really aren\'t. The reason
    they seem that way is the pot tapers. Most people assume knobs
    should be set somewhere around noon. If you do this on a Bogner
    it\'s like turning the treble way down on a Marshall. Close your
    eyes and adjust the tone controls with your ears. Don\'t be afraid
    to turn them way up or way down.\"
    [\[248\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1031334){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"Human nature is to put the knobs near noon. We are reticent to
    deviate much from noon. Amp designers exploit this and use different
    tapers to change the sound of their amps WITH THE KNOBS AT NOON. A
    prime example are Bogner amps. Everyone says \"Bogner amps are
    dark\". No they aren\'t. But he uses a Log10A taper for the treble
    pot. It\'s a standard Marshall tone stack. Usually a linear taper
    pot is used for the treble. The treble knob at 5.0 (noon) on a
    Bogner is equivalent to the treble knob at 1.0 on a Marshall. People
    put the knob at 5.0 and go \"wow, this amp is dark\". No it isn\'t.
    If you turned the treble up to 8 or 9 it would sound a lot like a
    Plexi but humans are reticent to turn the knobs to extremes. Amp
    designers know this and exploit it to give their amps a \"signature
    sound\".\"
    [\[249\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1047275){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"Bogner\'s are notoriously \"slow\" due to the low B+ voltage. Main
    reason I can\'t get along with them. You can try increasing the
    Variac.\"
    [\[250\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/fast-pick-attack-amp.170370/post-2049711){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"Most amps use a linear taper for the treble pot. Bogners use a log
    taper. So when the knob is at noon on a Bogner it\'s similar to 8
    o\'clock on most amps.\"
    [\[251\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-11-cygnus-firmware-public-beta-8.171486/post-2067364){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#EURO_BLUE_(Bogner_Ecstasy_20th_Anniversary)}[EURO BLUE (Bogner Ecstasy 20th Anniversary)]{#EURO_BLUE_.28Bogner_Ecstasy_20th_Anniversary.29 .mw-headline}

[![Ecstasy.png](/wiki/images/thumb/4/41/Ecstasy.png/325px-Ecstasy.png){decoding="async"
width="325" height="120"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/4/41/Ecstasy.png/488px-Ecstasy.png 1.5x, /wiki/images/4/41/Ecstasy.png 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Ecstasy.png){.image}

Models:

- Blue channel, structure: Vintage
- Blue channel, structure: Modern
- Red channel, structure: Vintage
- Red channel, structure: Modern

Cab:

- original: Bogner 2x12 or 4x12 (V30)
- matching DynaCab: 4x12 Friedman V30

Gain, Master, Bass, Middle, Treble, Presence, Bright switch, Structure
switch (gain reduction), Old/New Style switch (not modeled), Excursion
switch, Gain switch, Plexi Mode (not modeled)

Power tubes: EL34 (earlier models were based on the 6L6 version)

1.  \"My actual XTC has a Log10 pot for the treble which is an odd
    choice. The problem with a log-taper pot is that the treble does
    almost nothing for the first 50%. So you can\'t use your eyes if you
    want to copy the tone.\"
    [\[252\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/part-ii-things-learned-comparing-axe-fx-to-bogner-blue-chan.31706/#post-449541){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"Our reference amp is a 20th anniversary and N is Bright Off, B1 is
    150 pF and B2 is 1000 pF for both channels. The models default to
    B1. Change the Bright Cap value to 1 nF to emulate B2. Or better yet
    use your ears to select a value that sounds best.\"
    [\[253\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/bogner-ecstasy-pre-amp-eq-b1-n-b2.109077/#post-1305047){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  (Class A) \"Turn up Power Tube Grid Bias. In real life that is tough
    on tubes as it makes them run very hot.\"
    [\[254\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/replicating-the-bogner-ecstasy-class-a-mode.145294/#post-1718463){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"The tonestack tapers in the Ecstasy model match the amp.\"
    [\[255\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/5150-presence-knob.199908/page-9#post-2492617){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"Excursion is Depth. Adjust to taste.\"
    [\[256\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/euro-blue-and-red-excursion-switch.201955/post-2525380){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"The Ecstacy uses a switch with three fixed resistor values. The
    model uses a pot instead. The model is based on a 20th Anniversary
    addition. It is different than a 101.\"
    [\[257\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/euro-blue-and-red-excursion-switch.201955/post-2525522){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  \"The values for the L, M and T are 1M, 180K, 0 ohms. The capacitor
    does not change.\"
    [\[258\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/euro-blue-and-red-excursion-switch.201955/page-2#post-2527379){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#EURO_UBER_(Bogner_Uberschall)}[EURO UBER (Bogner Uberschall)]{#EURO_UBER_.28Bogner_Uberschall.29 .mw-headline}

[![Uber.png](/wiki/images/thumb/0/0f/Uber.png/300px-Uber.png){decoding="async"
width="300" height="118"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/0/0f/Uber.png/450px-Uber.png 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/0/0f/Uber.png/600px-Uber.png 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Uber.png){.image}

High gain channel model

Cab:

- original: Bogner 4x12 Uberkab (G12-T75 and V30)
- matching DynaCab: 4x12 Recto Straight

Gain, Master, Bass, Middle, Treble, Presence, Depth (only on Twin-Jet
Uberschall, not modeled)

Power tubes: EL34

1.  \"The feedback circuit is responsible for the behavior of the
    Presence and Depth controls. Certain Bogners and Diezels have a
    unique type of feedback circuit. There are no new parameters and
    nothing to do except twist the Presence and Depth knobs to your
    desired tone. Note that an Uberschall doesn\'t have a Depth knob.
    The default Depth value when you select the Euro Uber model is
    equivalent to the amp\'s fixed depth circuit.\"
    [\[259\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1159760){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"My Uber is a very early one and probably different than later
    models. It has the feedback of the 4-ohm tap whereas I\'ve heard
    later versions have the feedback off the 8-ohm tap. To simulate this
    increase the Negative Feedback.\"
    [\[260\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/bogner-uberschall-help.185084/post-2282705){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"That model does the chugga-chugga better than Thomas the Tank
    Engine.\"
    [\[261\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-firmware-version-21-00-release-candidate-beta-7.188382/post-2336626){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"The Uber has massive amounts of negative feedback and an RLC
    resonant network in the feedback. If the speaker impedance is highly
    resonant at the same frequency as the network (as is the Recto
    Straight) then the power amp becomes an oscillator if you turn the
    Presence down enough. I suspect the real amp would behave the same
    way but I\'m simply not inclined at this time to lug a Recto cab up
    here to prove it. You can do the following:
    1.  Reduce Depth
    2.  Reduce Negative Feedback
    3.  Use a different speaker impedance curve.\"
        [\[262\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/euro-uber-presence-bug.200892/#post-2508072){.external
        .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#FAS_6160_(custom_model)}[FAS 6160 (custom model)]{#FAS_6160_.28custom_model.29 .mw-headline}

[![Logo small.png](/wiki/images/e/ef/Logo_small.png){decoding="async"
width="50"
height="50"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Logo_small.png){.image}

Custom Fractal Audio model

Matching DynaCab: 4x12 5153

Power tubes: 6L6

1.  \"Based on the PVH 6160 model but more open and less fizzy than the
    original amp. Also, a virtual choke has replaced the resistor found
    on the original's power supply filter. This results in a bouncier
    feel.\"

\

------------------------------------------------------------------------

Regarding the following custom FAS models:

1.  \"If I had my way there would be only FAS models but too many people
    demand reproductions of existing amps.\"
    [\[263\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/fas-class-a-is-even-better-than-the-real-thing.162257/post-1944014){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The FAS models are idealized and have some of the \"design flaws\"
    removed or reduced.\"
    [\[264\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-10-00-public-beta-2.154782/post-1841528){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The FAS models typically remove or minimize the undesirable
    characteristics of those old amps. Guitar tube amp design was
    nascent in the 60s and 70s and designers didn\'t fully understand
    the impact of overdriving tubes. One of the biggest issues was
    blocking distortion which is excessive bias excursion. When the grid
    conducts it shifts the bias point and in those old amps it can shift
    so much that the tube goes into cutoff prematurely. More modern
    designs employ grid stoppers and smaller coupling capacitors to
    reduce bias excursion.\"
    [\[265\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/fas-class-a-is-even-better-than-the-real-thing.162257/post-1944071){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#FAS_BROOTALZ_(custom_model)}[FAS BROOTALZ (custom model)]{#FAS_BROOTALZ_.28custom_model.29 .mw-headline}

[![Logo small.png](/wiki/images/e/ef/Logo_small.png){decoding="async"
width="50"
height="50"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Logo_small.png){.image}

Custom Fractal Audio model

Matching DynaCab: 4x12 515 Stealth

Power tubes: 6550

1.  \"This amp was an accident. I was working on the Savage model and
    accidentally used the input stage from an SLO100. So it\'s the front
    end of an SLO100 with the back end of a Savage. It\'s probably an
    SLO100 power amp too but I\'d have to check.\"
    [\[266\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1020502){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"Brootalz uses the Engl Savage presence network which reduces
    negative feedback as the control is turned down causing an increase
    in volume.\"
    [\[267\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-5-cygnus-firmware-public-beta-2.170901/post-2059273){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#FAS_BUTTERY_(custom_model)}[FAS BUTTERY (custom model)]{#FAS_BUTTERY_.28custom_model.29 .mw-headline}

[![Logo small.png](/wiki/images/e/ef/Logo_small.png){decoding="async"
width="50"
height="50"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Logo_small.png){.image}

Custom Fractal Audio model. In the original Cygnus release, it was
replaced by an authentic Budda Twinmaster model. It returned in firmware
17 for the Axe-Fx III and later, and firmware for the FM3 and FM9.

Matching DynaCab: 2x12 Double Verb

Power tubes: EL84

No negative feedback

1.  \"I did the Buttery model by ear. I listened to some clips of Buddas
    (Matchbox 20\... excellent!) and tweaked the model until I thought
    it sounded like one. Screwed around a little with the tube bias
    points until it had the right balance of harmonics and called it a
    day.\"
2.  \"It\'s still the \"ear tuned\" version. I bought the amp but
    because it was so popular as-is I didn\'t dare change it.\"
    [\[268\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/question-for-cliff-regarding-the-buttery-model.90943/#post-1095174){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"Buttery is a virtual amp model that was created by ear. There is
    no physical, real amp that exists upon which it was based. It\'s
    like the FAS models. They exist solely in the virtual world. They
    all still benefit from the Quantum stuff though as they use the same
    underlying algorithms for the tube modeling. The amp model,
    regardless of how accurate it is (and it\'s probably grossly
    inaccurate as I never compared it to any actual amp) is very popular
    and that\'s why it was never matched to any real amp.\"
    [\[269\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/question-for-cliff-regarding-the-buttery-model.90943/page-2#post-1283301){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"Yeah, Buttery was a legacy model from the first Axe-Fx.\"
    [\[270\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-12-cygnus-firmware-public-release-candidate.172027/post-2075782){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"The previous model wasn\'t based on any real amp. It was a \"FAS
    Original\".
    [\[271\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-12-cygnus-firmware-public-release-candidate.172027/post-2076487){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#FAS_EXPRESS_(custom_model)}[FAS EXPRESS (custom model)]{#FAS_EXPRESS_.28custom_model.29 .mw-headline}

[![Logo small.png](/wiki/images/e/ef/Logo_small.png){decoding="async"
width="50"
height="50"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Logo_small.png){.image}

Custom Fractal Audio model

Matching DynaCab: 4x12 Friedman GB

Power tubes: EL34

See [Wrecker Express](#WRECKER_EXPRESS_.28Trainwreck_Express.29)

1.  \"Based on hypothetical modifications to a Trainwreck Express.\"
2.  \"It has a master volume. That\'s one of the \"mods\".\"
    [\[273\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-version-11-02-public-beta-5-beta_4.157025/post-1875792){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  (Trainwreck Express) \"That amp exhibits a lot of blocking
    distortion (in the phase inverter) due to its design. You can reduce
    this via either the PI Bias Excursion or Master Bias Excursion
    parameters. Another option is to use the FAS Express model which
    puts some resistors between the last triode stage and the PI to
    reduce the bias excursion.\"
    [\[274\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/blocking-distortion-found-in-trainwreck-express.182895/post-2247268){.external

## []{#FAS_MODERN_(custom_model)}[FAS MODERN (custom model)]{#FAS_MODERN_.28custom_model.29 .mw-headline}

[![Logo small.png](/wiki/images/e/ef/Logo_small.png){decoding="async"
width="50"
height="50"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Logo_small.png){.image}

Custom Fractal Audio model

Matching DynaCab: 4x12 Recto Straight

Power tubes: 6L6

1.  \"This model is my interpretation of the ideal modern metal tone. In
    the digital realm we are not constrained by the limitations that
    face tube amp designers so we are free to implement designs that
    would be nearly impossible with a tube amp. The Axe-Fx II modeling
    includes a variety of general purpose filters that I can place
    anywhere in the signal path. So I put some second-order filters in
    there to tighten up the tone. Implementing second-order filters in a
    real tube amp is difficult and costly so is rarely seen.\"
    [\[276\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/715029){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"It\'s loosely based on a Recto but with tighter bass.\"
    [\[277\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/fw-6-0-rectifier-obsevation.51197/#post-658849){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  (MESA Rectifier) \"Personally I hate the 39K resistor. It biases the
    stage much too cold for my tastes. It prevents blocking distortion
    but there are better ways to do it IMO. The FAS Modern model is
    similar but biases the stage more towards the center.\"
    [\[278\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/new-amp-models.159097/post-1901438){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#FOX_ODS_(Fuchs_Overdrive_Supreme_50)}[FOX ODS (Fuchs Overdrive Supreme 50)]{#FOX_ODS_.28Fuchs_Overdrive_Supreme_50.29 .mw-headline}

[![Fuchs.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/9/90/Fuchs.jpg/300px-Fuchs.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="168"
srcset="/wiki/images/9/90/Fuchs.jpg 1.5x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Fuchs.jpg){.image}

The amp has been modeled with Pre-Amp Bypass engaged (no tone controls):

- ODS: Deep switch off
- ODS Deep: Deep switch on

The AM4 has a single model, based on the amp with PAB engaged, with a
Mid Boost switch

Cab:

- original: Fuchs 2x12 (Eminence)
- matching DynaCab: 4x12 Rumble EV12S

Gain, High (pull: mid boost), Mid (pull: gain boost), Low, Input, Brite
switch, Deep switch, Rock/Jazz switch (not modeled), Master, Accent (=
Presence), Pre-Amp Bypass

Power tubes: 6L6

1.  \"Supposedly a Dumble ODS clone but our reference amp has way more
    gain than our Dumble.\"
    [\[280\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1174814){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The topology of the Fuchs is pure Dumble. The difference is that
    there is less padding between stages 2 and 3 (IIRC). So it\'s a
    high-gain Dumble. Personally I don\'t think the Dumble topology
    lends itself to that much gain but I didn\'t design the amp. If you
    like the base Dumble sound but want a little more gain without the
    fuzziness of a Fuchs try the Carol-Ann models.\"
    [\[281\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/fuchs-ods-in-cygnus.172291/post-2081523){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## [FOX ODS DEEP]{#FOX_ODS_DEEP .mw-headline}

## []{#FRIEDMAN_BE_2010_(Friedman_BE)}[FRIEDMAN BE 2010 (Friedman BE)]{#FRIEDMAN_BE_2010_.28Friedman_BE.29 .mw-headline}

[![BE.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/a/a2/BE.jpg/300px-BE.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="140"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/a/a2/BE.jpg/450px-BE.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/a/a2/BE.jpg/600px-BE.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:BE.jpg){.image}

Current models:

- BE 2010: 2010 Friedman BE-100 (probably the \"Marsha\" edition)
- BE C45: later BE-100, C45 switch engaged
- BE V1: later BE-100, voice: left
- BE V1 Fat: later BE-100, voice: left, FAT switch engaged
- BE V2: later BE-100, voice: middle (brightest)
- BE V3: later BE-100, voice: right
- HBE 2010: 2010 Friedman BE-100 (probably the \"Marsha\" edition), HBE
  mode
- HBE C45: later BE-100, C45 switch engaged
- HBE V1: later BE-100, voice: left
- HBE V1 Fat: later BE-100, voice: left, FAT switch engaged
- HBE V2: later BE-100, voice: middle (brightest)
- HBE V3: later BE-100, voice: right

The AM4 has consolidated models with switches

Previous models:

- BE: based on old Marsha model, BE mode
- BE C45: based on Mark Day\'s BE-100, C45 switch engaged
- BE V1: based on Mark Day\'s BE-100, voice: right (less mids)
- BE V2: based on Mark Day\'s BE-100, voice: left (more mids)
- HBE: based on old Marsha model, HBE mode
- HBE 2018: based on 2018 BE-100, HBE mode
- HBE 2018 C45: based on 2018 BE-100, HBE mode, C45 switch engaged
- HBE V1: based on Mark Day\'s BE-100, HBE mode, voice: right (less
  mids)
- HBE V2: based on Mark Day\'s BE-100, HBE mode, voice: left (more mids)

Cab:

- original: Friedman 4x12 (V30 and/or G12M)
- matching DynaCab: 4x12 Friedman V30

Gain, Master, Bass, Middle, Treble, Presence, Bright (clean channel
only). BE-100 Deluxe: Thump control. Switches: FAT, C45 (treble boost),
SAT (model: SAT), 3-position Voice switch (changes the top-end response
of the dirty channels), Negative feedback switch

Power tubes: EL34

1.  (before Cygnus) \"The old model is an original, hand-built
    \"Marsha\". It\'s MUCH darker than Mark\'s newer BE/HBE. In fact
    it\'s so dark and boomy I emailed Dave to make sure the amp was
    built correctly. Turns out the snubber cap is the wrong value. But
    even with the snubber cap corrected it\'s still very dark and boomy
    which made me question as to whether there are other components that
    are incorrect. So we decided to redo the model based on Mark\'s amp
    which is the amp that was the demo model at Tone Merchants.\"
    [\[282\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/the-new-hbe.112717/#post-1348497){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  (before Cygnus) \"The models are based on two different amps. The V1
    and V2 are based on Mark Day\'s BE100. The other models are based on
    our original \"Marsha\". Like most boutique amp makers Friedman\'s
    designs have evolved over time with changes to the circuit. The
    original Marsha we have is dark and bassy with lots of lowpass
    filtering. The newer amp is brighter and tighter. For now note that
    V1/V2 refer to the newer amp and represent the position of the
    Voicing switch.\"
    [\[283\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/which-are-the-new-be-hbe-models.114510/#post-1369754){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The BE/HBE has a fixed depth circuit that gives a lot of bass
    boost. The model defaults the Depth to match this.\"
    [\[284\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/833169){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"Some amps have a fixed depth circuit, e.g. 5153, Freidman BE/HBE,
    Dirty Shirley, TripTik, Tucana, et. al. In these cases the Depth
    knob will default to a value that corresponds to the fixed
    circuit.\"
    [\[285\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/lets-talk-about-the-depth-control.88747/#post-1071598){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"When you watch a video Dave himself turns the bass way up. Steve
    Stevens and Jerry Cantrell turn the bass way up too. If I did that
    with my guitar it would be a muddy mess. Puzzling to me because the
    BE has a fixed depth circuit and a significant amount of negative
    feedback so there is quite a bit of bass boost in the power amp as
    well.\"
    [\[286\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/friedman-be-100-hbe-channel-vs-the-axe-fx-3-hbe-model.144911/#post-1714308){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"C45 is a treble boost on the input. Put a filter block before the
    amp as follows: Type: Tilt EQ - Freq: 700 Hz - Gain: 4.5 dB\"
    [\[287\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/friedman-hbe-with-c45-switch.110686/#post-1324975){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  [Discussion about the Bass
    control](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/friedman-be-100-hbe-channel-vs-the-axe-fx-3-hbe-model.144911){.external
    .text target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
8.  \"The BE has very light power supply filtering like old Plexis.\"
    [\[288\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-release-version-14-01.165716/post-1990715){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
9.  \"That\'s the way the HBE channel sounds. The problem with the
    design is that the drive control is located between the 3rd and 4th
    gain stages. Too far back IMO. This causes a lot of distortion and
    also a lot of bias excursion before the drive control with no way to
    control it. In most amps the drive control is located after the
    first stage (input buffer). Some amps have a second drive control,
    typically called an Overdrive, located further downstream which
    allows you to balance the pre- and post distortion. One way to deal
    with it is to decrease the Input Trim and increase the Input Drive.
    You can also try reducing the Master Bias Excursion but that won\'t
    get rid of the pre-drive control distortion. A lot of people like
    this sound though. It has a certain stringy quality that many people
    find desirable.\"
    [\[289\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-10-cygnus-firmware-public-beta-7.171198/post-2062927){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
10. \"There are now three \"Voicings\": V1, V2 and V3 corresponding to
    the three positions of the Voice switch.\"
    [\[290\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-11-cygnus-firmware-public-beta-8.171486){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
11. Based on latest version of amp. There are now three \"Voicings\":
    V1, V2 and V3 corresponding to the three positions of the Voice
    switch.\"
    [\[291\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-11-cygnus-firmware-public-beta-8.171486/post-2067182){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
12. \"All the Friedman models are now based on the latest amp. Our
    reference amp was made in 2018 and has the feedback off the 4-ohm
    tap.\"
    [\[292\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-4-cygnus-firmware-public-beta.170253/post-2047861){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
13. \"Our reference amp is a 2018 model year. It has NFB off the speaker
    jack.\"
    [\[293\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-28-00-release.211568/page-3#post-2646363){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
14. \"The BE100 design has changed over the years. Dave is constantly
    fiddling with things. The original \"Marsha\" (which became the
    BE100 after the cease-and-desist) had the Gain control after the
    second stage. Later versions have the gain control after the third
    stage so even if you turn the gain down you may still get some
    distortion. There were also numerous changes to component values,
    feedback tap, etc., etc. Our models are authentic recreations of the
    two particular versions we have. Whether those versions match your
    particular version is unknown.\"
    [\[294\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/friedman-amps-in-axefx3-vs-helix.197851/post-2458958){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
15. \"Here\'s the story with the Friedman models: The BE/HBE have the
    gain pot before the last gain stage. This is a poor design choice
    IMO because you\'re always getting distortion even if you turn the
    gain down. Bad gain-staging IOW. Before the Cygnus firmware I was
    more about \"make it sound good\" rather than accuracy. Hence,
    non-authentic pot tapers, etc. So I moved the gain pot forward a
    stage because it sounded better to me that way. I left the treble
    peaker before the last stage and just moved the gain pot forward.
    More like a classic Marshall. But as our products became more and
    more popular the cries of \"it doesn\'t sound exactly like my amp\"
    became more frequent. So Cygnus became all about authenticity. There
    are still some remnants of Ares left over (i.e., pot tapers) that we
    have been correcting over time as we discover them but now the
    models behave like the amps and my tweaks to make things \"sound
    better\" have been removed, for better or worse.\"
    [\[295\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/fractal-talk.2745/post-151874){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
16. \"The BE tone stack is almost identical to a Marshall. The reason
    the BE is smoother is there are several caps sprinkled about that
    roll off the highs. The snubber cap is also twice as big as a
    Marshall which rolls off the highs in the power amp more. The
    feedback network has a fixed Depth cap which boosts the lows. It\'s
    also strange in that the feedback is taken off the speaker jack
    rather than a tap on the transformer. So if you use a 16-ohm cab it
    will sound different than using an 8-ohm load (even more bassy).\"
    [\[296\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/fractal-talk.2745/page-495#post-296102){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
17. \"Added Negative Feedback control to UI for Friedman BE/HBE models
    since this is now a control on the actual amp.\"
18. \"The newer BE-100s have the feedback off the 4-ohm tap. This
    corresponds to a Negative Feedback setting of about 3.87.\"
    [\[297\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/the-be100-model-thread.10825/#post-458759){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
19. (firmware 32) \"Fixed wrong B+ voltage in Friedman BE/HBE models
    (due to wrong dropping resistor value). These models have been
    remastered accordingly. The default Negative Feedback has been
    changed to being commensurate with being taken from the 4-ohm tap.
    Note that the first-generation BE-100 had the feedback off the
    speaker jack. This was then changed to the 4-ohm tap. The latest
    version has a three-way switch to select between 4/8/16-ohm taps.
    Audition presets and adjust as necessary.\"

Previous comments on negative feedback:

1.  \"If you want more clarity in the low mids from the BE/HBE reduce
    Negative Feedback. Friedman\'s designs are a bit odd in that he
    takes the feedback off the speaker jack rather than off a
    transformer tap. The mating cab for a BE/HBE is 16 ohms which means
    lots of feedback. But if you connect the amp to an 8 ohm load there
    is about 30% less feedback. The amp will sound tighter and clearer
    in the low mids.\"
    [\[298\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/underrated-amp-models.109894/page-2#post-1316362){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The design is weird as the negative feedback is taken off the
    speaker jack. So if you use a 16-ohm speaker you get more feedback
    (and much more bass) than if you use an 8-ohm speaker. The model is
    based on using the matching cab. It\'s too much bass for me so I
    turn down the Depth and reduce Negative Feedback a bit.\"
    [\[299\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/question-about-the-friedman-amp-presets.110511/#post-1322655){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"I always lower the negative feedback. Friedman amps are a bit
    strange because the negative feedback is taken off the speaker jack
    instead of one of the transformer taps. The matching cabs are 16
    ohms but if you use an 8-ohm cab you\'ll get 30% less feedback.\"
    [\[300\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/couple-of-observations-about-the-friedmans-in-7-02.126030/page-2#post-1504343){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  (firmware 28) Updated default Negative Feedback value for Friedman
    BE/HBE models. On the actual amp the negative feedback comes off the
    speaker jack (for some weird reason). Previously the amp models
    assumed an 8-ohm cabinet which would make the feedback effectively
    off the 8-ohm tap. However, the matching cabinet is 16 ohms and
    using a 16-ohm cabinet results in more negative feedback and a
    "tighter" tone so we're now using that as a default value as people
    seem to prefer that. The models were also "remastered" as a
    result.\"

## []{#FRIEDMAN_SMALL_BOX_(Friedman_Smallbox)}[FRIEDMAN SMALL BOX (Friedman Smallbox)]{#FRIEDMAN_SMALL_BOX_.28Friedman_Smallbox.29 .mw-headline}

[![Smallbox.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/3/36/Smallbox.jpg/300px-Smallbox.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="133"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/3/36/Smallbox.jpg/450px-Smallbox.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/3/36/Smallbox.jpg/600px-Smallbox.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Smallbox.jpg){.image}

Channel 2 model

Channel 1 (Plexi sound) has not been modeled

Cab:

- original: Friedman 3x12 (V30 and/or G12M)
- matching DynaCab: 4x12 Friedman GB

Gain, Master, Bass, Middle, Treble, Presence, Bright switch (channel 1
\"Plexi\" only)

Power tubes: EL34

1.  \"The schematic shows a 2.2 nF coupling cap off the first stage but
    the actual amp has a 4.7 nF. 2.2 nF would mean less bass. I can only
    assume the amp was built to the latest specs. If an amp model is
    \"G3\'d\" it is deadly accurate. I go through the amps and check the
    values of each component, measure the voltages, compare the
    frequency response to the model, etc., etc., etc. If the model is
    too bassy for you then you would find the real amp too bassy, or at
    least our particular reference model.\"
    [\[301\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/friedman-sm-box-smallbox.99488/#post-1193341){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"If you want more clarity in the low mids (\...) reduce Negative
    Feedback. Friedman\'s designs are a bit odd in that he takes the
    feedback off the speaker jack rather than off a transformer tap.
    (\...) The amp will sound tighter and clearer in the low mids.\"
    [\[302\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/underrated-amp-models.109894/page-2#post-1316362){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The design is weird as the negative feedback is taken off the
    speaker jack. So if you use a 16-ohm speaker you get more feedback
    (and much more bass) than if you use an 8-ohm speaker. (\...) It\'s
    too much bass for me so I turn down the Depth and reduce Negative
    Feedback a bit.\"
    [\[303\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/question-about-the-friedman-amp-presets.110511/#post-1322655){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"I always lower the negative feedback. Friedman amps are a bit
    strange because the negative feedback is taken off the speaker jack
    instead of one of the transformer taps. The matching cabs are 16
    ohms but if you use an 8-ohm cab you\'ll get 30% less feedback.\"
    [\[304\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/couple-of-observations-about-the-friedmans-in-7-02.126030/page-2#post-1504343){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#HERBIE_CH2+_(Diezel_Herbert)}[HERBIE CH2+ (Diezel Herbert)]{#HERBIE_CH2.2B_.28Diezel_Herbert.29 .mw-headline}

[![Herbert.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/d/d1/Herbert.jpg/300px-Herbert.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="122"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/d/d1/Herbert.jpg/450px-Herbert.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/d/d1/Herbert.jpg/600px-Herbert.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Herbert.jpg){.image}

Models:

- original Herbert, channel 2+ (based on Marshall JC800)
- original Herbert, channel 2- (based on Marshall Plexi)
- original Herbert, Channel 3 (based on Diezel VH4)
- Black-panel Herbert MK III, Channel 2+

Cab:

- original: Diezel 4x12 (V30, G12-K100)
- DynaCab match: 4x12 Recto Straight

Gain (not on channel 1), Bass, Middle (1 kHz), Treble, Master, Presence
(\> 3kHz), Deep (120Hz), Mid-Cut (not modeled), Gain Boost switch (not
modeled)

Power tubes: KT77

1.  \"The reason Diezels compress so much is due to the cathode follower
    design. You can reduce the compression in the models by lowering the
    Compression parameter in the Cathode Follower section.\"
    [\[306\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-release-version-14-00.165157/post-1981183){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  (Mid Cut) \"Use a Peak EQ filter at 400 Hz with a Q of 1.4. Decrease
    its Gain until the desired scoop is achieved. Play with the Q to set
    the width of the scoop.\"
    [\[307\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1144887){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"Humans perceive high frequency thermal noise as hiss. The more
    gain the more hiss. Diezel\'s have a lot of filtering. Large grid
    stoppers, plate capacitors, etc. This reduces the bandwidth which
    lowers the hiss. Camerons are pretty much wide open. Small grid
    stoppers or bypass caps on the grid stoppers, no plate caps, etc.\"
    [\[308\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/why-lower-gain-cameron-ccv-amp-model-feels-more-noisy-than-much-higher-gain-herbie-3.188658/post-2339783){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  (MKIII) \"I like it a lot more than the old version of the amp. The
    original Herbert is too dark, fuzzy, compressed and muddy IMO.
    Sounds great playing alone but when I play along with a recording it
    just gets lost. The new Herbert is tighter and sits in the mix
    better.\"
    [\[309\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-firmware-version-21-00-release-candidate-2-beta-8.188778/post-2340412){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#JMPRE-1_CLEAN_1_(Marshall_JMP-1_preamp)}[JMPRE-1 CLEAN 1 (Marshall JMP-1 preamp)]{#JMPRE-1_CLEAN_1_.28Marshall_JMP-1_preamp.29 .mw-headline}

[![Cliff
JMP-1.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/2/27/Cliff_JMP-1.jpg/300px-Cliff_JMP-1.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="90"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/2/27/Cliff_JMP-1.jpg/450px-Cliff_JMP-1.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/2/27/Cliff_JMP-1.jpg/600px-Cliff_JMP-1.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Cliff_JMP-1.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Clean 1
- Clean 1, Bass Shift
- Clean 2
- Clean 2, Bass Shift
- OD1 mode
- OD1 mode, Bass Shift
- OD2 mode
- OD2 mode, Bass Shift

The AM4 has consolidated models with Bass Shift switch

DynaCab match: 4x12 1960TV

Volume, Gain, Bass, Mid, Treble, Presence (preamp), Bass shift, Depth,
P.A. Presence (power amp)

Power tubes: EL34

1.  \"The power amp is based on a typical Marshall 100 watts power amp
    of the same era.\"
2.  \[before firmware 19.02 for the Axe-Fx III\] \"The JMP-1 tone
    controls have more range than the actual preamp. The preamp has
    about +/- 8 dB for each tone control while the model has the
    standard +/- 12 dB.\"
3.  \"Actually a JMP-1 is unique in that the tone controls do not
    interact. Most guitar amps use a passive \"tone stack\" where the
    controls interact. The JMP-1 has a fixed passive tone stack followed
    by an active 4-band EQ.\"
    [\[316\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/is-the-brit-pre-good-enough.132950/#post-1573028){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  (Def Leppard) \"The amp model you are looking for is \"JMPre-1
    OD1\". Some cabs you might like to try with that amp model: Factory
    2 #97 2x12 RECTO V60 57 OH, Factory 2 #995 4x12 UBER V30 57
    OFF-AXIS, Factory 2 #530 4x12 BRIT 70s GB 121 I.\"
    [\[317\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/are-phil-and-viv-using-brit-pre-or-jmpre-1-on-the-iii.139394){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  Firmware 19.02 and later for the Axe-Fx III:
    - Added JMPRE-1 Output EQ type to Amp block. This type replicates
      the active EQ used in the JMP-1 preamp.
    - Added Clean models.
    - The real amp has a fixed, passive tone stack with an active 4-band
      EQ. Therefore, the Bass/Mid/Treble controls when using Authentic
      Tone Controls are mapped to the Graphic EQ. Clean channels only:
      the passive tone stack itself, however, is adjustable. With all
      controls at noon the tone stack is equivalent to the real amp's
      fixed tone stack. You can access these controls using the Ideal
      Tone Controls or via Axe-Edit.

## []{#JR_BLUES_(Fender_Blues_Junior)}[JR BLUES (Fender Blues Junior)]{#JR_BLUES_.28Fender_Blues_Junior.29 .mw-headline}

[![Bluesjr.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/6/6c/Bluesjr.jpg/300px-Bluesjr.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="251"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/6/6c/Bluesjr.jpg/450px-Bluesjr.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/6/6c/Bluesjr.jpg/600px-Bluesjr.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Bluesjr.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Fat switch off
- Fat switch on

The AM4 has a single model with Fat switch

Cab:

- original: Fender 1x12 (Eminence, Jensen C12N, P12R)
- DynaCab: 1x12 Jr Blues

Bass, Middle, Treble, Gain, Volume, FAT button (boosts gain and midrange
frequencies), Reverb effect (not modeled)

Power tubes: EL84

1.  \"The Blues Jr. amp has a fixed presence circuit.\"
    [\[318\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/question-of-proper-axe-eq-values-for-amps-that-dont-have-them.67260/#post-828733){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"They\'re actually pretty decent little amps and sound great when
    cranked.\"
    [\[319\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/forgot-how-loud-tube-amps-are.170551/post-2052934){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The Master Volume in a Blues Jr. is linear taper. This is
    ridiculous as it makes it very difficult to find the sweet spot. The
    model uses an audio taper instead which makes finding the sweet spot
    easier.\"
    [\[320\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/cygnus-is-absolutely-magnificent.173225/post-2096570){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"Blues Jr. is a very colored preamp. The best you can do is turn
    Bass and Treble to zero and Mid all the way up. That will make it
    somewhat flat but you still have the bright cap on the drive and the
    bandpass between the preamp and power amp.\"
    [\[321\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/negative-results-playing-my-fm9-through-a-blues-jr.189057/post-2343390){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  "Our reference amp has a Fender speaker in it. No indication as to
    who makes it but probably Jensen."
    [\[322\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/settings-for-authentic-fender-blues-jr-sound.218510/#post-2751869){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#JS410_CRUNCH_ORANGE_(Joe_Satriani's_Marshall_JVM410HJS)}[JS410 CRUNCH ORANGE (Joe Satriani\'s Marshall JVM410HJS)]{#JS410_CRUNCH_ORANGE_.28Joe_Satriani.27s_Marshall_JVM410HJS.29 .mw-headline}

[![Js.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/c/ce/Js.jpg/350px-Js.jpg){decoding="async"
width="350" height="144"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/c/ce/Js.jpg/525px-Js.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/c/ce/Js.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Js.jpg){.image}

Models of Joe Satriani\'s JVM410HJS:

- Crunch Orange (based on JCM 2203)
- Crunch Red (based on modded JCM 2203)
- Lead Green (bass on OD1 channel on original JVM410H)
- Lead Orange (more gain)
- Lead Red (even more gain)

The AM4 has consolidated models with Mode switch

Cab:

- original: Marshall 4x12 (V30 and G12H)
- DynaCab match: 4x12 Friedman V30

Channel Volume, Gain, Bass, Middle, Treble, Master, Presence, Resonance,
Gate (not modeled), Mid-Shift (off: around 650hz, on: around 500hz)

Mid-Shift is available as a Tonestack type

Power tubes: EL34

1.  \"Joe said he puts all the tone controls at around 10:00.\"
    [\[323\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/jvm-js-in-the-tonestack.109946/#post-1316690){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The JVM has a huge plate resistor on the cathode follower, the JS
    does not.\"
    [\[324\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/jvm-sounding-weird.150157/page-2#post-1785256){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The model is based on Joe\'s personal amp. He sent it to me. When
    I entered the values from the schematic it didn\'t match. The tapers
    of the controls were different and there were some other
    differences. I can only assume that his personal amp is different
    than production models. This is often the case as production models
    are designed to be inexpensive to build (i.e., using control tapers
    that are used in other models to reduce inventory, etc.). Another
    possibility is there were changes made during production. It is not
    uncommon for amps to have changes made to the circuitry over the
    production run. For example, the Blues Jr. has had numerous
    revisions. The first ones sound nothing like the later models. This
    is sometimes done due to perceived customer reaction (\"The amp is
    too dark\" or \"The amp is too harsh\"). Simply adjusting BMT should
    get you what you want. Control tapers make a big difference. For
    example, a Bass pot that is a linear taper would need to be set to
    1.0 to match a Log10A taper at 5.0.\"
    [\[325\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/marshall-jvm410hjs-real-amp-versus-axe3.197259/post-2450481){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  Firmware 23: \"Updated all JS410 Lead models based on a current
    production JVM410HJS. The Crunch models were tested and did not
    require updating.\"
5.  (difference between the production amp and Satriani\'s own amp?)
    \"Yes, they measure quite differently.\"
    [\[326\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-23-00-public-beta-1.198479/post-2467475){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  (firmware 24.00) \"Added Global MV control to JS410 amp models.
    Master Volume has been renamed Channel MV. These two master volume
    controls can be used to balance the tone into the power amp (as in
    the real amp). The Channel MV decreases the high frequencies as it
    is turned down whereas the Global MV is transparent.\"
7.  \"Our models are based on Joe\'s personal amp which is not the same
    as the stock version of the amp. His personal amp is modded and
    considerably darker than stock.\"
    [\[327\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/marshall-jvm410hjs-real-amp-versus-axe3.197259/page-5#post-2669685){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#LEGEND_100_(Steve_Vai's_Carvin_Legacy_VL100)}[LEGEND 100 (Steve Vai\'s Carvin Legacy VL100)]{#LEGEND_100_.28Steve_Vai.27s_Carvin_Legacy_VL100.29 .mw-headline}

[![Legacy.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/4/40/Legacy.jpg/300px-Legacy.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="150"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/4/40/Legacy.jpg/450px-Legacy.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/4/40/Legacy.jpg/600px-Legacy.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Legacy.jpg){.image}

Previously: CALI LEGGY (VL100) and LEGATO 100 (VL300)

Models:

- Legend 100: lead channel of Steve Vai\'s Carvin VL100 Legacy
- Legend 100 II: channel 3 of Carvin VL300 Legacy 3

The AM4 has a single model

Cab:

- original: Carvin 2x12 or 4x12 (V30)
- DynaCab match: 4x12 Friedman V30

VL100: Presence, Treble (11kHz), Mid (650Hz), Bass (80Hz), Drive, Volume

VL300: Bass, Middle, Treble, Presence, Drive, Volume, Master, Boost (not
modeled), Reverb effect (not modeled), Gain switch (not modeled)

Power tubes: EL34

1.  \"The thing that makes a Legacy unique is the tone stack. It uses a
    \"James\" tone stack which is more like hi-fi tone controls.\"
    [\[328\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/thank-you-fractal-for-the-leggy-legacy-model-its-great.47586/#post-620139){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"Adds the \"Legato 100\" model based on Steve Vai\'s Legacy 100.
    This model is unique in that it uses a Baxandall (sometimes called a
    \"James\") tone stack. More often used on tube hi-fi gear the
    controls are less interactive than a typical guitar amp tone stack
    and impart a different tonal quality.\"
    [\[329\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-ii-quantum-rev-4-01-beta.119527/){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The Legato 100 is based on a one-of-a-kind version owned by a
    certain Californian guitar player. It is a very dark amp. Part of
    this is due to the tapers on the tone pots. With everything at noon
    the tone stack looks like a highshelf with a good amount of high
    frequency cut. The tone stack is a Baxandall which is more common in
    hi-fi gear than guitar amps. It lends a unique character to the
    tone.\"
    [\[330\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1426142){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"SV\'s personal settings are: Drive: 7.5, Bass: 6, Mid: 4, Treble:
    8, Presence: 8. I had to increase the Mid control on the model to
    about 5 to match the amp which indicates the mid pot on the amp was
    greater than spec. This is not unusual. Typical consumer-grade pots
    have pretty poor tolerance in both end-to-end resistance and
    resistance at the midpoint.\"
    [\[331\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1429558){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"Legend II is channel 3 from the Legacy 3.\"
    [\[332\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-12-cygnus-firmware-public-release-candidate.172027/post-2075753){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"What is happening is the power amp is oscillating at that very low
    frequency cabinet resonance. This occurs because the Legacy has so
    much negative feedback (12 dB, which is the highest of any amp I\'ve
    ever modeled). Combined with the smallish output transformer there
    is a loss of phase margin at low frequencies which causes the power
    amp to become unstable. The Rumble cab is unique in that it is
    ported and has two different types of speakers in it. This causes a
    double resonance and one of the resonances is at a very low
    frequency. For typical power amps with reasonable amounts of
    feedback this isn\'t an issue.\"
    [\[333\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/bizzare-yet-interesting-legend-amp-model-possible-issue.173492/post-2101586){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  \"The tonestack in a Legacy is a James. A Baxandall is active.\"
    [\[334\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/have-we-reached-the-end-of-new-amp-models-in-the-axe-3.184271/post-2483056){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#MATCHBOX_CHIEFTAIN_1_(Matchless_Chieftain)}[MATCHBOX CHIEFTAIN 1 (Matchless Chieftain)]{#MATCHBOX_CHIEFTAIN_1_.28Matchless_Chieftain.29 .mw-headline}

[![Chieftain.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/c/c0/Chieftain.jpg/300px-Chieftain.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="244"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/c/c0/Chieftain.jpg/450px-Chieftain.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/c/c0/Chieftain.jpg/600px-Chieftain.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Chieftain.jpg){.image}

Previously: BOUTIQUE 1 and BOUTIQUE 2

Models:

- Single channel
- Boosted (more gain and high-frequency emphasis)

The AM4 has a single model

Cab:

- original: Matchless 2x12 (G12H)
- DynaCab match: 2x12 Chiefman

Volume, Master, Bass, Mid, Treble, Brilliance

Power tubes: EL34

No negative feedback

1.  \"The secret of the Chieftain is the split cathode bias. Most
    \"Class-A\" amps use a shared cathode bias but the Chieftain uses
    separate cathode bias networks which results in less bias shift so
    there\'s less fizz.\"
    [\[335\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-release-version-12-03.158240/post-1895726){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The Treble control in a Chieftain is actually a \"Preamp
    Presence\" control, similar to the Presence control in a Dual
    Rectifier in Modern mode. It is separate from the tone stack and
    located later in the gain stages. The tone stack has no treble
    control.\"
    [\[336\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-firmware-version-21-00.189017/post-2344358){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#MATCHBOX_D-30_(Matchless_DC-30)}[MATCHBOX D-30 (Matchless DC-30)]{#MATCHBOX_D-30_.28Matchless_DC-30.29 .mw-headline}

[![Dc30.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/7/7c/Dc30.jpg/300px-Dc30.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="249"
srcset="/wiki/images/7/7c/Dc30.jpg 1.5x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Dc30.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Channel 1 D-30 (12AX7 preamp tubes)
- Channel 2 D-30 EF86 (EF86 preamp tubes)

Cab:

- original: Matchless 2x12 (25w G12M and 30w G12H)
- DynaCab match: 2x12 Chiefman

Channel 1: Volume, Bass, Treble, Cut, bypassable Master

Channel 2: Volume, Tone, Cut, bypassable Master

On the AM4, the Master control is provided, on other products it isn\'t
(bypassed)

Power tubes: EL84

No negative feedback

1.  \"The DC-30 is basically an AC-30 copy. The voltages are a bit
    different but the topology is nearly identical. However, IMO, it
    does sound better. Not sure why. Perhaps the better quality
    components. AC-30\'s have kind of crappy OTs.\"
    [\[337\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/968982){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  (channel 2) \"The switch selects the coupling capacitor between the
    EF86 and the volume pot.\"
    [\[338\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-ii-quantum-rev-9-00-beta.130981/page-11#post-1552400){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"Added "Matchbox D-30 EF86" amp model. While the real amp has a
    six-position Tone switch, the model has a continuously variable tone
    control. Note that the Tone control is mapped to the Bass control in
    Ideal mode as the Tone switch is essentially a bass cut control.\"
4.  "The new DC-30 model may have dethroned the mighty AC-20 as my
    favorite \"Class A\" model."
    [\[339\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-version-11-01.156108/post-1858859){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"EL-84 amps are not known for being clean. They are typically
    biased as \"Class-A\" using cathode biasing and no feedback. The
    power amp transfer function is therefore very nonlinear resulting in
    distortion even at low input levels. You can clean up the power amp
    by increasing the Negative Feedback.\"
    [\[340\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/cleaner-headroom-for-matchbox-d-30.215313/page-3#post-2705507){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  (about DC-30 jumpered model) \"It\'s not going to happen. The
    hardware isn\'t powerful enough to run two preamp simulations
    simultaneously.\"
    [\[341\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/i-come-to-you-once-again-asking-for.216780/#post-2726238){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#MR_Z_MZ-38_(Dr._Z_Maz_38_SR)}[MR Z MZ-38 (Dr. Z Maz 38 SR)]{#MR_Z_MZ-38_.28Dr._Z_Maz_38_SR.29 .mw-headline}

[![Maz38.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/9/9d/Maz38.jpg/300px-Maz38.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="241"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/9/9d/Maz38.jpg/450px-Maz38.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/9/9d/Maz38.jpg/600px-Maz38.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Maz38.jpg){.image}

Cab:

- original: Dr. Z 1x12 (G12H)
- DynaCab match: 1x12 AC20

Volume, Master, Bass, Mid, Treble, Cut, Reverb effect on some models
(not modeled)

Power tubes: EL84

No negative feedback

1.  \"Dr. Z is the quintessential country amp.\"
    [\[342\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/828934){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}\"
2.  \"IMO the designs are poor because\... wait for it\... they exhibit
    a papery buzz. The problem with most cathode biased Class A amps is,
    1: they aren\'t really Class A (more like hot Class AB) and 2: They
    go into Class B operation when they are overdriven. The cathode
    capacitor charges up and the bias point shifts dramatically. This
    causes lots of crossover distortion (papery buzz). It\'s worse on
    lower notes because lower notes have more energy and charge the cap
    more. The is probably the reason Leo Fender switched to fixed bias
    amps with negative feedback. Fixed bias is just that, the bias point
    is fixed so the amp doesn\'t shift into Class B operation when
    overdriven (not as much anyways, depends on the bias circuit, grid
    stoppers, etc.). Negative feedback linearizes the amp and reduces
    the crossover distortion (at the expense of gain). That\'s why the
    buzzing went away when you increased negative feedback. Crossover
    distortion is a unique sound. For cleaner sounds it tends to be
    objectionable. For overdriven sounds some find it desirable. EVH
    ostensibly liked his amps biased cold to get some crossover
    distortion. There are even some amps that have circuits to
    intentionally generate crossover distortion. Some distortion pedals
    also do this. Lowering the Cathode Resistance reduces the crossover
    distortion as it keeps the amp in Class A operation longer but the
    tubes run hotter and don\'t last as long. This is not a problem with
    our virtual amps though. I forget the actual values but I\'m pretty
    certain if you look at the Cathode Resistance value for those amps
    it\'s pretty high. This means the amps are biased somewhat cold to
    begin with and shift to very cold as soon as overdriven. Then
    there\'s shared vs. split cathode. If you look at the schematics on
    the web the Maz-38 is shared cathode. I could never get the model to
    sound exactly like our reference amp. Finally I traced the entire
    circuit and our particular amp is a split cathode. As soon as I
    changed the model to split cathode it was spot on. This is not
    exposed to the user though (there\'s a hidden shared/split switch).
    Our particular amp says \"Humbucker\" inside the chassis. Not sure
    if the difference in the cathode circuit is because Dr. Z likes
    split cathode for humbucking guitars or what.\"
    [\[343\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/papery-buzz-under-some-models.149193/page-2#post-1772639){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#MR_Z_MZ-8_(Dr._Z_Maz_8)}[MR Z MZ-8 (Dr. Z Maz 8)]{#MR_Z_MZ-8_.28Dr._Z_Maz_8.29 .mw-headline}

[![Maz8.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/1/1a/Maz8.jpg/300px-Maz8.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="148"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/1/1a/Maz8.jpg/450px-Maz8.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/1/1a/Maz8.jpg/600px-Maz8.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Maz8.jpg){.image}

Cab:

- original: Dr. Z 1x12 (G12H)
- DynaCab match: 1x12 AC20

Volume, Master, Bass, Mid, Treble, Cut, Reverb effect (not modeled),
Pentode/Triode switch (not modeled)

Power tubes: EL84

No negative feedback

1.  \"Dr. Z is the quintessential country amp.\"
    [\[344\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/828934){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#NUCLEAR-TONE_(Swart_Atomic_Space_Tone)}[NUCLEAR-TONE (Swart Atomic Space Tone)]{#NUCLEAR-TONE_.28Swart_Atomic_Space_Tone.29 .mw-headline}

[![Swart.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/1/16/Swart.jpg/300px-Swart.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="222"
srcset="/wiki/images/1/16/Swart.jpg 1.5x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Swart.jpg){.image}

Single channel model

Cab:

- original: Swart 1x12 (Mojotone BV-25m)
- DynaCab match: 1x12 Nuclear Tone

Volume, Tone, Tremolo effect, Reverb effect (not modeled)

Power tubes: 6V6

No negative feedback

1.  \"It\'s unique character comes from the PI. It\'s a cathodyne phase
    inverter so it doesn\'t drive the grids as hard.\"
    [\[345\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/828241){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The real amp is known for it\'s tremolo so that\'s why we used the
    bias trem on the preset. Bias trem works by modulating the power
    tube grid bias. One of the side-effects is that the effect becomes
    less pronounced as you play harder which makes it basically \"auto
    ducking\". Also since it\'s modulating the bias it gives an almost
    Univibe like effect since the phase changes a bit too.\"
    [\[346\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/patch-62-nuclear-tone-weird-tremolo-effect.122258/#post-1454602){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#ODS-100_CLEAN_(Dumble_Overdrive_Special)}[ODS-100 CLEAN (Dumble Overdrive Special)]{#ODS-100_CLEAN_.28Dumble_Overdrive_Special.29 .mw-headline}

[![Dumble.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/c/c3/Dumble.jpg/300px-Dumble.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="141"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/c/c3/Dumble.jpg/450px-Dumble.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/c/c3/Dumble.jpg/600px-Dumble.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Dumble.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Clean: clean channel of ODS-100 Ford
- Ford: based on schematics of Robben Ford\'s #102 Dumble, Overdrive
  channel, Pre Amp Boost (PAB): off
- Ford PAB: same as Ford model, PAB ON (bypasses the tone controls), Mid
  switch: off
- Ford PAB Mid: same as Ford model, PAB ON, Mid switch (Deep): on
- HRM: based on HRM circuit, Overdrive channel, Mid switch (Deep): off
- HRM Mid: based on HRM circuit, Overdrive channel, Mid switch (Deep):
  on

Cab:

- original: Dumble 2x12 or 4x12 (G12-65, EVM)
- DynaCab: 4x12 Rumble EV12L

Volume (Clean), Bass, Middle, Treble, Overdrive Level, Overdrive Ratio,
Master, Presence, Bright switch, Mid boost switch (Deep), Jazz/Rock
switch (not modeled), foot switchable Pre Amp Boost (PAB)

Power tubes: EL34 (HRM), 6L6 (Ford)

1.  \"The ODS100 has two drive controls, one is right at the input, the
    other is in the lead boost section.\"
2.  \"I hate to admit it but there is something special about a real
    Dumble. I don\'t know what it is but there is something in the
    voicing. The various clones I have are cool and have their own thing
    going but they don\'t sound like the Dumble. Hard amp to play
    though. Very unforgiving but tremendous clarity.\"
    [\[347\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/824398){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"They call HRM \"Hot Rubber Monkey\" but what it really means is
    \"Hot Rod Marshall\".\" The HRM Dumbles have a fixed Marshall tone
    stack at the output of the lead channel. This gives a little scoop
    to the mids.\"
    [\[348\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/828279){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"My Dumble is S/N 0213 IIRC. It\'s an EL-34 ODS HRM.\"
    [\[349\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1170559){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"The ODS-100 Ford 2 model is not based on the HRM model with the
    HRM tonestack removed. Whether or not the model matches any
    particular Dumble is unknown as we have not been able to procure a
    non-HRM Dumble yet. The model is based on schematics that were given
    to us that supposedly accurately represent Robben Ford\'s Dumble.
    Whether or not the schematics are accurate I do not know. The
    voltage divider at the output of V1B is set to 0.078 which is based
    on the values that are indicated on the schematic for the set-point
    of the trimmer. As no two Dumbles are identical it stands to reason
    that one person\'s interpretation of the ideal Dumble voicing may
    not agree with another\'s. Since V1 is running clean you can get
    more gain by simply increasing Input Trim. It will have basically
    the same effect as increasing the trimmer.\"
6.  \"A signal divider, which is more correctly called a voltage
    divider, is calculated by taking the resistance to ground divided by
    the sum of the resistances. In this case the voltage divider would
    be 26.7/317 = 0.084. This is very close to the values that we were
    given (which yield 0.078). Our model also uses local feedback on V1B
    (which is about 2-3 dB less gain) and accounts for the voltage
    divider\'s affect on the AC load line. In fact all stages in a
    Dumble typically have an AC load-line that\'s different than the DC
    load-line due to the load resistance being significant in relation
    to the plate resistor. Since V1A and V1B run clean (linear) Input
    Trim will accomplish the same thing as increasing the trimmer into
    the drive stages. This is because a linear system is commutative
    (see any introductory Signals and Systems text for properties of
    linear systems). The commutative property is where A x B = B x A.
    Therefore it does not matter if the gain is before or after the
    linear stages.\"
7.  \"The Mid switch, sometimes labeled \"Deep\", shorts out the 390 pF
    cap in the tone stack (which is in series with a 2 nF cap). All that
    is left then is the 2 nF cap. With PAB active this lowers the lowcut
    frequency.\"
    [\[350\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/dumbles-in-q2.110382/#post-1321445){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
8.  \"Maybe the best clean model IMO. You have to really crank the MV
    though (just like the real amp).\"
    [\[351\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-ii-quantum-rev-8-00-public-beta.126728/page-7#post-1507967){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
9.  \"The only amps with a bright cap on the MV are Dumbles and their
    various clones/derivatives. This was/is done to compensate for the
    lack of a buffer for the fx loop. The loop send is taken right off
    the MV which means the output impedance is very high. Any
    significant length of cable will then attenuate the highs due to the
    cable capacitance. The bright cap boosts the highs to compensate.
    It\'s the same idea as a bright cap on your guitar\'s volume knob.
    Crude. FWIW, this is a terrible loop design but \"it\'s a Dumble\"
    so it\'s all part of the mystique. Dumble then released the
    \"Dumbleator\" which is nothing more than a buffer and recovery in
    an external box. Dumble fanatics, of course, claim that to have the
    true Dumble experience you MUST use the Dumbleator which is just
    another load of BS.\"
    [\[352\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/pick-attack.137945/#post-1720592){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
10. \"We actually own a real Dumble. I bought it off a lawyer (surprise,
    surprise) some years ago who was in trouble with the IRS. Also a
    matching 4x12 cab. Both in mint condition. At the time I paid \$50K
    for both. Probably worth twice that now.\"
    [\[353\]](https://www.thegearpage.net/board/index.php?threads/modelers-with-accurate-dumble-models.2120479/page-7#post-30771582){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
11. \"PAB disconnects some components in the tone stack. The treble cap
    is still in the circuit path.\"
    [\[354\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/ods-pab.180951/#post-2215259){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
12. Firmware 21: \"Added "Overdrive Volume" parameter to Dumble-type amp
    models (ODS-100, Two Stone, etc.). This is sometimes labeled "Ratio"
    or "Lead Master". As the Master Volume on these amps often has a
    bright capacitor the Overdrive Volume control allows setting the
    Master Volume higher to counteract the bright cap and then lowering
    the power amp drive with the Volume.\"
13. \"Most, if not all, Dumble-style amps have a Ratio/Volume/Lead
    Master/etc. control so this makes the models complete in that
    regard. My Fuchs ODS 50 does NOT have a bright cap on the MV but it
    has an \"Output\" control for the overdrive channel that is in
    series with MV.\"
    \[[https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-firmware-version-21-00-public-beta-2-beta-2.187991/post-2331157](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-firmware-version-21-00-public-beta-2-beta-2.187991/post-2331157){.external
    .free target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
14. \"The Dumble tone stack is the same as Plexi except it is plate
    driven instead of cathode follower driven. The increased source
    impedance increases the insertion loss. The insertion loss also
    increases more at higher frequencies.\"
    [\[355\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/modeling-questions.199009/post-2528617){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
    [\[356\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/modeling-questions.199009/page-8#post-2528896){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
15. (ODS Clean) \"The default tone stack for this model is a Skyliner
    with location set to \"Mid\". This matches the reference amp. The
    frequency is arbitrary, it\'s just a reference value and if you
    don\'t change it the tone stack is accurate. Regardless, the notch
    frequency is approx. 422 Hz so the value of 400 Hz is appropriate.\"
    [\[357\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/tone-stack-in-ods-models.205711/#post-2566292){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## [ODS-100 FORD]{#ODS-100_FORD .mw-headline}

## [ODS-100 FORD PAB]{#ODS-100_FORD_PAB .mw-headline}
