------------------------------------------------------------------------

Regarding the following PLEXI models:

1.  \"One of the first mods people make to real \'Plexi\' Marshalls is
    to \"clip the bright cap\". The bright cap varied over the years,
    supposedly depending on what was lying around in the shop. The model
    defaults to the bright cap in the circuit. If you turn off Bright
    you\'re effectively clipping the bright cap. The bright cap in
    Marshalls can be very bright and harsh. However, if you crank the
    Master you might find the extra brightness helps compensate for the
    power amp getting darker.\"
2.  \"It\'s the way a Plexi is supposed to sound. That\'s due to the
    cathode follower. That raspiness helps it cut through in a mix. I
    own three of them and they are that fizzy.\"
    [\[358\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/576475){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"Don\'t be afraid to turn the bass all the way down or the treble
    all the way up. Just like with the actual amp. For example, on the
    Normal channel of a Plexi most people turn the bass way down.
    Otherwise it\'s too flubby.\"
    [\[359\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/577248){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"My settings for a \"typical\" Plexi tone are Bass: 2, Mid: 8,
    Treble 7.5. Adjust Presence to taste.\"
    [\[360\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1179420){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  (Boston/Rockman sound) \"Plexi Jump. Everything on 7. Put a Filter
    block in front: Type: Peaking, Freq: \~800 Hz, Q: 0.707, Gain 12
    dB.\"
6.  \"What you are hearing is output transformer high frequency
    resonance. Old Plexis didn\'t do this because they had good
    transformers. New transformers are crappy and resonate at the cutoff
    frequency because they are underdamped. This causes a raspy, fizzy
    texture to the distortion. The transformer resonance is adjustable
    but the parameter isn\'t exposed to the user. When you turn it up
    you get that same squishy rasp that you are hearing. For the Plexis
    I have the damping set to flat with no resonance because that\'s how
    our vintage Plexis measure. Our 50W is a little underdamped but
    people complain about raspy high frequencies so I erred on the safe
    side.\"
    [\[361\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/dimed-real-plexi-vs-dimed-simulation-q8-01.127161/page-2#post-1513888){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  \"When modding Marshalls for higher gain sometimes the modder will
    decrease the input frequency response to reduce noise and fizziness.
    You can do this by reducing the high-cut frequency in the input EQ.
    Or you can use a high-shelf filter which is a little more subtle.
    Another technique is to put a capacitor across the second-to-last
    triode stage. This is the \"Triode 1 Plate Freq\" parameter. Reduce
    this to around 2 kHz to start which is typical of amps like an
    SLO100, etc.\"
    [\[362\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/dialling-in-the-marshalls.143682/post-1707222){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
8.  \"All the distortion comes from the power amp so the tone controls
    don\'t do much.\"
    [\[363\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-4-cygnus-firmware-public-beta.170253/post-2052743){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
9.  \"The following models have the 0.68uF cap on the second triode:
    [\[364\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-firmware-version-20-05-public-beta-beta-1.187133/page-4#post-2317922){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
    - Plexi 50W Normal
    - Plexi 50W High 2
    - Plexi 50W Jumped
    - Brit Brown
    - Plexi 100W Normal
    - Plexi 100W High
    - Plexi 100W Jumped
    - Plexi 100W 1970
    - 1959SLP Normal
    - 1959SLP Treble
    - 1959SLP Jumped\"

## []{#PLEXI_100W_1970_(1970_100W_Marshall_Plexi)}[PLEXI 100W 1970 (1970 100W Marshall Plexi)]{#PLEXI_100W_1970_.281970_100W_Marshall_Plexi.29 .mw-headline}

[![SLP.png](/wiki/images/thumb/d/d5/SLP.png/300px-SLP.png){decoding="async"
width="300" height="171"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/d/d5/SLP.png/450px-SLP.png 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/d/d5/SLP.png/600px-SLP.png 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:SLP.png){.image}

Models:

- 1970 100 watts, EL34, jumpered channels
- 1969 100 watts, High Treble channel
- 1969 100 watts, jumpered channels
- 1969 100 watts, Normal channel
- 1972 50 watts, 6550 power tubes
- 6AC7 50 watts, 6AC7 power tubes
- 1981 50 watts JMP with master volume, EL34
- 1967 50 watts, EL34, High Treble channel (\"High 1\")
- 1967 50 watts, EL34, High Treble channel (\"High 2\") (2nd triode
  stage has a 0.68uF cathode bypass capacitor, which was added in the
  early 70's and gives a slightly brighter tone)
- 1967 50 watts, EL34, jumpered channels
- 1967 50 watts, EL34, Normal channel

Cab:

- original: Marshall 4x12 (G12M, G12H)
- DynaCab: 4x12 1960TV

Volume Normal / Volume Treble, Bass, Middle, Treble, Presence, Master
(Plexi 2204 only)

Power tubes: EL34

1.  \"1970 Marshall 1959SLP 100 has a darker, smoother sound than
    earlier Plexis.\"
2.  \"Try the Plexi 100W 1970 with Factory Cab 54. Be sure to dial it in
    like you would in 1970, i.e. turn the Mid, Treble and Presence way
    up; turn Norm Drive and Bass down a bit.\"
    [\[365\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-ii-quantum-2-00-public-beta-deux.109702/#post-1312811){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"I\'ve never cared for that model nor the actual amp. IMO it
    doesn\'t have enough feedback (100K off the 4-ohm tap). Some amps of
    that era had 47K off the 4-ohm tap. Some had 47K off the 8-ohm tap.
    Some had 100K off the 8-ohm tap and some even had 47K off the 16-ohm
    tap! IOW all over the map. Bottom line: try adjusting Negative
    Feedback. I always raise it up a bit with that model. Around 4 or
    so.\"
    [\[366\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/plexi-100watt-1970-is-something-wrong-with-it-now.125522/#post-1493932){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"The Plexi 100W 1970 model is a non-MV \"Plexi\". Circuit is
    slightly different than the late 60\'s model (Plexi 100W).\"
    [\[367\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/marshall-amp-question.155223/post-1847908){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"The 1970 model has less negative feedback.\"
    [\[368\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/modeling-questions.199009/post-2528926){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"There\'s a 0.68uF cap on the second triode.\"
    [\[369\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-firmware-version-20-05-public-beta-beta-1.187133/post-2317922){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

[Forum discussion about the Plexi 2204
model](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/late-70s-marshall-jmp-master-model-50w-mk2-lead.135541){.external
.text target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

Power tubes: EL34

1.  \"Just scored a \'69 SLP 100.\"

    [\[372\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/marshall-jmp-100w.198803/post-2478167){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"All the pots are log pots in our reference amp\" and \"I was
    puzzled by the pot tapers but they all look original. I then thought
    about it a bit and wondered if that\'s why Bogner uses log pots for
    his amps. His stuff is definitely Plexi-inspired. Or maybe all
    Marshall could find at the surplus electronics store that week was
    log pots. Who knows.\"
    [\[373\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/modeling-questions.199009/post-2491180){.external

    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  \"1959 circuit.\"
    [\[376\]](https://www.facebook.com/photo.php?fbid=10151759408979517&set=a.10151759408834517.621839.312081419516&type=1&theater){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
8.  \"Marshall amps in those days were wildly inconsistent. There are
    conflicting reports of the tone stacks. Our reference amp has log
    pots. George Metropolous says most of the amps he\'s seen had log
    pots. Some people claim linear pots were more prevalent.\"
    [\[377\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/modeling-questions.199009/post-2528926){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
9.  \"Our reference 100W Plexi is sort of in between 1968 and 1969. It
    has an 820 ohm cathode resistor on V1B. Coupling cap is 2.2n.
    Feedback is 47K off the speaker jack (!!!). The model assumes a full
    stack w/ (2) 16-ohm cabs so that would equivalent to 8-ohm tap.\"
    [\[378\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/modeling-questions.199009/post-2528947){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
10. \"Our reference Plexi 100 has log taper tone pots. If you want a
    more conventional 100W Plexi sound use the 1959SLP models.\"
    [\[379\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/plexi-100-very-blanketed-now.205645/#post-2565083){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
11. \"Our reference amp has a 560p treble cap and a 10A treble pot
    taper. Both components appear to be original. The tech who checked
    it out after I bought it said it was one of the best sounding 100W
    Plexis he\'d ever heard. That tech just happens to be Alan Phillips
    of Carol-Ann Amps. So I modeled it to agree with the reference
    amp.\"
    [\[380\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/modeling-questions.199009/post-2491136){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
12. \"The default tone stack for the Plexi 100W is Plexi 100W. The
    equivalent tone stack w/ linear mid and treble pots is Plexi. The
    Dumble tone stack is the same as Plexi except it is plate driven
    instead of cathode follower driven.\"
    [\[381\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/modeling-questions.199009/post-2528617){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#PLEXI_2204_(1981_50W_Marshall_JMP_2204)}[PLEXI 2204 (1981 50W Marshall JMP 2204)]{#PLEXI_2204_.281981_50W_Marshall_JMP_2204.29 .mw-headline}

This amp/model has a master volume control

Power tubes: EL34

1.  \"Based on a 1981 JMP 50W Master Volume head.\"
2.  \"Everything on 10.\"
3.  \"There were several versions of the \"2204\" Plexi. Our model is
    based on a 1981 2204 Master Volume JMP. It has a different circuit
    than a JCM800.\"
    [\[382\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/marshall-sound-clips.169296/post-2034903){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"The model is based on the Hi input of a 1981 50W Master Volume
    \"2204\" Plexi. There were two versions of the 2204. One was
    essentially a Plexi with a Master Volume. Similar to a 1987x but
    with some different values and voltages in addition to the MV. The
    other was virtually identical to a JCM800. The model is the Plexi
    version. Mine is an \'81 and doesn\'t have cascaded gain stages.\"
    [\[383\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/plexi-2204-question.178464/){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"It\'s a 1981 \"CSA\" 2204.\"
    [\[384\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/plexi-2204-question.178464/post-2175316){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"It\'s a Master Volume Plexi. Turn the MV up to get more
    distortion. Or put a pedal in front like people did in those days.\"
    [\[385\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-27-03-public-beta.209954/page-9#post-2625397){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  \"There were two versions of the 2204. One was a \"Plexi\" with a
    master volume. The other was essentially a JCM800 in a smaller
    chassis. The JCM800 version is more common.\"
    [\[386\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-27-03-public-beta.209954/page-9#post-2625472){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#PLEXI_50W_6CA7_(50W_Marshall_Plexi)}[PLEXI 50W 6CA7 (50W Marshall Plexi)]{#PLEXI_50W_6CA7_.2850W_Marshall_Plexi.29 .mw-headline}

## [PLEXI 50W HIGH 2]{#PLEXI_50W_HIGH_2 .mw-headline}

1.  \"Similar to Plexi 50W High 1 except the second triode stage has a
    0.68uF cathode bypass capacitor. The second bypass capacitor was
    added in the early 70's and gives a slightly brighter tone.\"
2.  \"There\'s a 0.68uF cap on the second triode.\"
    [\[388\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-firmware-version-20-05-public-beta-beta-1.187133/post-2317922){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

    network is JCM800-style.\"
    [\[389\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/modeling-questions.199009/page-3#post-2491179){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

    the normal channel removed.\"

    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

    way. This was a common mod for people who only used the High
    input.\"

## [PLEXI 50W JUMPED]{#PLEXI_50W_JUMPED .mw-headline}

## [PLEXI 50W NORMAL]{#PLEXI_50W_NORMAL .mw-headline}

1.  \"There\'s a 0.68uF cap on the second triode.\"
    [\[392\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-firmware-version-20-05-public-beta-beta-1.187133/post-2317922){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The topology of that model does not support a bright cap and the
    actual amp has no bright cap.\"
    [\[393\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/q2-01-plexi-50w-nrml-bright-cap-doesnt-work.111836/#post-1337410){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#PVH_6160_BLOCK_(Peavey_\"Block_Letter\"_EVH_5150)}[PVH 6160 BLOCK (Peavey \"Block Letter\" EVH 5150)]{#PVH_6160_BLOCK_.28Peavey_.22Block_Letter.22_EVH_5150.29 .mw-headline}

[![5150.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/7/7c/5150.jpg/300px-5150.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="103"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/7/7c/5150.jpg/450px-5150.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/7/7c/5150.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:5150.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Clean channel (firmware 32.05)
- Rhythm channel, Crunch switch engaged
- Lead channel

Cab:

- original: Peavey 4x12 (Sheffield 1200)
- DynaCab match: 4x12 5153

Pre Gain, Post Gain (Master), Low, Mid, High, Resonance/Depth, Presence,
Bright switch (Rhythm channel only), Crunch switch (Rhythm channel only)

Power tubes: 6L6

1.  \"I have a \"holy grail\" Block Letter 5150 (supposedly). It sounds
    way better than most 5150s for some reason which is a good thing for
    you guys. I think it\'s partly due to the fact that it has a bias
    mod so it\'s biased a bit warmer than a stock version.\"
    [\[397\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1152978){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"Another technique is to use negative feedback to the grid. This is
    done in 5150-based designs which makes the stage clip even harder.
    The last stage of a 5150 basically looks like a diode clipper. The
    harder the clipping the more overtones that are created and the
    better the tone cuts. Without those overtones your sound is lost in
    the mix.\"
    [\[398\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/fizz-is-good.67719/#post-833875){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  (Peavey 5150 vs 6505) \"There are differences. The input gain
    network is different and the coupling cap after the second triode
    stage is a different value.\"
    [\[399\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/peavey-invective-killer-amp.172625/post-2088479){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#PVH_6160+_CLEAN_(Peavey_6505+_/_EVH_5150-II)}[PVH 6160+ CLEAN (Peavey 6505+ / EVH 5150-II)]{#PVH_6160.2B_CLEAN_.28Peavey_6505.2B_.2F_EVH_5150-II.29 .mw-headline}

[![6505.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/a/af/6505.jpg/300px-6505.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="115"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/a/af/6505.jpg/450px-6505.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/a/af/6505.jpg/600px-6505.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:6505.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Clean channel, Bright switch off
- Clean channel, Bright switch on
- Crunch channel, Bright switch off
- Crunch channel, Bright switch on
- Lead channel

Cab:

- original: Peavey 4x12 (V30)
- DynaCab match: 4x12 5153

Rhythm channel: Pre (gain), Bright switch (6dB at 2kHz, not on Lead
channel), Crunch switch, Low, Mid, High, Post (Master), Resonance/Depth,
Presence

Lead channel: Pre (gain), Low, Mid, High, Post (Master), Resonance,
Presence

Power tubes: 6L6

1.  \"Chris Quigley\'s 6505 was the reference amp. It\'s my amp now.
    It\'s a very good sounding one.\"
    [\[400\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/824411){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  (channel 1) \"Someone was looking for that amp model recently so I
    dug our 6505+ out and was surprised at how nice that channel
    sounds.\"
    [\[401\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-ii-quantum-rev-1-03-firmware-release.106931/#post-1278700){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"A 6505+ is identical to a 5150 except it has no bright cap. Use
    the 5150 model and turn off the bright switch.\"
    [\[402\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/request-acoustic-peavy-6505.56527/#post-711922){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"The Bright switch on clean and crunch channels does not engage a
    capacitor on the drive potentiometer as is typical but instead
    disengages a treble cut circuit.\"

## []{#PVH_6160+_CLEAN_BRIGHT}[PVH 6160+ CLEAN BRIGHT]{#PVH_6160.2B_CLEAN_BRIGHT .mw-headline}

## []{#RECTO1_ORANGE_MODERN_(MESA_Dual_Rectifier,_2_channels)}[RECTO1 ORANGE MODERN (MESA Dual Rectifier, 2 channels)]{#RECTO1_ORANGE_MODERN_.28MESA_Dual_Rectifier.2C_2_channels.29 .mw-headline}

[![Recto.png](/wiki/images/thumb/0/00/Recto.png/300px-Recto.png){decoding="async"
width="300" height="140"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/0/00/Recto.png/450px-Recto.png 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/0/00/Recto.png/600px-Recto.png 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Recto.png){.image}

Models:

- Recto1: original 2-channel Rectifier, Orange channel, Modern mode
- Recto1: original 2-channel Rectifier, Orange channel, Vintage mode
- Recto1: original 2-channel Rectifier, Red channel, Modern mode
- Recto2: later 3-channel Rectifier, Orange channel, Modern mode
- Recto2: later 3-channel Rectifier, Orange channel, Vintage mode
- Recto2: later 3-channel Rectifier, Red channel, Modern mode
- Recto2: later 3-channel Rectifier, Red channel, Vintage mode

Cab:

- original: Mesa 4x12 (V30)
- DynaCab match: 4x12 Recto Straight

Gain, Master, Bass, Middle, Treble, Presence, Supply Sag

Use the Supply Sag control to simulate solid-state rectifier (reduce) or
tube rectifier (increase).

Power tubes: 6L6

Modern modes: no negative feedback

1.  \"The reason you\'re hearing the highs rolled off is because the
    Master is too high. As you increase the Master the highs get
    muffled. 7.02 for the Recto Master is ridiculous and will sound like
    crap.\"
    [\[403\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-vs-tube-amps-my-first-experience.27192/page-3#post-412068){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"Note that the Orange Modern and Red Modern models have no negative
    feedback and therefore the Presence control is a Hi Cut control.\"
    [\[404\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/version-10-00-stuff.63202/#post-783037){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"A typical Recto cabinet has a resonant frequency a little over 100
    Hz.\"
    [\[405\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/dual-recto-with-the-lb-2-vs-the-axe-fx-iii-and-more.143501/page-2#post-1699892){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"The unique thing about a Dual Recto tone stack is that the
    Presence control is part of the tone stack. So the Recto tone
    controls also interact with the presence control.\"
    [\[406\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/dual-recto-with-the-lb-2-vs-the-axe-fx-iii-and-more.143501/#post-1699011){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"Rectos don\'t have a Depth control and even if they did it
    wouldn\'t do anything in Modern Red mode since that mode has no
    negative feedback. When you put a Recto into Modern Red mode it
    opens a relay which removes the NFB.\"
    [\[407\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/recto-depth.92482/#post-1111780){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"Real Rectos are bassy/fizzy beasts but that tone works great for
    certain genres.\"
    [\[408\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/658849){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  \"If you are using the Modern modes be very careful with the MV. If
    you turn it up too high it will flub out really quick. If in doubt
    reduce the MV. Compensate with the Level control.\"
    [\[409\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/829334){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
8.  \"The Modern mode in Rectos has no negative feedback so there\'s a
    huge bass boost from the speaker impedance. Fortunately you can
    reduce this by reducing the LF Resonance on the Spkr tab which is
    something you can\'t do with the real amp without trying different
    speakers or cabinet.\"
    [\[410\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/829906){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
9.  \"Depth works by varying the negative feedback at low frequencies.
    There is no NFB in the Modern Red mode so the Depth knob won\'t do
    anything.\"
    [\[411\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1111770){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
10. \"All passive tone controls interact and all the Axe-Fx tone stacks
    replicate this behavior. The unique thing about a Dual Recto tone
    stack is that the Presence control is part of the tone stack. So the
    Recto tone controls also interact with the presence control.\"
    [\[412\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/dual-recto-eq-potentially-silly-question.93890/#post-1126242){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
11. \"If you are using the Modern mode then it\'s all about the Spkr
    page. Since that mode has no negative feedback the speaker resonance
    has a tremendous effect on the sound. Adjust LF Res, Freq and Q to
    get desired response.\"
    [\[413\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/anyone-have-any-luck-with-the-rectifier-models.109907/#post-1315682){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
12. \"Another thing with the Modern modes is that the power amp distorts
    early (again since there is no negative feedback and, therefore, the
    power amp has a lot more gain). At 9:00 on the Master the power amp
    is distorting (it\'s probably a linear taper pot for the ol\' \"Wow,
    this amp is loud bro!\"). (\...) Another thing is that if you put
    ANYTHING in the loop of a Recto it changes the tone significantly.
    Even just a short cable. All the models were made with the loop off.
    And another thing is that Rectos changed a lot. I have three of them
    and they all sound completely different. One of them has a different
    value Gain pot than the others. One of them has a different value
    bright cap than the one with the same Gain pot. Since the gain pot
    and bright cap interact this makes a HUGE difference. Experiment
    with the Bright Cap value. The Recto1 models are based on our Rev. F
    (IIRC, whatever the desirable ones are). The Recto2 models are based
    on the latest version.\"
    [\[414\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/anyone-have-any-luck-with-the-rectifier-models.109907/#post-1315714){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
13. \"We have three of them, a single and two duals.\"
    [\[415\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/when-were-the-rectos-improved.122719/#post-1459883){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
14. \"If you want that Recto crunch but not so flubby and fizzy try the
    SOLO models.\"
    [\[416\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/ax8-v7-00-public-beta.125015/page-3#post-1487394){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
15. \"A Recto is not a Mark series amp. Totally different preamp
    topology. A Recto preamp is very similar to a SLO100.\"
    [\[417\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/the-greatest-digital-guitar-recording-of-all-time.154788/post-1841448){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
16. (amp model closest to the MESA Roadster) \"Recto 2.\"
    [\[418\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/what-amp-model-is-closest-to-the-mesa-roadster.127060/post-1512755){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
17. \"The Rectifier preamp is almost identical to an SLO100.\" \...
    \"There\'s a treble cut on the tone stack and a some minor changes
    to the power amp and power supply but it\'s basically a ripoff. The
    schematics are readily available for both so anyone interested can
    see for themselves. Personally I hate the 39K resistor. It biases
    the stage much too cold for my tastes. It prevents blocking
    distortion but there are better ways to do it IMO. The FAS Modern
    model is similar but biases the stage more towards the center.\"
    [\[419\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/new-amp-models.159097/post-1901310){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
18. \"Using the loop on a modern 3-channel rectifier changes the tone
    pretty dramatically (we model the amp with the loop bypassed). There
    are several reasons for this:
    1.  The source impedance to the power amp is changed.
    2.  There is a treble peaker on the Output pot. Presumably this was
        done to counteract treble loss in the loop.
    3.  An extra highpass filter is present due to the loop send stage.
        The corner frequency is around 30 Hz. That\'s low but it does
        affect subharmonics due to intermodulation. I would\'ve made the
        capacitor around 1uF.\"
        [\[420\]](https://www.thegearpage.net/board/index.php?threads/blind-test-mesa-dual-rectifier-vs-mystery-modeler-update-results-revealed.2208367/post-31646126){.external
        .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
19. \"Recto2 is based on a new 3-channel Dual Rectifier. Recto1 is based
    on the original 2-channel.\"
    [\[421\]](https://www.thegearpage.net/board/index.php?threads/blind-test-mesa-dual-rectifier-vs-mystery-modeler-update-results-revealed.2208367/post-31647001){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
20. \"I have three Rectos: an old Single Rectifier, an old (Rev. G
    maybe) Dual Rectifier and a new Dual Rectifier. They all sound
    completely different. The old Dual is the best sounding of the
    bunch.\"
    [\[422\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-9-cygnus-firmware-public-beta-6.171176/post-2062420){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
21. \"The MV taper of the model is authentic so just like the real amp
    the power amp starts to clip very early. With the real amp there\'s
    audible feedback (as in it gets insanely loud) but with the model
    you don\'t get that and humans have this weird thing where they
    don\'t like knobs to deviate from noon. I\'ve debated changing the
    taper or adding a pad between the preamp and power amp but, in the
    end, I decided to keep things authentic.\"
    [\[423\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/simple-tip-for-recto-tones.174349/post-2114224){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
22. \"You have to be very careful with the Master Volume. A Recto will
    start saturating the power amp in Modern mode at VERY low MV
    settings. Once the power amp starts clipping the tone will change.
    With digital products I often see people set the MV higher than they
    would on the real amp because there are no sonic repercussions
    (i.e., pissing off the wife/neighbors, knocking Grandma\'s urn off
    the mantel, etc.). If an emulation sounds darker or more midrangey
    than the real amp try turning down the MV. If it\'s a good emulation
    you should find a point (around 1-2) where you can hear the power
    amp start to saturate. Go up/down from there to get the desired
    power amp overdrive.\"
    [\[424\]](https://www.thegearpage.net/board/index.php?threads/why-are-rectifier-emulations-so-off.2341907/post-34347979){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
23. (Recto1) \"Our OG Dual Rectifier has a 10A MV taper. The model uses
    20A which is the same taper as the Recto2. (\...) Other than that
    the model is in very good agreement with the amp.\"
    [\[425\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/adventures-in-fractals-dual-rectifiers.3949/post-151166){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
24. \"The Red channel has no negative feedback so the response is highly
    dependent upon the impedance curve. Vintage has quite a bit.\"
    [\[426\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/adventures-in-fractals-dual-rectifiers.3949){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
25. \"On the amp the MV is around 9 o\'clock (as loud as I dared to go
    and not get divorced). I had to set the model to 1.2 to get the same
    response. Above that and the power amp starts clipping and the highs
    get reduced. This is to be expected given the different taper
    between the amp and the model.\"
    [\[427\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/adventures-in-fractals-dual-rectifiers.3949/post-151193){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
26. (about the non-working Presence control on the two-channel Dual
    Rectifier\'s Orange channel) \"These situations always present a
    dilemma:
    1.  Option 1: Remove the presence control and deal with \"Why u no
        hav presence control on the Recto1 Orange Modern model. The real
        map has one.\"
    2.  Option 2: Put a presence control on there that doesn\'t do
        anything and deal with \"Hey idiots, the presence control on the
        Recto1 Orange Model is broken.\"
    3.  Option 3: Put a presence control on the model that actually does
        something but defaults to a value (in this case 5.0) that
        matches the amp\'s native behavior. We chose Option 3.\"
        [\[428\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/adventures-in-fractals-dual-rectifiers.3949/page-17#post-159707){.external
        .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
27. A Dual Rectifier\'s preamp is a similar to an SLO100 except for a
    few differences. Otherwise they are very similar down to the
    topology and component values. The power amps are very similar
    EXCEPT in Modern mode. In Modern mode there is no negative feedback.
    The polite thing to say is that a Dual Rectifier was inspired by an
    SLO100.
    [\[429\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/new-synergy-drect-module.5181/page-2#post-206461){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
    - The gain pot is 250K vs. 1M
    - There\'s a treble roll-off network on the output of the tone stack
      (this is a big one)
    - There are two cathode followers in series on an SLO100 (fx loop
      send and fx loop return)

## []{#REVV_GEN_GREEN_1_(REVV_GENERATOR_120_MKIII)}[REVV GEN GREEN 1 (REVV GENERATOR 120 MKIII)]{#REVV_GEN_GREEN_1_.28REVV_GENERATOR_120_MKIII.29 .mw-headline}

[![Revv Generator
120.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/3/3d/Revv_Generator_120.jpg/350px-Revv_Generator_120.jpg){decoding="async"
width="350" height="141"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/3/3d/Revv_Generator_120.jpg/525px-Revv_Generator_120.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/3/3d/Revv_Generator_120.jpg/700px-Revv_Generator_120.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Revv_Generator_120.jpg){.image}

Models (MKIII revision A):
[\[430\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/revv-generator-120-mk.213093/post-2668940){.external
.autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

- Green channel, Drive switch: off
- Green channel, Drive switch: blue
- Green channel, Drive switch: red
- Purple Gain channel, Aggression: least (green)
- Purple Gain channel, Aggression: tight (blue)
- Purple Gain channel, Aggression: fat (red)
- Red Gain channel, Aggression: least (green)
- Red Gain channel, Aggression: tight (blue)
- Red Gain channel, Aggression: fat (red)

The AM4 has three models (Green, Purple, Red) with Aggression switches

Cab:

- original: Revv 4x12 (V30)
- DynaCab match: 4x12 Friedman V30

Gain, Bass, Mid, Treble, Level, Master, Presence, Depth

Switches per channel: Wide, Drive, Bright, Aggression, Cut, Fat

Power tubes: 6L6

1.  \"Revv is a great amp. Sort of a Marshall/SLO vibe but more open.
    Really well designed and built.\"
    [\[431\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-22-00-release.195047/post-2429051){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The Revv actually has an MV that makes sense. Instead of driving
    the power amp into oblivion at around 3, power amp overdrive
    doesn\'t start happening until you turn the knob up quite a bit.\"
    [\[432\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-22-00-release.195047/post-2429139){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#RUBY_ROCKET_(Paul_Ruby_Rocket)}[RUBY ROCKET (Paul Ruby Rocket)]{#RUBY_ROCKET_.28Paul_Ruby_Rocket.29 .mw-headline}

[![Rocket.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/9/9d/Rocket.jpg/300px-Rocket.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="206"
srcset="/wiki/images/9/9d/Rocket.jpg 1.5x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Rocket.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Bright switch: on
- Bright switch: off

Cab:

- original: 1x12 (Alnico, G12M)
- DynaCab match: 1x12 Div13 CJ

Volume, Bass, Treble, Cut, Bright switch

Power tubes: EL84

No negative feedback

1.  \"The Ruby Rocket is not the same as an actual Trainwreck Rocket.
    There are topology differences and the amps don\'t sound the same.\"
    [\[433\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1154295){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"Ruby Rocket is based on a Paul Ruby Rocket which is based on a TW
    Rocket but with some notable differences.\"
    [\[434\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-ii-firmware-18-00-public-beta.96198/page-30#post-1154336){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The Bright switch changes a coupling cap and the treble cap in the
    tone stack. This cuts the bass, shifts the midrange and lowers the
    gain slightly. That\'s why there are two separate models. Otherwise
    you would just engage the Bright switch under the Treble knob.\"
4.  \"The Ruby Rocket has a bright switch but it\'s actually a channel
    select (selects the bright channel).\"

## [RUBY ROCKET BRIGHT]{#RUBY_ROCKET_BRIGHT .mw-headline}

## []{#SHIVER_CLEAN_(Bogner_Shiva_20th_Anniversary)}[SHIVER CLEAN (Bogner Shiva 20th Anniversary)]{#SHIVER_CLEAN_.28Bogner_Shiva_20th_Anniversary.29 .mw-headline}

[![Shiva.png](/wiki/images/thumb/e/ec/Shiva.png/325px-Shiva.png){decoding="async"
width="325" height="143"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/e/ec/Shiva.png/488px-Shiva.png 1.5x, /wiki/images/e/ec/Shiva.png 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Shiva.png){.image}

Models:

- Clean channel
- Lead channel

Cab:

- original: Bogner 1x12 or 2x12 (Classic 80, V30)
- DynaCab match: 2x12 Lead 80

Clean channel: Volume, Bass, Treble, Bright switch

Lead channel: Gain, Volume, Bass, Middle, Treble, Shift EQ (not
modeled), Bright switch, Mode switch (not modeled)

Shared: Master, Presence, Excursion/Depth, Boost switch (not modeled)

Power tubes: KT88

1.  \"People think Bogners are dark but they really aren\'t. The reason
    they seem that way is the pot tapers. Most people assume knobs
    should be set somewhere around noon. If you do this on a Bogner
    it\'s like turning the treble way down on a Marshall. Close your
    eyes and adjust the tone controls with your ears. Don\'t be afraid
    to turn them way up or way down.\"
    [\[435\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1031334){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"Human nature is to put the knobs near noon. We are reticent to
    deviate much from noon. Amp designers exploit this and use different
    tapers to change the sound of their amps WITH THE KNOBS AT NOON. A
    prime example are Bogner amps. Everyone says \"Bogner amps are
    dark\". No they aren\'t. But he uses a Log10A taper for the treble
    pot. It\'s a standard Marshall tone stack. Usually a linear taper
    pot is used for the treble. The treble knob at 5.0 (noon) on a
    Bogner is equivalent to the treble knob at 1.0 on a Marshall. People
    put the knob at 5.0 and go \"wow, this amp is dark\". No it isn\'t.
    If you turned the treble up to 8 or 9 it would sound a lot like a
    Plexi but humans are reticent to turn the knobs to extremes. Amp
    designers know this and exploit it to give their amps a \"signature
    sound\".\"
    [\[436\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1047275){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The original Shiva models were based on a borrowed amp. We now
    have a 20th Anniversary Shiva (with KT88s) and the new models are
    based on that amp. We did notice that this amp has less gain than
    the one used originally but the model is faithful to the amp.\"
    [\[437\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1152978){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"Bogner\'s are notoriously \"slow\" due to the low B+ voltage. Main
    reason I can\'t get along with them. You can try increasing the
    Variac.\"
    [\[438\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/fast-pick-attack-amp.170370/post-2049711){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"Most amps use a linear taper for the treble pot. Bogners use a log
    taper. So when the knob is at noon on a Bogner it\'s similar to 8
    o\'clock on most amps.\"
    [\[439\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-11-cygnus-firmware-public-beta-8.171486/post-2067364){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## [SHIVER LEAD]{#SHIVER_LEAD .mw-headline}

## []{#SOLO_88_CLEAN_(Soldano_X88R_preamp)}[SOLO 88 CLEAN (Soldano X88R preamp)]{#SOLO_88_CLEAN_.28Soldano_X88R_preamp.29 .mw-headline}

[![X88r.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/1/18/X88r.jpg/300px-X88r.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="55"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/1/18/X88r.jpg/450px-X88r.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/1/18/X88r.jpg/600px-X88r.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:X88r.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Clean channel
- Rhythm channel
- Lead channel

DynaCab match: 4x12 Solo 100

Gain, Bass, Middle, Treble, Volume, Bright switch (Clean and Rhythm
channels only)

Power tubes: same as SLO-100 model (6L6)

1.  \"Solo 88 RHY is based on an X88R since the rhythm channel of an X99
    is identical to an SLO-100.\"
2.  "We have two X88s and they sound and measure quite different.
    They\'re both OG versions. Ultimately I found one had a quality in
    the low end that I liked better so I went with that."

## []{#SOLO_99_CLEAN_(Soldano/Caswell_X99_preamp)}[SOLO 99 CLEAN (Soldano/Caswell X99 preamp)]{#SOLO_99_CLEAN_.28Soldano.2FCaswell_X99_preamp.29 .mw-headline}

[![Cliff
X88.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/4/44/Cliff_X88.jpg/325px-Cliff_X88.jpg){decoding="async"
width="325" height="91"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/4/44/Cliff_X88.jpg/488px-Cliff_X88.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/4/44/Cliff_X88.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Cliff_X88.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Clean channel
- Lead channel, Bright off
- Lead channel, Bright on

DynaCab match: 4x12 Solo 100

Gain, Bass, Middle, Treble, Volume, Bright switch

Power tubes: same as SLO-100 model (6L6)

1.  \"The rhythm channel of an X99 is identical to a SLO 100.\"
    [\[440\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/718846){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"Power amp: same as SLO100.\"
    [\[441\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1250203){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The bright cap on the X99 Clean is not across the Drive pot. The
    exposed \"Bright Cap\" is across the Drive pot, the X99 clean
    channel does not have one.\"
    [\[442\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/found-a-bug-soldano-x99-clean-bright-cap.28046/post-418468){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#SOLO_100_CLEAN_(Soldano_SLO-100)}[SOLO 100 CLEAN (Soldano SLO-100)]{#SOLO_100_CLEAN_.28Soldano_SLO-100.29 .mw-headline}

[![SOLDANO
SLO-100.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/4/4e/SOLDANO_SLO-100.jpg/350px-SOLDANO_SLO-100.jpg){decoding="async"
width="350" height="154"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/4/4e/SOLDANO_SLO-100.jpg/525px-SOLDANO_SLO-100.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/4/4e/SOLDANO_SLO-100.jpg/700px-SOLDANO_SLO-100.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:SOLDANO_SLO-100.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Normal channel, Clean mode
- Normal channel, Rhythm mode
- Overdrive channel

Cab:

- original: Soldano 4x12 (Eminence)
- DynaCab match: 4x12 Solo 100

Gain, Bass, Middle, Treble, Master, Presence, Bright switch (Normal
channel only), Depth (with Depth mod)

Power tubes: 6L6

1.  \"Cold-biased stages are where there\'s a very large cathode
    resistor so the operating point is close to the supply rail. For
    example, the SLO 100 has a 39K cathode resistor on the cold-biased
    stage.\"
    [\[443\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/ultra-firmware-version-9-00-released.22557/page-2#post-366580){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The SLO-100 is the loudest amp I\'ve ever used. It feels like
    there\'s a small nuclear explosion going off inside when ever you
    hit a power chord. It\'s a wicked amp but not something I would
    recommend for anything but large gigs. If you like the SLO-100 model
    you might want to try the Recto models too. It\'s not widely known
    but the Rectifier preamp is a derivative of the SLO-100. Some minor
    changes but the basic topology is identical.\"
3.  \"I have a really good SLO-100. An original black faceplate version.
    Pristine condition. That amp was one of the primary amps used in the
    G2 modeling development. It was by studying that and a really nice
    JCM-800 that I finally figured out the secret to cathode follower.\"
    [\[444\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/562187){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"Mine doesn\'t have the depth mod but I used the values from the
    schematic I have and I believe the schematic is correct.\"
    [\[445\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/830925){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"SLOs are brittle at low volumes. When you crank them up it smooths
    out. The problems is at cranked volumes they can kill small
    animals.\"
6.  \"The key to an SLO100 is to run the MV high so that the mids
    thicken up. Otherwise it\'s a shrill mess. In certain contexts with
    the right IR it can be a cool sound.\"
    [\[446\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1146118){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  \"Note that the knobs on \'5\' on the Axe-Fx correspond to \'6\' on
    an SLO because they go to 11. \'Noon\' on an SLO isn\'t actually the
    knobs at half-way. The range of the knobs is like 8:00 to 6:00 as
    opposed to 7:00 to 5:00. They\'re biased clockwise.\"
    [\[447\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1057829){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
8.  \"Another caveat when comparing amps: many times the knobs aren\'t
    \"centered\". IOW if you put the Treble knob at noon it isn\'t
    actually at 50%. You can see this by turning the knob all the way
    down and all the way up. It may not be symmetrical. This happens
    when the pots don\'t have a flat spot and/or the pot is rotated
    within the mounting hole. Or in the case of an SLO100 it is
    intentional. On an SLO100 all the way down is around 8:00 and all
    the way up is 6:00 so 50% is around 1:00 not noon.\"
    [\[448\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1158815){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
9.  \"Many people find SLOs too bright. The \"Warren Haynes\" mod is a
    popular mod to reduce the brightness.\"
10. \"Those amps are all designed to get their character from power amp
    distortion. If you don\'t push the power amp all you are hearing is
    the preamp which is voiced to be trebly. The power amp then
    compresses the highs and the sound gets fatter.\"
11. \"If you want that Recto crunch but not so flubby and fizzy try the
    SOLO models. They\'re much brighter so I turn the treble down quite
    a bit.\"
    [\[449\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/ax8-v7-00-public-beta.125015/page-3#post-1487394){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
12. \"SLO 100s are NOT smooth amps. They are nasty, aggressive things
    that you have to crank the MV.\"
    [\[450\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-version-5-00-beta-3.148907/page-4#post-1764615){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
13. \"A Recto is not a Mark series amp. Totally different preamp
    topology. A Recto preamp is very similar to a SLO100.\"
    [\[451\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/the-greatest-digital-guitar-recording-of-all-time.154788/post-1841448){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
14. \"The Rectifier preamp is almost identical to an SLO100.\"
    [\[452\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/new-amp-models.159097/post-1901310){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
15. \"They\'re pretty awesome amps but to sound great you have to crank
    \'em and they\'re ear-splitting loud.\"
    [\[453\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-release-version-12-09.162488/post-1947441){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## [SOLO 100 RHYTHM]{#SOLO_100_RHYTHM .mw-headline}

## []{#SPAWN_NITROUS_1_(Splawn_Nitro)}[SPAWN NITROUS 1 (Splawn Nitro)]{#SPAWN_NITROUS_1_.28Splawn_Nitro.29 .mw-headline}

[![Nitro.gif](/wiki/images/thumb/f/ff/Nitro.gif/300px-Nitro.gif){decoding="async"
width="300" height="121"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/f/ff/Nitro.gif/450px-Nitro.gif 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/f/ff/Nitro.gif/600px-Nitro.gif 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Nitro.gif){.image}

Models:

- Overdrive channel, OD-1 (Rhythm) mode
- Overdrive channel, OD-2 (Lead) mode

Cab:

- original: Splawn 4x12 (G12M, G12-65, V30)
- DynaCab match: 4x12 Lerxst

Resonance/Depth, Presence, Bass, Middle, Treble, Master, Gain

Power tubes: KT88

1.  \"Based on a Splawn Nitro with KT-88 power tubes.\"

## [SPAWN NITROUS 2]{#SPAWN_NITROUS_2 .mw-headline}

## []{#SPAWN_Q-ROD_OD1-1_(Splawn_Quickrod)}[SPAWN Q-ROD OD1-1 (Splawn Quickrod)]{#SPAWN_Q-ROD_OD1-1_.28Splawn_Quickrod.29 .mw-headline}

[![Quickrod.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/b/be/Quickrod.jpg/300px-Quickrod.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="225"
srcset="/wiki/images/b/be/Quickrod.jpg 1.5x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Quickrod.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Overdrive channel, Rhythm mode, 1st gear (\"Plexi\")
- Overdrive channel, Rhythm mode, 2nd gear (\"hot-rodded JCM 800\")
- Overdrive channel, Rhythm mode, 3rd gear (\"super hot-rodded 800\")
- Overdrive channel, Lead mode, 1st gear
- Overdrive channel, Lead mode, 2nd gear
- Overdrive channel, Lead mode, 3rd gear

The AM4 has two models ()OD1 and OD2) with gear switches

Cab:

- original: Splawn (G12M, G12-65, V30)
- DynaCab match: 4x12 Friedman GB

Presence, Bass, Middle, Treble, Volume, Gain, Mode

Power tubes: EL34

1.  \"The reason Splawns sound weird is because the tone stack is plate
    driven. You lose the cathode follower compression and the high
    source resistance of the plate alters the tone stack frequency
    response. The plate driven tone stack in the Splawn reduces the
    highs considerably. You can see this is you run Tone Stack
    Calculator for the Marshall tone stack and increase the source
    resistance.\"
    [\[454\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1070559){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"OD2 switches in a cathode bypass cap which increases the gain of
    that stage.\"
    [\[455\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1158818){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The Quick Rod is a bit odd in that the Drive pot is linear taper.
    Most amps use an audio taper pot. This means that at noon the amp is
    nearly at full gain. Not sure why they did it that way but it is
    what it is.\"
    [\[456\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1159425){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#SUHR_BADGER_18_(Suhr_Badger_18)}[SUHR BADGER 18 (Suhr Badger 18)]{#SUHR_BADGER_18_.28Suhr_Badger_18.29 .mw-headline}

[![Badger18.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/3/3c/Badger18.jpg/325px-Badger18.jpg){decoding="async"
width="325" height="130"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/3/3c/Badger18.jpg/488px-Badger18.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/3/3c/Badger18.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Badger18.jpg){.image}
[![Badger30.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/c/c3/Badger30.jpg/325px-Badger30.jpg){decoding="async"
width="325" height="130"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/c/c3/Badger30.jpg/488px-Badger30.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/c/c3/Badger30.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Badger30.jpg){.image}

Badger models:

- Badger 18
- Badger 30

Cab:

- original: Suhr 1x12 or 2x12 (V30)
- DynaCab match: 1x12 Hot Kitty

Bass, Middle, Treble, Gain, Power (controls Power Scaling, not modeled),
Drive (acts as Master with Power at 10)

Power tubes: EL84 (Badger 18), EL34 (Badger 30)

No negative feedback

1.  \"The Badgers are very different amps. If you are used to hot-rod
    Marshall tones the Badgers won\'t be your \"thing\". These are
    edge-of-breakup amps. No negative feedback so they are loose and can
    be farty with certain pickups. They are \"players\" amps for guys
    who rely on technique and riding the volume knob.\"
    [\[457\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/amps-that-have-surprised-impressed-you-in-v10.67050/page-5#post-845093){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The Badgers were MIMIC\'d with power scaling at full. The knobs
    are a bit confusing on a Badger. The knob closest to the input jack
    is labeled \"Gain\". It is equivalent to the Drive knob in the Axe.
    The knob labeled Drive is the Master Volume.\"
    [\[458\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/830810){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The controls on the Badger are a bit confusing. Master Volume is
    labeled Drive. You have the Drive at 10 which means your power amp
    is at full blast. This can make the bass muddy. Turn the Drive
    down.\"
    [\[459\]](https://www.thegearpage.net/board/index.php?threads/i-have-to-say-im-a-little-upset.2205478/post-31553496){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"The worst amp in this regard is the Badger 18. The cathode
    resistors are very large and the amp shifts into Class B operation
    early causing a spitty, buzzy distortion quality. This amp, however,
    is liked by many so that just goes to show that some people like
    that. It\'s like fuzz pedals. Some people like that spitty sound.\"
    [\[460\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/papery-buzz-under-some-models.149193/page-2#post-1772639){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"The Badger doesn\'t have a Bright switch.\"
    [\[461\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/fixed-next-rel-wild-rumbling-chirping-artifacts-switching-between-presets.154544/post-1837842){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#SUHR_BADGER_30_(Suhr_Badger_30)}[SUHR BADGER 30 (Suhr Badger 30)]{#SUHR_BADGER_30_.28Suhr_Badger_30.29 .mw-headline}

## []{#SUPER_VERB_NORMAL_(1964_Fender_Super_Reverb,_AB763)}[SUPER VERB NORMAL (1964 Fender Super Reverb, AB763)]{#SUPER_VERB_NORMAL_.281964_Fender_Super_Reverb.2C_AB763.29 .mw-headline}

[![Superreverb.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/6/62/Superreverb.jpg/300px-Superreverb.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="281"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/6/62/Superreverb.jpg/450px-Superreverb.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/6/62/Superreverb.jpg/600px-Superreverb.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Superreverb.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Normal channel
- Vibrato channel

Cab:

- original: Fender 4x10 (C10R, C10Q, P10R)
- DynaCab match: 4x10 Bassguy RI

Volume, Bass, Middle (Vibrato channel only), Treble, Bright switch,
Reverb effect (not modeled), Vibrato effect (not modeled)

Power tubes: 6L6

1.  \"I modeled the Super with V1 pulled as most people pull V1 so the
    amp has more grunt. Turn down the MV to make it cleaner.\"
2.  \"The Super Reverb model is based on the amp with V1 removed (which
    is a common mod). This increases the level into the power amp by
    about a factor of two.\"
    [\[462\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/xl-units-quantum-6-fw-austin-buddy-raw-amp-bank-part-i-feedback.123065/#post-1464566){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The Super Reverb model is \"Diaz Modded\". IOW, I pulled V1. This
    gives the amp a lot more gain so it\'s not surprising you\'re
    getting breakup at around 1.5. You can un-mod the model by turning
    down the MV Trim to around 0.5.\"
    [\[463\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/851580){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"A Pro Reverb is basically identical to a Super Reverb except for
    the speakers (and faceplate).\"
    [\[464\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/933261){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"} And:
    \"The Blackface Pro Reverb, model AA165, was virtually identical to
    the AB763 Super Reverb except for the speakers and tone stacks. If
    you use the Super Verb model and set the Tone Stack type to
    Blackface you\'ll basically have a Pro Reverb. Set the Mid control
    fairly high to emulate the fixed 6.8K mid resistor. I\'d say around
    7 or 8.\"
    [\[465\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1079578){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  (blackface) \"Not a huge change with the Silverfaced versions.
    They\'re a little cleaner and brighter but the topology is the same.
    Some minor circuit changes here and there. Same transformers. The
    biggest change, IMO, was changing the PI resistors to 47K which
    gives you a little less gain in the PI.\"
    [\[466\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1252495){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"The Super Reverb is really just a 50W version of a Twin Reverb
    with different speakers.\"
    [\[467\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/wanted-amps-to-model.56753/page-4#post-713267){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  (Bright cap) \"It\'s only 120pF so it\'s subtle.\"
    [\[468\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-27-03-public-beta-3.210142/page-5#post-2627312){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#TRIPLE_CREST_2_(MESA_Triple_Crown_TC-100)}[TRIPLE CREST 2 (MESA Triple Crown TC-100)]{#TRIPLE_CREST_2_.28MESA_Triple_Crown_TC-100.29 .mw-headline}

[![Triplecrown.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/f/f7/Triplecrown.jpg/300px-Triplecrown.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="169"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/f/f7/Triplecrown.jpg/450px-Triplecrown.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/f/f7/Triplecrown.jpg/600px-Triplecrown.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Triplecrown.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Low gain channel
- High gain channel

Cab:

- original: MESA cab with V30 speakers
- DynaCab match: 4x12 USA Mc90

Gain, Treble, Mid, Bass, Normal/Tight switch (not modeled), Presence,
Reverb effect (not modeled), Master, attenuator (not modeled)

Power tubes: EL34

1.  "The actual amp's "Tight" switch engages a built-in Tube Screamer
    circuit which can be replicated using a Drive block or the Amp
    block's internal Boost feature."
    [\[476\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-release-version-12-04.159140/post-1901363){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The clean channel is like every other Mesa clean channel: a
    Blackface Fender copy.\"
    [\[477\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-release-version-12-05.159156/post-1901965){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The clean channel uses the same built-in tube screamer as the
    other channels. There\'s a single fixed tube screamer circuit at the
    input of the amp. It can be switched in via relays which are
    controlled by the channel switches.\"
    [\[478\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-release-version-12-05.159156/post-1904010){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"A Mesa Triple Crown has a built-in Tube Screamer set clean on the
    input.\"
    [\[479\]](https://www.thegearpage.net/board/index.php?threads/looks-like-fractal-devices-are-getting-a-new-modeling-update-cygnus.2224849/post-32213988){.external

5.  \"The Triple Crest models are based off a Mesa Triple Crown which is
    \"derived from\" a Fender Tonemaster.\"

## []{#TWO_STONE_J35_(Two-Rock_Jet_35)}[TWO STONE J35 (Two-Rock Jet 35)]{#TWO_STONE_J35_.28Two-Rock_Jet_35.29 .mw-headline}

## []{#USA_BASS_400_1_(MESA_Bass_400_bass_amp)}[USA BASS 400 1 (MESA Bass 400 bass amp)]{#USA_BASS_400_1_.28MESA_Bass_400_bass_amp.29 .mw-headline}

[![Mesabass400.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/6/69/Mesabass400.jpg/300px-Mesabass400.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="104"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/6/69/Mesabass400.jpg/450px-Mesabass400.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/6/69/Mesabass400.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Mesabass400.jpg){.image}

The Fat switch in the model performs the same function as the Treble
Shift function on the original amp.

## [USA BASS 400 2]{#USA_BASS_400_2 .mw-headline}

\
\

------------------------------------------------------------------------

Regarding the following MESA/Boogie Mark models:

1.  \"The Mark series have lots of mids because the tone-stack is
    \"pre\". You can move it to post but it will change the feel. The
    pre- position is what gives you that singing lead tone and sustain.
    As with the real thing, the rule of thumb is to set the bass pretty
    low. You can add it back in with EQ after. The kids all do the \"V\"
    EQ but I use very little EQ. I happen to like lots of mids as it
    makes the tone fit in the mix better.\"
    [\[485\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/ive-had-a-change-of-heart-about-the-mark-iv-sim.23935/#post-380547){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"I have a Mark IIC+, a Mark IV, a Mark V and a Triaxis. They\'re
    all completely different. Mesa always says things like \"sounds the
    same as a IIC+\" but the circuits are different and, probably most
    important, the knob tapers are completely different.\"
    [\[486\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-ii-quantum-2-00-public-beta-numero-tres.109852/page-6#post-1315609){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The key to a good Boogie sound, IMO, is the Fat Switch. This is
    the treble Pull Shift on the IIC+ and the Pull Fat on the Mark IV.
    Mesa knew this and the Lead 2 modes on the Triaxis all had the
    treble shift engaged by default.\"
4.  \"The tone stack on a Boogie is pre-distortion. As you increase gain
    you want less bass into the distortion stages so the idea is you
    turn the bass down. In later versions of the Boogies (TriAxis for
    example) they changed the taper so that noon was equivalent to 1 on
    earlier models because people are reticent to move controls very far
    from noon for some weird reason.\"
    [\[487\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/highly-compressed-sound-on-high-gain-amps.169132/post-2032825){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
    - Turn the bright switch on. Every bit of information I\'ve found
      says that people typically used the Pull Bright on the Volume
      knob. This is equivalent to the Bright switch under the Treble
      control on the model. I always turn it on and I\'ve set it on by
      default for Q2.03.
    - USE THE EQ. The tone stack is pre-distortion which is atypical for
      a high-gain amp. Tone stacks are almost always post-distortion.
      Since the tone stack is pre-distortion you need to do your post
      distortion tone shaping using the EQ. The tone controls set the
      feel and the distortion texture, the EQ shapes the final tone. I
      like to do a gentle V-curve.
5.  \"The Mark series graphic EQ sucks. I know some people want
    authenticity but it\'s simply a bad design.\"
    [\[488\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/fractal-audio-firmware-update-thread.673/post-154508){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"With the presence control at noon it\'s roughly neutral. Turn it
    down and you are actually boosting bass and reducing treble.\"
    [\[489\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-ii-quantum-rev-1-03-firmware-release.106931/page-12#post-1282192){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#USA_JP_IIC+_GREEN_(MESA/Boogie_JP-2C)}[USA JP IIC+ GREEN (MESA/Boogie JP-2C)]{#USA_JP_IIC.2B_GREEN_.28MESA.2FBoogie_JP-2C.29 .mw-headline}

[![Jp2c.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/9/98/Jp2c.jpg/300px-Jp2c.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="197"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/9/98/Jp2c.jpg/450px-Jp2c.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/9/98/Jp2c.jpg/600px-Jp2c.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Jp2c.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Green: channel 1
- Yellow: channel 2
- Yellow: channel 2, Shred mode
- Red: channel 3
- Red: channel 3, Shred mode

The AM4 has less models, with Shred Mode switch

Cab:

- original: Mesa 1x12 (C90, V30)
- DynaCab match: 4x12 Recto Straight

Channel 1 (Mark IIC+ Clean): Gain, Master, Presence, Treble, Mid, Bass,
Mid/Boost switch (not modeled)), graphic EQ, Reverb effect (not modeled)

Channel 2 (Mark IIC+ Gain/Shred) and Channel 3 (Mark IIC+ Gain/Shred):
(Pull) Gain, Master, (Pull) Presence, Presence Shift, Treble, Mid, Bass,
graphic EQ, Shred mode switch

Power tubes: 6L6

1.  \"The JP amp has a fixed input gain control. The \"Gain\" control on
    the amp is actually an Overdrive control. If you use Authentic
    controls there is no Input Gain on \"Gain\".\"
    [\[490\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-version-5-03.149363/page-3#post-1772020){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"Presence Shift is Presence pull. Tone stack effectively has fat
    switch on.\"
    [\[491\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-version-5-05.149428/page-10#post-1775746){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  (difference between \"JP Green\" and \"USA Clean\") \"JP has less
    gain and a much larger midrange potentiometer.\"
    [\[492\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-version-5-06.149775/page-2#post-1777979){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"JP himself gave the models his stamp of approval.\"
    [\[493\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/i-am-confused-about-the-jp2c.153540/post-1826396){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"JP (Green) has less gain (than USA Clean) and a much larger
    midrange potentiometer.\"
    [\[494\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-version-5-06.149775/post-1777979){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"Those are great amps. The particular amp used for the models was
    John Petrucci\'s personal recording amp. I didn\'t want to give it
    back and offered to buy it from him but he wouldn\'t sell it.\"
    [\[495\]](https://www.thegearpage.net/board/index.php?threads/fractal-fm3-reviews-tones-questions.2124913/post-31011638){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  \"It\'s not that the Graphic EQ isn\'t the same, the TAPERS are not
    the same. On the real amp the controls do virtually nothing until
    you get near the ends of the range. If you move a slider to, say,
    3/4 of its range it does almost nothing. If you were to set the
    model\'s slider to the same position you would get significantly
    more boost. I didn\'t model the nonlinear slider behavior because
    IMO it\'s a design flaw. Graphic EQs should have a nice,
    linear-in-dB response. Otherwise the graphic EQ is very accurate.
    The frequency and Q behavior is spot-on. If you have pulled the
    presence knob on the amp you have to activate the Presence Shift on
    the model. Otherwise they will sound VERY different. Presence shift
    gives a much more focused sound. I always use the Presence Shift.
    You can\'t compare the amp with a switch engaged to the model
    without the equivalent switch engaged. Of course it will sound
    different. The tapers of the other controls should be very close
    including the Presence and Master Volume. (\...) JP himself was very
    impressed with the model and the model was matched to his PERSONAL
    head that he sent me.\"
    [\[496\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/real-jp2c-vs-axe-fx-3-sim-comparison.168942/post-2029916){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
8.  \"I thought that Shred mode is the same as the Red mode on the
    Triaxis which is just a treble boost on the output when, in fact,
    it\'s a clean boost on the input similar to a Tube Screamer but
    without the treble rolloff.\"
    [\[497\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-11-cygnus-firmware-public-beta-8.171486/post-2067465){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
9.  (fixed internal gain) \"Yellow is 2.9. Red is 5.7.\"
    [\[498\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-16-00-beta-11-cygnus-firmware-public-beta-8.171486/post-2067603){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
10. \"JP2C doesn\'t have a depth knob. If a knob isn\'t present in the
    Authentic menu then it may not do anything in the Ideal menu.\"
    [\[499\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-release-version-16-01-beta-1-public-beta.172736/post-2088439){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
11. \"USA JP models have a fixed Input Drive so when switching to the
    models the Input Drive is reset to the default value. The Input
    Drive knob is not visible in the Authentic menu.\"
    [\[500\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/bug-presence-not-working-at-the-usa-lead-models-triaxis-16-1-b.172777/post-2088655){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
12. \"A JP IIC+ is not a Mark IV. They sound different. The biggest
    difference is in the behavior of the Presence Shift. With the
    Presence Shift on the JP IIC+ will be very similar to the Mark IV
    with its Presence Shift on. With the Presence Shifts off they are
    very different sounding.\"
    [\[501\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/jp-ii-c-red-sounds-muffled-compared-to-mk-iv-mid-gain-in-fw-21-00-with-audio-and-preset.191858/post-2385695){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
13. \"All these amps have the same basic circuit with minor differences.
    The only unique thing I\'ve encountered in all my tests is the
    function of the Presence Shift pull on the JP2C. It\'s different
    than the pull shift on the other Mark amps.\"
    [\[502\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/mesa-mark-iic-mark-iic-mark-vii-the-jp2c-mark-iic.192824/post-2398526){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
14. \"The \"Gain\" control on a Mark V is equivalent to the Overdrive
    control on a Mark II/IV. The actual gain control on a Mark V is
    fixed (same as the JPIIC+). In the Axe-Fx you can actually change
    the Gain control using the Ideal tone controls. You\'ll see that
    when choosing the model it will be initialized to a value (4.4 for
    the Mark V).\"
    [\[503\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/fractal-audio-firmware-update-thread.673/page-119#post-154512){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#USA_METRO_BLUES_(MESA_Subway_Blues)}[USA METRO BLUES (MESA Subway Blues)]{#USA_METRO_BLUES_.28MESA_Subway_Blues.29 .mw-headline}

## []{#USA_MK_IIC+_(MESA/Boogie_Mark_IIC+)}[USA MK IIC+ (MESA/Boogie Mark IIC+)]{#USA_MK_IIC.2B_.28MESA.2FBoogie_Mark_IIC.2B.29 .mw-headline}

[![Iic+.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/7/7e/Iic%2B.jpg/300px-Iic%2B.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="225"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/7/7e/Iic%2B.jpg/450px-Iic%2B.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/7/7e/Iic%2B.jpg/600px-Iic%2B.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Iic%2B.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Lead Master, Pull Bright engaged
- Lead Master, Pull Bright off
- Lead Master, Pull Deep engaged
- Lead Master, Pull Deep off

The AM4 has a single model with switches

Cab:

- original: Mesa 1x12 (C90, EVM)
- DynaCab match: 4x12 Recto Straight

Volume (pull: Bright), Treble (pull: Shift = Fat), Bass (pull: Shift,
not modeled), Middle, Presence, Master rhythm (pull: Deep), Lead Drive
and Master Lead (pull: Bright)

Power tubes: 6L6

1.  \"The model was based on an early non-SimulClass version. I updated
    the model to be consistent with the later SimulClass version which
    most people prefer. The mode in the Mark V is based on the later
    SimulClass version.\"
    [\[506\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/fw11-iic-vs-mark-v-iic-not-getting-good-results-solved.74069/page-5#post-910018){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"If you want the sound of the non-SimulClass version set Triode 1
    Plate Freq to 1350 Hz.\"
    [\[507\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/910386){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The Pull Bright on the Volume knob is the classic \"Bright Cap\"
    which engages a capacitor across the potentiometer. This is already
    modeled in the Axe-Fx via the Bright Switch. The Pull Bright on the
    Lead Master knob engages a 0.22uF cap on the cathode of the last
    triode in the overdrive circuit. As there is no switch for this in
    the Axe-Fx it requires a separate model. Cathode caps are very
    common in tube amps. If the value is large the stage has more gain
    and the response is relatively flat. If the value is small the stage
    has more gain at higher frequencies. Amp designers use cathode caps
    to shape the frequency response. Caps in the range of 0.1 to 1.0 uF
    are commonly used to reduce bass response. A cathode cap works by
    decreasing the amount of negative feedback through shunting higher
    frequencies to ground. This reduced negative feedback increases the
    gain (and reduces linearity). FWIW the Axe-Fx is the only modeler of
    which I\'m aware that actually models triodes using a feedback
    technique. Other modelers use static waveshapers. The Axe-Fx triode
    models incorporate feedback so if there is a virtual cathode cap the
    stage is less linear in addition to having more gain.\"
    [\[508\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1186462){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"The IIC+ does not have a gain boost and doesn\'t need one. There
    is plenty of gain. The Pull Deep switch engages a large cathode cap
    on the final triode stage. With Pull Deep off there is actually a
    shelving response into the power amp (bass is reduced).\"
5.  (emulate Pull Shift on Bass) \"Put a Tilt EQ before the amp block
    with a frequency of 320 Hz and a gain of -3 dB. Set the Level to +3
    dB.\"
    [\[509\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1202633){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"I always used the Fat switch with the real amp.\" (IIC+)
    [\[510\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/mark-iic-amp-model-issues.121463/page-2#post-1446683){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  \"The IIC++ amp model is the same as the IIC+ with different
    tapers.\"
    [\[511\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/question-about-the-mark-series-graphic-eq-modeling.149223/post-1770773){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

<!-- -->

1.  \"Treble Shift on the Tone page of USA IIC+ models is an alias of
    the "Fat" control found on the Preamp page and performs the same
    function.\" (firmware 22)
2.  \"The \"Gain\" control on a Mark V is equivalent to the Overdrive
    control on a Mark II/IV. The actual gain control on a Mark V is
    fixed (same as the JPIIC+). In the Axe-Fx you can actually change
    the Gain control using the Ideal tone controls. You\'ll see that
    when choosing the model it will be initialized to a value (4.4 for
    the Mark V).\"
    [\[512\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/fractal-audio-firmware-update-thread.673/page-119#post-154512){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  (Bass: 1, Mids: 5, Treble: 8, Presence: 4.5, Volume 1: 7.5,
    Overdrive: 6, Vol bright: on, Lead bright: on, Treble shift: off,
    cranks the 80hz slider 7-8 db and yanks the 750 maybe 7-8 db) \"THIS
    is how you dial in a Mark IIC+. Almost exactly how I would dial one
    in when I was gigging. Turning the bass almost all the way down and
    cranking the treble is key.\"
    [\[513\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/fractal-audio-systems-am4-amp-modeler.10317/page-91#post-444165){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

\"I begrudgingly dragged the amp out of storage today (as it weighs a
metric ton) and repeated the measurements and did some A/B tests. As
expected the models are extremely accurate. That being said it is a bear
to dial in. Here are some tips:
[\[514\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/mark-iic-tips.112378){.external
.autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

1.  - The old version of the model incorrectly referenced the Mark IV
      tone stack. These tone stacks are identical except for the taper
      of the mid pot. The IIC+ has a linear pot and the Mark IV has a
      Log10 pot. I had it backwards in my earlier comments. My guess is
      that Mesa found that turning the midrange down sounds best (and it
      does) so they changed the pot taper to do this automatically since
      noon on a Log10 pot is equal to a 1.0 on a linear pot.
    - Commensurate with (1) I found myself turning the midrange down as
      well as the bass and turning the treble up.
    - Turn the bright switch on. Every bit of information I\'ve found
      says that people typically used the Pull Bright on the Volume
      knob. This is equivalent to the Bright switch under the Treble
      control on the model. I always turn it on and I\'ve set it on by
      default for Q2.03.
    - USE THE EQ. The tone stack is pre-distortion which is atypical for
      a high-gain amp. Tone stacks are almost always post-distortion.
      Since the tone stack is pre-distortion you need to do your post
      distortion tone shaping using the EQ. The tone controls set the
      feel and the distortion texture, the EQ shapes the final tone. I
      like to do a gentle V-curve.
    - These were my settings for a killer high-gain tone: Model: USA
      IIC+ / Input Drive: 8.1 / Overdrive: 9-10 / Bass: 1.0 / Midrange:
      1.8 / Treble: 8.9 / Presence: 4.5 / MV: 4.0 / Level: -20 dB /
      Bright Switch ON / 80 Hz: 4.8 / 240 Hz: 2.6 / 750 Hz: -4.5 / 2200:
      -0.2 / 6600: 0.\"
2.  \"Bright is the Pull Bright on the Lead Master. Deep is the Pull
    Deep on the Master.\"
    [\[515\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/bright-differences-between-usa-mk-iic-deep-bright-and-usa-mk-iic-bright.218847/#post-2755554){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
