## []{#USA_MK_IIC++_(custom_model_of_MESA/Boogie_IIC+)}[USA MK IIC++ (custom model of MESA/Boogie IIC+)]{#USA_MK_IIC.2B.2B_.28custom_model_of_MESA.2FBoogie_IIC.2B.29 .mw-headline}

Previously: METALLICA USA IIC++

See [USA
IIC+](/wiki/index.php?title=Amp_models#USA_MK_IIC.2B_.28MESA.2FBoogie_Mark_IIC.2B.29 "Amp models")

1.  (Metallica engineers) \"This model is part of our live sound. This
    amp was removed when the new MKII models were added and firmware
    updated. I asked if it could be ported for Q3 as I was having a
    difficult time migrating to the updated firmware and retaining our
    earlier work.\"
    [\[516\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/metallica-amp.115857/page-2#post-1384750){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"The IIC++ amp model is the same as the IIC+ with different
    tapers.\"
    [\[517\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/question-about-the-mark-series-graphic-eq-modeling.149223/post-1770773){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The model isn\'t just different tapers. It\'s based on one of
    Metallica\'s actual amps.\"
    [\[518\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/iic.214886/#post-2704556){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"They provided us with certain unique details and Cliff created the
    model. I was on site at Metallica HQ during this process.\"
    [\[519\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/iic.214886/post-2704561){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#USA_MK_IV_LEAD_/_RHYTHM_(MESA/Boogie_Mark_IV)}[USA MK IV LEAD / RHYTHM (MESA/Boogie Mark IV)]{#USA_MK_IV_LEAD_.2F_RHYTHM_.28MESA.2FBoogie_Mark_IV.29 .mw-headline}

[![Markiv.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/3/3b/Markiv.jpg/300px-Markiv.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="217"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/3/3b/Markiv.jpg/450px-Markiv.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/3/3b/Markiv.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Markiv.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Rhythm 1 channel (previously: USA Clean model)
- Rhythm 2 channel
- Lead channel, Voicing: Harmonics, Pull Bright engaged
- Lead channel, Voicing: Mid Gain, Pull Bright engaged
- Lead channel, Voicing: Harmonics, Pull Bright off
- Lead channel, Voicing: Mid Gain, Pull Bright off

The AM4 has less models, with switches

Cab:

- original: Mesa 1x12 (C90, V30)
- DynaCab match: 4x12 Recto Straight

Rhythm 1 channel: Gain, Treble, Bass, Mid, Presence, Master, Pull Bright

Rhythm 2 channel: Gain, Treble, Bass, Mid, Presence, Master, Pull Fat,
Presence Shift

Lead channel: Gain, Treble, Bass, Mid, Presence, Master

Shared: graphic EQ, Pentode/Triode switch, Class-A/Simul-Class switch,
Voicing switch (Mid Gain / Harmonics), Variac

Power tubes: 6L6

1.  \"Having owned multiple Mark IV\'s, multiple Triaxis\'s and a
    variety of other Boogie products, I can tell that the Mark series in
    general are a bitch to dial in. Once you figure them out though they
    are great amps. IMO, the key to a MKIV is to use the TMB to get the
    feel and the EQ to get the tone.\"
2.  \"If it isn\'t Mid Gain then it\'s Harmonics.\"
    [\[520\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1165578){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The Depth knob is inactive on that amp model. The real amp
    doesn\'t have one either.\"
    [\[521\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1205835){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"Fat and Presence shift work as the real amp.\"
    [\[522\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1246666){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"USA Clean is based on the MKIV.\"
    [\[523\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/mesa-iic-clean-channel.106851/#post-1280186){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"There isn\'t any way to run the virtual power tubes in triode
    mode\... but you can change the Power Tube Type to \"300B\" which is
    a triode. When you run a pentode (or beam tetrode) in triode mode
    you connect the screen to the anode which effectively defeats the
    screen. This lowers the output impedance of the plate significantly
    which, in turn, lowers the output impedance of the amp itself making
    the voltage output less dependent on the speaker impedance. Using
    the 300B tube type should get you pretty close.\"
    [\[524\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/mesa-mark-iv-pentode-triode-switch.122527/#post-1458293){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  (GEQ) \"The range of the sliders is the same as the amp. The taper
    is not. The amp is much more abrupt since it uses linear taper
    (should use \'S\'-taper).\"
    [\[525\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/question-about-the-mark-series-graphic-eq-modeling.149223/post-1769764){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
8.  (difference between \"JP Green\" and \"USA Clean\") \"JP has less
    gain and a much larger midrange potentiometer.\"
    [\[526\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-version-5-06.149775/page-2#post-1777979){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
9.  (simulate Class-A mode) \"Turn Power Tube Grid Bias all the way
    up.\"
    [\[527\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/mesa-mk-4-class-a-possible.154438/post-1836241){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
10. \"A JP IIC+ is not a Mark IV. They sound different. The biggest
    difference is in the behavior of the Presence Shift. With the
    Presence Shift on the JP IIC+ will be very similar to the Mark IV
    with its Presence Shift on. With the Presence Shifts off they are
    very different sounding.\"
    [\[528\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/jp-ii-c-red-sounds-muffled-compared-to-mk-iv-mid-gain-in-fw-21-00-with-audio-and-preset.191858/post-2385695){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
11. \"The amp uses linear taper sliders. The ideal taper for this type
    of circuit is S-taper. S-taper will give you approximately
    linear-in-dB. The Axe-Fx III is precisely linear-in-dB.\"
    [\[529\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/mark-series-eq.191595/post-2389621){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
12. \"The circuit didn\'t change in the new ones, they just changed the
    taper of the bass pot. The Triaxis is like this too. With the
    control at noon it\'s like the old ones with the control around 9
    o\'clock or so.\"
    [\[530\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/fractal-talk.2745/post-296429){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
13. Fractal Audio\'s MKIV probably is a revision B.
    [\[531\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/fractal-talk.2745/page-630#post-365529){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
14. The main difference between Rev A and Rev B is C23 is removed on the
    Rev B. Set Triode 1 Plate Frequency to 2200 Hz to simulate Rev A.
    This is for the Lead Channel. The most significant difference
    between the two is the Rhythm 2 channel.
    [\[532\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/mesa-boogie-mark-iv-rev-a.216637/#post-2724374){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
15. \"On a Mark IV (at least on our reference amp) all three controls
    have a Log10A taper. On a Mark V the tapers are different so you get
    more midrange and treble for the same settings. Channel 3 on a Mark
    V is virtually identical to the Mark IV Lead channel except for the
    pot tapers.\"
    [\[533\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/question-about-the-mark-series-graphic-eq-modeling.149223/post-1771767){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## [USA MK IV LEAD MID GAIN]{#USA_MK_IV_LEAD_MID_GAIN .mw-headline}

## [USA MK IV RHYTHM 1]{#USA_MK_IV_RHYTHM_1 .mw-headline}

## [USA MK IV RHYTHM 2]{#USA_MK_IV_RHYTHM_2 .mw-headline}

## []{#USA_MK_V_GREEN_(MESA/Boogie_Mark_V)}[USA MK V GREEN (MESA/Boogie Mark V)]{#USA_MK_V_GREEN_.28MESA.2FBoogie_Mark_V.29 .mw-headline}

[![MARK
V.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/d/d6/MARK_V.jpg/300px-MARK_V.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="192"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/d/d6/MARK_V.jpg/450px-MARK_V.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/d/d6/MARK_V.jpg/600px-MARK_V.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:MARK_V.jpg){.image}

- MK V Green: Channel 1, Clean
- MK V Red IIC+: Channel 3 in MK II C+ mode, Bright off
- MK V Red IIC+ Bright: same, Bright on
- MK V Red MKIV: Channel 3 in MK IV mode,Bright off
- MK V Red MKIV Bright: same, Bright on
- MK V Red XT: Channel 3 in Extreme mode, Bright off
- MK V Red XT Bright: same, Bright on

The AM4 has 4 models, with a Bright switch in the Red models

Cab:

- original: Mesa 1x12 (C90, V30)
- DynaCab match: 4x12 Recto Straight

Channel 1: Gain, Bass, Mid, Treble, Presence, Master, Normal/Bold
switch, Clean/Fat/Tweed switch (not modeled), EQ switch, power switch
(not modeled), diodes/tube switch (not modeled)

Channel 3: Gain, Bass, Mid, Treble, Presence, Master, Normal/Bright, EQ
switch, power switch (not modeled), pentode/triode switch (not modeled)

Power tubes: 6L6

1.  \"The MK V is basically a compendium of previous Mesa amps. There
    may be minor differences in tone due to circuit layout but nothing a
    few tweaks to the EQ can\'t fix.\"
    [\[534\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/573437){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  "A Mark V is a greatest hits of the Mark IV and IIC+. You already
    have all those models."
    [\[535\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/wish-list-new-amps.137944/post-1991426){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"I have a Mark IIC+, a Mark IV, a Mark V and a Triaxis. They\'re
    all completely different. Mesa always says things like \"sounds the
    same as a IIC+\" but the circuits are different and, probably most
    important, the knob tapers are completely different.\"
    [\[536\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-ii-quantum-2-00-public-beta-numero-tres.109852/page-6#post-1315609){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"Mark V is the same thing as a Mark IV w/ a few extra features.
    They sound virtually identical.\"
    [\[537\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-firmware-version-21-02.191637/post-2382608){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"The \"Gain\" control on a Mark V is equivalent to the Overdrive
    control on a Mark II/IV. The actual gain control on a Mark V is
    fixed (same as the JPIIC+). In the Axe-Fx you can actually change
    the Gain control using the Ideal tone controls. You\'ll see that
    when choosing the model it will be initialized to a value (4.4 for
    the Mark V).\"
    [\[538\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/fractal-audio-firmware-update-thread.673/page-119#post-154512){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"The MK V has a fixed gain control. They replaced the pot with
    resistors. So when you select the model it sets the gain to the
    preset value.\"
    [\[539\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/usa-pre-clean-changes-gain-value.210415/#post-2630155){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  \"On a Mark IV (at least on our reference amp) all three controls
    have a Log10A taper. On a Mark V the tapers are different so you get
    more midrange and treble for the same settings. Channel 3 on a Mark
    V is virtually identical to the Mark IV Lead channel except for the
    pot tapers.\"
    [\[540\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/question-about-the-mark-series-graphic-eq-modeling.149223/post-1771767){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#USA_PRE_CLEAN_(MESA_TriAxis_preamp)}[USA PRE CLEAN (MESA TriAxis preamp)]{#USA_PRE_CLEAN_.28MESA_TriAxis_preamp.29 .mw-headline}

[![Triaxis.png](/wiki/images/thumb/c/cc/Triaxis.png/300px-Triaxis.png){decoding="async"
width="300" height="81"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/c/cc/Triaxis.png/450px-Triaxis.png 1.5x, /wiki/images/thumb/c/cc/Triaxis.png/600px-Triaxis.png 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Triaxis.png){.image}

Models:

- Rhythm Green
- Lead 1 Red (TX-4 board)
- Lead 2 Green
- Lead 2 Red
- Lead 2 Yellow

DynaCab match: 2x12 Lead 80

Drive, Lead Drive (Lead channel), Treble, Middle, Bass, preamp Presence,
P.A. Presence (Rhythm and Lead 2), Presence Shift (Lead 2), Dynamic
Voice EQ (not modeled)

Power tubes: same as USA Lead model (6L6)

1.  \"I used a Triaxis for, shoot, I dunno, over a decade before
    designing the Axe-Fx. I have two of them. So I\'d say I\'m pretty
    familiar with the tones. To my ears (and my measurement equipment),
    the Axe-Fx models are spot-on.\"
2.  \"I can nail the sound of my Triaxis now by setting it (Bright)
    around 9:00 - 10:00.\"
    [\[541\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1001906){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"} And:
    \"10 on the Triaxis would be 0 dB on the Bright parameter. Anything
    below 10 is equivalent to less than noon on the Bright parameter.
    The \"Presence\" control on a Triaxis is always a hi cut, it never
    boosts. The Bright parameter is not an exact match to the Triaxis
    Presence control though. It is a fixed shelving filter. The Triaxis
    Presence control is passive so the center frequency changes with the
    amount of cut. It also changes the load on the plate which distorts
    the frequency response a bit too. The Presence parameter should be
    set to 5.00, which is neutral (see the manual for details).\"
3.  \"I have a Mark IIC+, a Mark IV, a Mark V and a Triaxis. They\'re
    all completely different. Mesa always says things like \"sounds the
    same as a IIC+\" but the circuits are different and, probably most
    important, the knob tapers are completely different.\"
    [\[542\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-ii-quantum-2-00-public-beta-numero-tres.109852/page-6#post-1315609){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"The key to a good Boogie sound, IMO, is the Fat Switch. This is
    the treble Pull Shift on the IIC+ and the Pull Fat on the Mark IV.
    Mesa knew this and the Lead 2 modes on the Triaxis all had the
    treble shift engaged by default.\"
5.  \"Mesa claims it\'s based on the IIC+ but it\'s different. The
    bright cap is different, the mid resistor is much greater, the
    source impedance of the drive \"pot\" is different, etc., etc,
    etc.\"
    [\[543\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/three-hours-with-the-usa-pre-ld2-yellow.111624/#post-1335224){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  (firmware Quantum 7) \"The USA Pre models now all use a MarkIV power
    amp model. The 2:90 power amp is basically the same as a MarkIV and
    does have a presence shift but it\'s accessed through a jack on the
    back (Voicing).\"
    [\[544\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-ii-quantum-rev-7-00-firmware-release.124944/page-15#post-1487194){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  \"I gigged with a Triaxis for years. I never put Dynamic Voice above
    1.0. Despite it\'s name, DV is just an EQ. It\'s the 5-band graphic
    EQ from the mark series with the potentiometers replaced by LDRs.
    It\'s really just a bunch of EQ presets and it interpolates between
    them as you increase the value.\"
    [\[545\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/triaxis-model-live-use.147163/#post-1740122){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
8.  \"I have two of them. Both with the Lead 1 Red board.\"
    [\[546\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/the-triaxis-is-spot-on.151673/post-1804830){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
9.  \"On our reference Triaxis (both of them) the Presence control
    doesn\'t do anything for the Clean and LD1 modes. The model\'s
    Presence knob is therefore the Power Amp Presence.\"
    [\[547\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/triaxis-usa-pre-models-inconsistencies-in-controls.156431/post-1862912){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
10. \"That\'s how our reference amps work. They are the later models
    with the TX4 board (different LD2 Red). When using the LD1 modes the
    Presence control doesn\'t do anything and is as if the control were
    at 10.\"
    [\[548\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/triaxis-usa-pre-models-inconsistencies-in-controls.156431/post-1865080){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
11. \"The tone stack on a Boogie is pre-distortion. As you increase gain
    you want less bass into the distortion stages so the idea is you
    turn the bass down. In later versions of the Boogies (TriAxis for
    example) they changed the taper so that noon was equivalent to 1 on
    earlier models because people are reticent to move controls very far
    from noon for some weird reason.\"
    [\[549\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/highly-compressed-sound-on-high-gain-amps.169132/post-2032825){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
12. \"Based on the Lead 1 Red mode of a Mesa Triaxis preamp with the
    TX-4 board.\"
13. In \"Cygnus\" amp modeling firmware the Lead models have an
    authentic Preamp Presence control (not in the Lead 1 model).
14. \"I gigged a Triaxis for years and I would have the knobs pretty
    much at noon (5.0). The Triaxis is a Mark IV preamp under the hood
    but with very different tapers on the \"pots\". I.e., with BMT at
    5.0 on the Triaxis the MKIV would be something like 1.0, 6.0, 6.0.
    I\'m just going by memory here but the point being that the bass
    control on the Triaxis doesn\'t need to be turned way down like you
    would on a Mark series.\"
    [\[550\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/bad-experience-with-choptones-i-need-a-2nd-opinion-watch-screenshots-plz.191948/post-2386734){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
15. \"The Triaxis used LDRs as variable resistance elements. There were
    resistor strings that were used to set the LDRs but those resistors
    weren\'t in the signal path.\"
    [\[551\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/5150-presence-knob.199908/page-17#post-2494019){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
16. \"The circuit didn\'t change in the new ones, they just changed the
    taper of the bass pot. The Triaxis is like this too. With the
    control at noon it\'s like the old ones with the control around 9
    o\'clock or so.\"
    [\[552\]](https://thegearforum.com/threads/fractal-talk.2745/page-496#post-296429){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
17. \"Triaxis with a 2:90 was one of my gigging rigs. Sounded glorious.
    Since the Triaxis holds a special place in the annals of my music
    career the models in our products were done with extra attention.\"
    [\[553\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/is-there-a-triaxis.220550/page-2#post-2781385){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#VIBRATO_VERB_(Fender_Vibroverb,_old_model)}[VIBRATO VERB (Fender Vibroverb, old model)]{#VIBRATO_VERB_.28Fender_Vibroverb.2C_old_model.29 .mw-headline}

[![Vibroverb.jpg](/wiki/images/3/3d/Vibroverb.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300"
height="226"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Vibroverb.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Vibrato Verb: old model ported from the Axe-Fx Ultra (not included on
  the AM4)
- Vibrato Verb AA: Cliff's own 1964 blackface Vibroverb with AA763
  circuit
- Vibrato Verb AB: AB763 circuit
- Vibrato Verb SRV: Custom Reissue

Cab:

- original: Fender 1x15 (Jensen C15N, JBL D130, Eminence)
- DynaCab match: 1x15 Vibratoverb

Volume, Bass, Treble, Bright switch, Reverb effect (not modeled),
Tremolo effect

Power tubes: 6L6

1.  \"The Transformer Matching value for the CS model is based on the
    output transformer in the actual amp. Legend has it that SRV used a
    Bassman transformer which would lead to significant overmatching. To
    replicate this increase Xfrmr Match to around 1.8.\"
2.  \"Some different component values in the AA vs. AB.\"
    [\[560\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/vibrato-verb-models-explained.192318/post-2391593){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"The 1x15 Vibroverb is a D130.\"
    [\[561\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/what-dyna-cab-models-would-you-like-to-see-added.193380/post-2404043){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  (SRV sound) \"For the amp model you want to use the Vibrato Verb
    Custom. Stevie pulled the normal channel triode out of his amp which
    increases the gain and changes the bias point of the vibrato
    channel. With the new Vibroverb Dyna-Cab I can get eerily close to
    the Couldn\'t Stand the Weather album tone.\"
    [\[562\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/vibroverb.214777/page-2#post-2697147){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  (SRV model) \"It is called Vibrato Verb Custom in the Axe-Fx. It\'s
    modeled after a VibroVerb with the normal channel\'s preamp tube
    removed. This roughly doubles the gain of the Vibrato channel.\"
    [\[563\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/what-is-the-vibrato-verb-srv-model.217972/#post-2743887){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#VIBRATO_VERB_AA_(1964_blackface_Fender_Vibroverb,_AA763)}[VIBRATO VERB AA (1964 blackface Fender Vibroverb, AA763)]{#VIBRATO_VERB_AA_.281964_blackface_Fender_Vibroverb.2C_AA763.29 .mw-headline}

## []{#VIBRATO_VERB_AB_(Fender_Vibroverb,_AB763)}[VIBRATO VERB AB (Fender Vibroverb, AB763)]{#VIBRATO_VERB_AB_.28Fender_Vibroverb.2C_AB763.29 .mw-headline}

## []{#VIBRATO_VERB_SRV_(Fender_Vibroverb_Custom_Reissue)}[VIBRATO VERB SRV (Fender Vibroverb Custom Reissue)]{#VIBRATO_VERB_SRV_.28Fender_Vibroverb_Custom_Reissue.29 .mw-headline}

\
\

------------------------------------------------------------------------

Regarding the following WRECKER models:

1.  \"The secret to a Trainwreck is the output transformer. The
    impedance ratio is about twice that of other amps. I.e. typical 50W
    Marshall has a primary impedance of about 3200 ohms. A Trainwreck is
    about 6500 ohms. The causes the power tubes to clip much sooner.\"
    [\[564\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/posts/1116254){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"Real Trainwrecks are very spitty amps. This is because the last
    stage heavily overdrives the phase inverter. 7.02 is faithful to the
    actual amps whereas previous firmwares were more idealized. As was
    indicated in the release notes you can dial out this behavior by
    decreasing the PI Bias Shift. If you set it to zero it will be like
    6.xx.\"
    [\[565\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-ii-quantum-rev-7-02-firmware-release.125625/page-17#post-1498318){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  [Cliff\'s Tech
    Note](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/trainwreck-express-tweaks.154796/post-1841547){.external
    .text target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}: \"A real
    Trainwreck Express is a fizzy, spitty amp. Some people like this.
    The same people who like fuzz pedals and that quasi-half-wave
    rectified sound. Personally I like more clarity. The reason the
    Express is like this is primarily due to the last triode stage
    before the phase inverter (PI). This stage is biased very cold and
    drives the PI very hard due to the lack of any limiting resistor
    (grid stopper) between the triode and PI. The lack of a grid stopper
    resistor and large coupling capacitor create significant bias
    excursion (blocking distortion). It appears the designer attempted
    to minimize the bias excursion by biasing the triode cold which
    limits its positive excursion and therefore limits the PI grid
    conduction. Despite the cold bias point the PI grid is still heavily
    overdriven resulting in massive blocking distortion. The Axe-Fx
    allows you to reduce the amount of block distortion via the PI Bias
    Excursion parameter. Simply turn this down and the spittiness will
    go away. You can then also rebias the triode via the Preamp Bias
    parameter. Values closer to zero result in a more symmetric
    waveform.\" (\...) \"Turn PI Bias Excursion to 0. Set Preamp Bias to
    -0.15 or so.
    [\[566\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-10-00-public-beta-2.154782/post-1841487){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}\"
4.  \"The reason they clean up when you back off the volume is because
    the OT is so overmatched. It\'s about twice the optimum value.\"
    [\[567\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-10-00-public-beta-2.154782/post-1841485){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"That\'s what amps do. You don\'t hear it through a guitar cab
    typically but using close-mic\'d IRs it\'s more noticeable. You can
    reduce it by turning on the Plate Suppressor diodes. Trainwrecks
    have plate suppressor diodes for just this reason.\"
    [\[568\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/note-decay-crackle-sizzle-noise.193575/post-2407689){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"That\'s blocking distortion and a \"feature\" of Trainwrecks.\"
    [\[569\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/wrecker-liverpool-bright-bug.205479/#post-2563010){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
7.  \"They\'re player\'s amps. They\'re meant for use with low-output
    pickups and a light touch. If you use a Dimarzio Dick Crusher pickup
    and a mason\'s hammer as a plectrum you\'re not going to get good
    results.\"
    [\[570\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-27-00-public-beta.207147/page-8#post-2584567){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## []{#WRECKER_EXPRESS_(Trainwreck_Express)}[WRECKER EXPRESS (Trainwreck Express)]{#WRECKER_EXPRESS_.28Trainwreck_Express.29 .mw-headline}

[![Trainwreck.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/5/53/Trainwreck.jpg/300px-Trainwreck.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="152"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/5/53/Trainwreck.jpg/450px-Trainwreck.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/5/53/Trainwreck.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Trainwreck.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Wrecker Express: Bright switch in center or top position
- Wrecker Express Bright: Bright switch in bottom (brightest) position

The AM4 has a single model with a Bright switch

Cab:

- original: Marshall 4x12 (G12-M25)
- DynaCab match: 4x12 Friedman GB

Power tubes: EL34

Volume, Bass, Mid, Treble, Presence, three-position Bright switch
(center: off, top: clarity and sparkle, bottom: jangly highs)

1.  \"The real amp is a nasty thing. Very spitty as one would expect
    given the lack of a grid stopper resistor between the last triode
    stage and the PI.\"
    [\[571\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-10-00-public-beta-2.154782/post-1841549){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"Got out the reference amp and it sounds the same. For all the
    hoopla surrounding Trainwrecks they\'re actually pretty bad designs.
    Tons of blocking distortion in the PI. If you don\'t want all that
    blocking distortion turn down PI Bias Excursion.\"
    [\[572\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-10-00-public-beta-2.154782/page-4#post-1841474){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  \"Turning down PI Bias Excursion yields the ultimate Trainwreck.
    Sounds much better than the real amp. I also adjusted the Preamp
    Bias so it wasn\'t so off-center.\"
    [\[573\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-10-00-public-beta-2.154782/page-4#post-1841480){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
4.  \"The only difference (between the two Express models) is the Bright
    Cap. An Express (at least mine) has a three-position switch: Off,
    100 pF, 500 pF. The amp block only supports Off and On and I figured
    people wouldn\'t know the fine details so a separate model seemed
    the easiest solution. Of course you can vary the Bright Cap but
    you\'d have to know that the real amp has two caps, etc.\"
    [\[574\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-iii-firmware-version-10-01.154923/post-1843572){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
5.  \"That amp exhibits a lot of blocking distortion (in the phase
    inverter) due to its design. You can reduce this via either the PI
    Bias Excursion or Master Bias Excursion parameters. Another option
    is to use the FAS Express model which puts some resistors between
    the last triode stage and the PI to reduce the bias excursion.\"
    [\[575\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/blocking-distortion-found-in-trainwreck-express.182895/post-2247268){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
6.  \"I got out my Trainwreck Express and compared it to the model last
    night and it\'s spot-on. Nasty, spitty, Neil Young-esque blocking
    distortion and all.\"
    [\[576\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/blocking-distortion-found-in-trainwreck-express.182895/post-2247538){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## [WRECKER EXPRESS BRIGHT]{#WRECKER_EXPRESS_BRIGHT .mw-headline}

## []{#WRECKER_LIVERPOOL_(Trainwreck_Liverpool)}[WRECKER LIVERPOOL (Trainwreck Liverpool)]{#WRECKER_LIVERPOOL_.28Trainwreck_Liverpool.29 .mw-headline}

[![Trainwreck.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/5/53/Trainwreck.jpg/300px-Trainwreck.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="152"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/5/53/Trainwreck.jpg/450px-Trainwreck.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/5/53/Trainwreck.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Trainwreck.jpg){.image}

Models:

- Liverpool: Bright switch in center or top position
- Liverpool Bright: Bright switch in bottom (brightest) position

The AM4 has a single model with a Bright switch

Cab:

- original: Marshall 4x12 (G12-M25)
- DynaCab match: 4x12 Friedman GB

Volume, Bass, Mid, Treble, Presence, three-position Bright switch
(center: off, top: clarity and sparkle, bottom: jangly highs)

Power tubes: EL84

1.  \"Just because a power amp is \"Class A\" doesn\'t mean it can\'t
    have negative feedback. True that the majority do not but this
    particular amp has quite a bit of NF.\"
    [\[577\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/wrecker-liverpool-neg-feedback-bug.116224/#post-1389082){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
2.  \"Uses a Vox-style phase inverter.\"
    [\[578\]](http://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/axe-fx-ii-quantum-rev-7-00-public-beta.123082/page-7#post-1464730){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
3.  (Tech Note) \"Applies to the Liverpool because the preamp is almost
    identical to the Express.\"
    [\[579\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/trainwreck-express-tweaks.154796/post-1842967){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}

## [WRECKER LIVERPOOL BRIGHT]{#WRECKER_LIVERPOOL_BRIGHT .mw-headline}

## []{#WRECKER_ROCKET_(Trainwreck_Rocket)}[WRECKER ROCKET (Trainwreck Rocket)]{#WRECKER_ROCKET_.28Trainwreck_Rocket.29 .mw-headline}

[![Trainwreck.jpg](/wiki/images/thumb/5/53/Trainwreck.jpg/300px-Trainwreck.jpg){decoding="async"
width="300" height="152"
srcset="/wiki/images/thumb/5/53/Trainwreck.jpg/450px-Trainwreck.jpg 1.5x, /wiki/images/5/53/Trainwreck.jpg 2x"}](/wiki/index.php?title=File:Trainwreck.jpg){.image}

Single channel model

Cab:

- original: Marshall 4x12 (G12-M25)
- DynaCab match: 4x12 Friedman GB

Volume, Treble, Bass, Cut

Power tubes: EL84

1.  \"The Rocket has a different preamp (than the Express) with the tone
    stack before the PI. This reduces the signal level substantially and
    lessens the amount of blocking distortion.\"
    [\[580\]](https://forum.fractalaudio.com/threads/trainwreck-express-tweaks.154796/post-1842967){.external
    .autonumber target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener"}
